# Book I

*Psalms 1&ndash;41*

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 1

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> That man hath perfect blessedness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who walketh not astray  
In counsel of ungodly men,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor stands in sinners’ way,

Nor sitteth in the scorner’s chair:  
<sup>2</sup> But placeth his delight  
Upon GOD’s law, and meditates  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on his law day and night.

<sup>3</sup> He shall be like a tree that grows  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;near planted by a river,  
Which in his season yields his fruit,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and his leaf fadeth never:

And all he doth shall prosper well.  
<sup>4</sup> The wicked are not so;  
But like they are unto the chaff,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which wind drives to and fro.

<sup>5</sup> In judgment therefore shall not stand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;such as ungodly are;  
Nor in th’ assembly of the just  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall wicked men appear.

<sup>6</sup> For why? the way of godly men  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto the LORD is known:  
Whereas the way of wicked men  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall quite be overthrown.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 2

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Why rage the heathen? and vain things  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;why do the people mind?  
<sup>2</sup> Kings of the earth do set themselves,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and princes are combined,

To plot against the LORD, and his  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Anointed, saying thus,  
<sup>3</sup> Let us asunder break their bands,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and cast their cords from us.

<sup>4</sup> He that in heaven sits shall laugh;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the Lord shall scorn them all.  
<sup>5</sup> Then shall he speak to them in wrath,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in rage he vex them shall.

<sup>6</sup> Yet, notwithstanding, I have him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to be my King appointed;  
And over Zion, my holy hill,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I have him King anointed.

<sup>7</sup> The sure decree I will declare;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD hath said to me,  
Thou art mine only Son; this day  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I have begotten thee.

<sup>8</sup> Ask of me, and for heritage  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the heathen I’ll make thine;  
And, for possession, I to thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;will give earth’s utmost line.

<sup>9</sup> Thou shalt, as with a weighty rod  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of iron, break them all;  
And, as a potter’s sherd, thou shalt  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;them dash in pieces small.

<sup>10</sup> Now, therefore, kings, be wise; be taught,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ye judges of the earth:  
<sup>11</sup> Serve GOD in fear, and see that ye  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;join trembling with your mirth.

<sup>12</sup> Kiss ye the Son, lest in his ire  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ye perish from the way,  
If once his wrath begin to burn:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;bless’d all that on him stay.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 3

*A Psalm of David, when he fled from Absalom his son.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O LORD, how are my foes increased?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;against me many rise.  
<sup>2</sup> Many say of my soul, For him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in God no succour lies.

<sup>3</sup> Yet thou my strength and glory art,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;th’ uplifter of mine head.  
<sup>4</sup> I cried, and, from his holy hill,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD me answer made.

<sup>5</sup> I laid me down and slept, I waked;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for GOD sustainèd me.  
<sup>6</sup> I will not fear though thousands ten  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;set round against me be.

<sup>7</sup> Arise, O LORD; save me, my God;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for thou my foes hast stroke  
All on the cheek-bone, and the teeth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of wicked men hast broke.

<sup>8</sup> Salvätion doth appertain  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto the LORD alone:  
Thy blessing, Lord, for evermore  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy people is upon.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 4

*To the chief Musician on Neginoth, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Give ear unto me when I call,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;God of my righteousness:  
Have mercy, hear my prayer; thou hast  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;enlarged me in distress.

<sup>2</sup> O ye the sons of men! how long  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;will ye love vanities?  
How long my glory turn to shame,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and will ye follow lies?

<sup>3</sup> But know, that for himself the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the godly man doth choose:  
The LORD, when I on him do call,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to hear will not refuse.

<sup>4</sup> Fear, and sin not; talk with your heart  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on bed, and silent be.  
<sup>5</sup> Off’rings present of righteousness,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and in the LORD trust ye.

<sup>6</sup> O who will show us any good?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is that which many say:  
But of thy countenance the light,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;LORD, lift on us alway.

<sup>7</sup> Upon my heart, bestowed by thee,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;more gladness I have found  
Than they, ev’n then, when corn and wine  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did most with them abound.

<sup>8</sup> I will both lay me down in peace,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and quiet sleep will take;  
Because thou only me to dwell  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in safety, LORD, dost make.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 5

*To the chief Musician, upon Nehiloth, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Give ear unto my words, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my meditation weigh.  
<sup>2</sup> Hear my loud cry, my King, my God;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for I to thee will pray.

<sup>3</sup> LORD, thou shalt early hear my voice:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I early will direct  
My prayer to thee; and, looking up,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;an answer will expect.

<sup>4</sup> For thou art not a God that doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in wickedness delight;  
Neither shall evil dwell with thee,  
<sup>5</sup> nor fools stand in thy sight.

All that ill-doers are thou hat’st;  
<sup>6</sup> cutt’st off that liars be:  
The bloody and deceitful man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;abhorrèd is by thee.

<sup>7</sup> But I into thy house will come  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in thine abundant grace;  
And I will worship in thy fear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;toward thy holy place.

<sup>8</sup> Because of those mine enemies,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;LORD, in thy righteousness  
Do thou me lead; do thou thy way  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;make straight before my face.

<sup>9</sup> For in their mouth there is no truth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their inward part is ill;  
Their throat’s an open sepulchre,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their tongue doth flatter still.

<sup>10</sup> O God, destroy them; let them be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by their own counsel quelled:  
Them for their many sins cast out,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for they ’gainst thee rebelled.

<sup>11</sup> But let all joy that trust in thee,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and still make shouting noise;  
For them thou sav’st: let all that love  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy name in thee rejoice.

<sup>12</sup> For, LORD, unto the righteous man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou wilt thy blessing yield:  
With favour thou wilt compass him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;about, as with a shield.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 6

*To the chief Musician on Neginoth upon Sheminith, A Psalm of David.*

### Version 1

*L.M.*

<sup>1</sup> LORD, in thy wrath rebuke me not;  
Nor in thy hot rage chasten me.  
<sup>2</sup> LORD, pity me, for I am weak:  
Heal me, for my bones vexèd be.

<sup>3</sup> My soul is also vexèd sore;  
But, LORD, how long stay wilt thou make?  
<sup>4</sup> Return, O LORD, my soul set free;  
O save me, for thy mercies’ sake.

<sup>5</sup> Because those that deceasèd are  
Of thee shall no remembrance have;  
And who is he that will to thee  
Give praises lying in the grave?

<sup>6</sup> I with my groaning weary am,  
I also all the night my bed  
Have causèd for to swim; and I  
With tears my couch have waterèd.

<sup>7</sup> Mine eye, consumed with grief, grows old,  
Because of all mine enemies.  
<sup>8</sup> Hence from me, wicked workers all;  
For GOD hath heard my weeping cries.

<sup>9</sup> GOD hath my supplication heard,  
My prayer receivèd graciously.  
<sup>10</sup> Shamed and sore vexed be all my foes,  
Shamed and back turnèd suddenly.

---

### Version 2

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> In thy great indignätion,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O LORD, rebuke me not;  
Nor on me lay thy chastening hand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in thy displeasure hot.

<sup>2</sup> LORD, I am weak, therefore on me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;have mercy, and me spare:  
Heal me, O LORD, because thou know’st  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my bones much vexèd are.

<sup>3</sup> My soul is vexèd sore: but, LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;how long stay wilt thou make?  
<sup>4</sup> Return, LORD, free my soul; and save  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;me for thy mercies’ sake.

<sup>5</sup> Because of thee in death there shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;no more remembrance be:  
Of those that in the grave do lie,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who shall give thanks to thee?

<sup>6</sup> I with my groaning weary am,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and all the night my bed  
I causèd for to swim; with tears  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my couch I waterèd.

<sup>7</sup> By reason of my vexing grief  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mine eye consumèd is;  
It waxeth old, because of all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that be mine enemies.

<sup>8</sup> But now, depart from me all ye  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that work iniquity:  
For why? the LORD hath heard my voice,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when I did mourn and cry.

<sup>9</sup> Unto my supplicätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD did hearing give:  
When I to him my prayèr make,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD will it receive.

<sup>10</sup> Let all be shamed and troubled sore,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that en’mies are to me;  
Let them turn back, and suddenly  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ashamèd let them be.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 7

*Shiggaion of David, which he sang unto the Lord, concerning the words of Cush the Benjamite.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O LORD my God, in thee do I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my confidence repose:  
Save and deliver me from all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my persecuting foes;

<sup>2</sup> Lest that the enemy my soul  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;should, like a lion, tear,  
In pieces rending it, while there  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is no deliverer.

<sup>3</sup> O LORD my God, if it be so  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that I committed this;  
If it be so that in my hands  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;iniquity there is:

<sup>4</sup> If I rewarded ill to him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that was at peace with me;  
(Yea, ev’n the man that without cause  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my foe was I did free);

<sup>5</sup> Then let the foe pursue and take  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my soul, and my life thrust  
Down to the earth, and let him lay  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mine honour in the dust.

<sup>6</sup> Rise in thy wrath, LORD, raise thyself,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for my foes raging be;  
And, to the judgment which thou hast  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;commanded, wake for me.

<sup>7</sup> So shall th’ assembly of thy folk  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;about encompass thee:  
Thou, therefore, for their sakes, return  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto thy place on high.

<sup>8</sup> The LORD he shall the people judge:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my judge, JEHOVAH, be,  
After my righteousness, and mine  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;integrity in me.

<sup>9</sup> O let the wicked’s malice end;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but stablish steadfastly  
The righteous: for the righteous God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the hearts and reins doth try.

<sup>10</sup> In God, who saves th’ upright in heart,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is my defence and stay.  
<sup>11</sup> God just men judgeth, God is wroth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with ill men ev’ry day.

<sup>12</sup> If he do not return again,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;then he his sword will whet;  
His bow he hath already bent,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and hath it ready set:

<sup>13</sup> He also hath for him prepared  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the instruments of death;  
Against the persecutors he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his shafts ordainèd hath.

<sup>14</sup> Behold, he with iniquity  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth travail, as in birth;  
A mischief he conceivèd hath,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and falsehood shall bring forth.

<sup>15</sup> He made a pit, and digged it deep,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;another there to take;  
But he is fall’n into the ditch  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which he himself did make.

<sup>16</sup> Upon his own head his mischief  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be returnèd home;  
His vi’lent dealing also down  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on his own pate shall come.

<sup>17</sup> According to his righteousness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD I’ll magnify;  
And will sing praise unto the name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of GOD that is most high.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 8

*To the chief Musician upon Gittith, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> How excellent in all the earth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;LORD, our Lord, is thy name!  
Who hast thy glory far advanced  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;above the starry frame.

<sup>2</sup> From infants’ and from sucklings’ mouth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou didest strength ordain,  
For thy foes’ cause, that so thou might’st  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;th’ avenging foe restrain.

<sup>3</sup> When I look up unto the heav’ns,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which thine own fingers framed,  
Unto the moon, and to the stars,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which were by thee ordained;

<sup>4</sup> Then say I, What is man, that he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;remembered is by thee?  
Or what the son of man, that thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;so kind to him should’st be?

<sup>5</sup> For thou a little lower hast  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;him than the angels made;  
With glory and with dignity  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou crownèd hast his head.

<sup>6</sup> Of thy hands’ works thou mad’st him lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all under ’s feet didst lay;  
<sup>7</sup> All sheep and oxen, yea, and beasts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that in the field do stray;

<sup>8</sup> Fowls of the air, fish of the sea,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all that pass through the same.  
<sup>9</sup> How excellent in all the earth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;LORD, our Lord, is thy name!

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 9

*To the chief Musician upon Muth-labben, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> LORD, thee I’ll praise with all my heart,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy wonders all proclaim.  
<sup>2</sup> In thee, Most High, I’ll greatly joy,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and sing unto thy name.

<sup>3</sup> When back my foes were turned, they fell,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and perished at thy sight:  
<sup>4</sup> For thou maintain’dst my right and cause;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on throne sat’st judging right.

<sup>5</sup> The heathen thou rebukèd hast,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the wicked overthrown;  
Thou hast put out their names, that they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;may never more be known.

<sup>6</sup> O en’my! now destructions have  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;an end perpetual:  
Thou cities razed, perished with them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is their memorial.

<sup>7</sup> GOD shall endure for aye; he doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for judgment set his throne;  
<sup>8</sup> In righteousness to judge the world,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;justice to give each one.

<sup>9</sup> GOD also will a refuge be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for those that are oppressed;  
A refuge will he be in times  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of trouble to distressed.

<sup>10</sup> And they that know thy name, in thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their confidence will place:  
For thou hast not forsaken them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that truly seek thy face.

<sup>11</sup> O sing ye praises to the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that dwells in Zion hill;  
And all the nätions among  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his deeds record ye still.

<sup>12</sup> When he enquireth after blood,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he then rememb’reth them:  
The humble folk he not forgets  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that call upon his name.

<sup>13</sup> LORD, pity me; behold the grief  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which I from foes sustain;  
Ev’n thou, who from the gates of death  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;dost raise me up again;

<sup>14</sup> That I, in Zion’s daughters’ gates,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;may all thy praise advance;  
And that I may rejoice always  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in thy deliverance.

<sup>15</sup> The heathen are sunk in the pit  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which they themselves prepared;  
And in the net which they have hid  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their own feet fast are snared.

<sup>16</sup> The LORD is by the judgment known  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which he himself hath wrought:  
The sinners’ hands do make the snares  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wherewith themselves are caught.

<sup>17</sup> They who are wicked into hell  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;each one shall turnèd be;  
And all the nations that forget  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to seek the Lord most high.

<sup>18</sup> For they that needy are shall not  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;forgotten be alway;  
The expectation of the poor  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall not be lost for aye.

<sup>19</sup> Arise, LORD, let not man prevail;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;judge heathen in thy sight:  
<sup>20</sup> That they may know themselves but men,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the nations, LORD, affright.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 10

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Wherefore is it that thou, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;dost stand from us afar?  
And wherefore hidest thou thyself  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when times so troublous are?

<sup>2</sup> The wicked in his loftiness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth persecute the poor:  
In these devices they have framed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let them be taken sure.

<sup>3</sup> The wicked of his heart’s desire  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth talk with boasting great;  
He blesseth him that’s covetous,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whom yet the LORD doth hate.

<sup>4</sup> The wicked, through his pride of face,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on God he doth not call;  
And in the counsels of his heart  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the Lord is not at all.

<sup>5</sup> His ways they always grievous are;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy judgments from his sight  
Removèd are: at all his foes  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he puffeth with despite.

<sup>6</sup> Within his heart he thus hath said,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I shall not movèd be;  
And no adversity at all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall ever come to me.

<sup>7</sup> His mouth with cursing, fraud, deceit,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is filled abundantly;  
And underneath his tongue there is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mischief and vanity.

<sup>8</sup> He closely sits in villages;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he slays the innocent:  
Against the poor that pass him by  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his cruel eyes are bent.

<sup>9</sup> He, lion-like, lurks in his den;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he waits the poor to take;  
And when he draws him in his net,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his prey he doth him make.

<sup>10</sup> Himself he humbleth very low,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he croucheth down withal,  
That so a multitude of poor  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;may by his strong ones fall.

<sup>11</sup> He thus hath said within his heart,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The Lord hath quite forgot;  
He hides his countenance, and he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for ever sees it not.

<sup>12</sup> O LORD, do thou arise; O God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;lift up thine hand on high:  
Put not the meek afflicted ones  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;out of thy memory.

<sup>13</sup> Why is it that the wicked man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thus doth the Lord despise?  
Because that God will it require  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he in his heart denies.

<sup>14</sup> Thou hast it seen; for their mischief  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and spite thou wilt repay:  
The poor commits himself to thee;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou art the orphan’s stay.

<sup>15</sup> The arm break of the wicked man,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and of the evil one;  
Do thou seek out his wickedness,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;until thou findest none.

<sup>16</sup> The LORD is king through ages all,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n to eternity;  
The heathen people from his land  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are perished utterly.

<sup>17</sup> O LORD, of those that humble are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou the desire didst hear;  
Thou wilt prepare their heart, and thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to hear wilt bend thine ear;

<sup>18</sup> To judge the fatherless, and those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that are oppressèd sore;  
That man, that is but sprung of earth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;may them oppress no more.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 11

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> I in the LORD do put my trust:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;how is it then that ye  
Say to my soul, Flee, as a bird,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto your mountain high?

<sup>2</sup> For, lo, the wicked bend their bow,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their shafts on string they fit,  
That those who upright are in heart  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they privily may hit.

<sup>3</sup> If the foundations be destroyed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;what hath the righteous done?  
<sup>4</sup> GOD in his holy temple is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in heaven is his throne:

His eyes do see, his eyelids try  
<sup>5</sup> men’s sons. The just he proves:  
But his soul hates the wicked man,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and him that vi’lence loves.

<sup>6</sup> Snares, fire and brimstone, furious storms,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on sinners he shall rain:  
This, as the portion of their cup,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth unto them pertain.

<sup>7</sup> Because the LORD most righteous doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in righteousness delight;  
And with a pleasant countenance  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;beholdeth the upright.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 12

*To the chief Musician upon Sheminith, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Help, LORD, because the godly man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth daily fade away;  
And from among the sons of men  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the faithful do decay.

<sup>2</sup> Unto his neighbour everyone  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth utter vanity:  
They with a double heart do speak,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and lips of flattery.

<sup>3</sup> GOD shall cut off all flatt’ring lips,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;tongues that speak proudly thus,  
<sup>4</sup> We’ll with our tongue prevail, our lips  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are ours: who’s lord o’er us?

<sup>5</sup> For poor oppressed, and for the sighs  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of needy, rise will I,  
Saith GOD, and him in safety set  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from such as him defy.

<sup>6</sup> The words of GOD are words most pure;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they be like silver tried  
In earthen furnace, seven times  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that hath been purified.

<sup>7</sup> LORD, thou shalt them preserve and keep  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for ever from this race.  
<sup>8</sup> On each side walk the wicked, when  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;vile men are high in place.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 13

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> How long wilt thou forget me, LORD?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall it for ever be?  
O how long shall it be that thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wilt hide thy face from me?

<sup>2</sup> How long take counsel in my soul,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;still sad in heart, shall I?  
How long exalted over me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be mine enemy?

<sup>3</sup> O LORD my God, consider well,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and answer to me make:  
Mine eyes enlighten, lest the sleep  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of death me overtake:

<sup>4</sup> Lest that mine enemy should say,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Against him I prevailed;  
And those that trouble me rejoice,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when I am moved and failed.

<sup>5</sup> But I have all my confidence  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy mercy set upon;  
My heart within me shall rejoice  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in thy salvätion.

<sup>6</sup> I will unto the LORD my God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sing praises cheerfully,  
Because he hath his bounty shown  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to me abundantly.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 14

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> That there is not a God, the fool  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth in his heart conclude:  
They are corrupt, their works are vile;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;not one of them doth good.

<sup>2</sup> Upon men’s sons the LORD from heav’n  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did cast his eyes abroad,  
To see if any understood,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and did seek after God.

<sup>3</sup> They altogether filthy are,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they all aside are gone;  
And there is none that doeth good,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;yea, sure there is not one.

<sup>4</sup> These workers of iniquity  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do they not know at all,  
That they my people eat as bread,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and on GOD do not call?

<sup>5</sup> There fear’d they much; for God is with  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the whole race of the just.  
<sup>6</sup> You shame the counsel of the poor,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;because GOD is his trust.

<sup>7</sup> Let Isr’el’s help from Zion come:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when back the LORD shall bring  
His captives, Jacob shall rejoice,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and Israèl shall sing.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 15

*A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Within thy tabernacle, LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who shall abide with thee?  
And in thy high and holy hill  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who shall a dweller be?

<sup>2</sup> The man that walketh uprightly,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and worketh righteousness,  
And as he thinketh in his heart,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;so doth he truth express.

<sup>3</sup> Who doth not slander with his tongue,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor to his friend doth hurt;  
Nor yet against his neighbour doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;take up an ill report.

<sup>4</sup> In whose eyes vile men are despised;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but those that GOD do fear  
He honoureth; and changeth not,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;though to his hurt he swear.

<sup>5</sup> His coin puts not to usury,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor take reward will he  
Against the guiltless. Who doth thus  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall never moved be.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 16

*Michtam of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Lord, keep me; for I trust in thee.  
<sup>2</sup> To GOD thus was my speech,  
Thou art my Lord; and unto thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my goodness doth not reach:

<sup>3</sup> To saints on earth, to th’ excellent,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;where my delight’s all placed.  
<sup>4</sup> Their sorrows shall be multiplied  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to other gods that haste:

Of their drink-offerings of blood  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I will no off’ring make;  
Yea, neither I their very names  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;up in my lips will take.

<sup>5</sup> GOD is of mine inheritance  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and cup the pörtion;  
The lot that fallen is to me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou dost maintain alone.

<sup>6</sup> Unto me happily the lines  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in pleasant places fell;  
Yea, the inheritance I got  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in beauty doth excel.

<sup>7</sup> I bless the LORD, because he doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by counsel me conduct;  
And in the seasons of the night  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my reins do me instruct.

<sup>8</sup> Before me still the LORD I set:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sith it is so that he  
Doth ever stand at my right hand,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I shall not movèd be.

<sup>9</sup> Because of this my heart is glad,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and joy shall be expressed  
Ev’n by my glory; and my flesh  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in confidence shall rest.

<sup>10</sup> Because my soul in grave to dwell  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall not be left by thee;  
Nor wilt thou give thine Holy One  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;corrüption to see.

<sup>11</sup> Thou wilt me show the path of life:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of joys there is full store  
Before thy face; at thy right hand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are pleasures evermore.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 17

*A Prayer of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> LORD, hear the right, attend my cry,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto my pray’r give heed,  
That doth not in hypocrisy  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from feignèd lips proceed.

<sup>2</sup> And from before thy presence forth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my sentence do thou send:  
Toward these things that equal are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do thou thine eyes intend.

<sup>3</sup> Thou prov’dst mine heart, thou visit’dst me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by night, thou didst me try,  
Yet nothing found’st; for that my mouth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall not sin, purposed I.

<sup>4</sup> As for men’s works, I, by the word  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that from thy lips doth flow,  
Did me preserve out of the paths  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wherein destroyers go.

<sup>5</sup> Hold up my goings, Lord, me guide  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in those thy paths divine,  
So that my footsteps may not slide  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;out of those ways of thine.

<sup>6</sup> I callèd have on thee, O God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;because thou wilt me hear:  
That thou may’st hearken to my speech,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to me incline thine ear.

<sup>7</sup> Thy wondrous loving-kindness show,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou that, by thy right hand,  
Sav’st them that trust in thee from those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that up against them stand.

<sup>8</sup> As th’ apple of the eye me keep;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in thy wings’ shade me close  
<sup>9</sup> From lewd oppressors, compassing  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;me round, as deadly foes.

<sup>10</sup> In their own fat they are inclosed;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their mouth speaks loftily.  
<sup>11</sup> Our steps they compassed; and to ground  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;down bowing set their eye.

<sup>12</sup> He like unto a lion is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that’s greedy of his prey,  
Or lion young, which lurking doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in secret places stay.

<sup>13</sup> Arise, and disappoint my foe,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and cast him down, O LORD:  
My soul save from the wicked man,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the man which is thy sword.

<sup>14</sup> From men, which are thy hand, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from worldly men me save,  
Which only in this present life  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their part and portion have.

Whose belly with thy treasure hid  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou fill’st: they children have  
In plenty; of their goods the rest  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they to their children leave.

<sup>15</sup> But as for me, I thine own face  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in righteousness will see;  
And with thy likeness, when I wake,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I satisfied shall be.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 18

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm of David, the servant of the Lord, who spake unto the Lord the words of this song in the day that the Lord delivered him from the hand of all his enemies, and from the hand of Saul: And he said,*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Thee will I love, O LORD, my strength.  
<sup>2</sup> My fortress is the LORD,  
My rock, and he that doth to me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;deliverance afford:

My God, my strength, whom I will trust,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a buckler unto me,  
The horn of my salvätion,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and my high tow’r, is he.

<sup>3</sup> Upon the LORD, who worthy is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of praises, will I cry;  
And then shall I preservèd be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;safe from mine enemy.

<sup>4</sup> Floods of ill men affrighted me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;death’s pangs about me went;  
<sup>5</sup> Hell’s sorrows me environèd;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;death’s snares did me prevent.

<sup>6</sup> In my distress I called on God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cry to my God did I;  
He from his temple heard my voice,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to his ears came my cry.

<sup>7</sup> Th’ earth, as affrighted, then did shake,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;trembling upon it seized:  
The hills’ foundations movèd were,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;because he was displeased.

<sup>8</sup> Up from his nostrils came a smoke,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and from his mouth there came  
Devouring fire, and coals by it  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;were turnèd into flame.

<sup>9</sup> He also bowèd down the heav’ns,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and thence he did descend;  
And thickest clouds of darkness did  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;under his feet attend.

<sup>10</sup> And he upon a cherub rode,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and thereon he did fly;  
Yea, on the swift wings of the wind  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his flight was from on high.

<sup>11</sup> He darkness made his secret place:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;about him, for his tent,  
Dark waters were, and thickest clouds  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of th’ airy firmament.

<sup>12</sup> And at the brightness of that light,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which was before his eye,  
His thick clouds passed away, hailstones  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and coals of fire did fly.

<sup>13</sup> The LORD God also in the heav’ns  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did thunder in his ire;  
And there the Highest gave his voice,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hailstones and coals of fire.

<sup>14</sup> Yea, he his arrows sent abroad,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and them he scatterèd;  
His lightnings also he shot out,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and them discomfited.

<sup>15</sup> The waters’ channels then were seen,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the world’s foundations vast  
At thy rebuke discovered were,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and at thy nostrils’ blast.

<sup>16</sup> And from above the Lord sent down,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and took me from below;  
From many waters he me drew,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which would me overflow.

<sup>17</sup> He me relieved from my strong foes,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and such as did me hate;  
Because he saw that they for me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;too strong were, and too great.

<sup>18</sup> They me prevented in the day  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of my calamity;  
But even then the LORD himself  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a stay was unto me.

<sup>19</sup> He to a place where liberty  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and room was hath me brought;  
Because he took delight in me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he my deliv’rance wrought.

<sup>20</sup> According to my righteousness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he did me recompense,  
He me repaid according to  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my hands’ pure innocence.

<sup>21</sup> For I GOD’s ways kept, from my God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did not turn wickedly.  
<sup>22</sup> His judgments were before me, I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his laws put not from me.

<sup>23</sup> Sincere before him was my heart;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with him upright was I;  
And watchfully I kept myself  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from mine iniquity.

<sup>24</sup> After my righteousness the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hath recompensèd me,  
After the cleanness of my hands  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;appearing in his eye.

<sup>25</sup> Thou gracious to the gracious art,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to upright men upright:  
<sup>26</sup> Pure to the pure, froward thou kyth’st  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto the froward wight.

<sup>27</sup> For thou wilt the afflicted save  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in grief that low do lie:  
But wilt bring down the countenance  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of them whose looks are high.

<sup>28</sup> The LORD will light my candle so,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that it shall shine full bright:  
The LORD my God will also make  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my darkness to be light.

<sup>29</sup> By thee through troops of men I break,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and them discomfit all;  
And, by my God assisting me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I overleap a wall.

<sup>30</sup> As for God, perfect is his way:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD his word is tried;  
He is a buckler to all those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who do in him confide.

<sup>31</sup> Who but the LORD is God? but he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who is a rock and stay?  
<sup>32</sup> ’Tis God that girdeth me with strength,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and perfect makes my way.

<sup>33</sup> He made my feet swift as the hinds,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;set me on my high places.  
<sup>34</sup> Mine hands to war he taught, mine arms  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;brake bows of steel in pieces.

<sup>35</sup> The shield of thy salvätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou didst on me bestow:  
Thy right hand held me up, and great  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy kindness made me grow.

<sup>36</sup> And in my way my steps thou hast  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;enlargèd under me,  
That I go safely, and my feet  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are kept from sliding free.

<sup>37</sup> Mine en’mies I pursuèd have,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and did them overtake;  
Nor did I turn again till I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;an end of them did make.

<sup>38</sup> I wounded them, they could not rise;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they at my feet did fall.  
<sup>39</sup> Thou girdest me with strength for war;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my foes thou brought’st down all:

<sup>40</sup> And thou hast giv’n to me the necks  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of all mine enemies;  
That I might them destroy and slay,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who did against me rise.

<sup>41</sup> They crièd out, but there was none  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that would or could them save;  
Yea, they did cry unto the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but he no answer gave.

<sup>42</sup> Then did I beat them small as dust  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before the wind that flies;  
And I did cast them out like dirt  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon the street that lies.

<sup>43</sup> Thou mad’st me free from people’s strife,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and heathen’s head to be:  
A people whom I have not known  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall service do to me.

<sup>44</sup> At hearing they shall me obey,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to me they shall submit.  
<sup>45</sup> Strangers for fear shall fade away,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who in close places sit.

<sup>46</sup> GOD lives, bless’d be my Rock; the God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of my health praisèd be.  
<sup>47</sup> God doth avenge me, and subdues  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the people under me.

<sup>48</sup> He saves me from mine enemies;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;yea, thou hast lifted me  
Above my foes; and from the man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of vi’lence set me free.

<sup>49</sup> Therefore to thee will I give thanks  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the heathen folk among;  
And to thy name, O LORD, I will  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sing praises in a song.

<sup>50</sup> He great deliv’rance gives his king:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he mercy doth extend  
To David, his anointed one,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and his seed without end.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 19

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> The heav’ns God’s glory do declare,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the skies his hand-works preach:  
<sup>2</sup> Day utters speech to day, and night  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to night doth knowledge teach.

<sup>3</sup> There is no speech nor tongue to which  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their voice doth not extend:  
<sup>4</sup> Their line is gone through all the earth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their words to the world’s end.

In them he set the sun a tent;  
<sup>5</sup> Who, bridegroom-like, forth goes  
From’s chamber, as a strong man doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to run his race rejoice.

<sup>6</sup> From heav’n’s end is his going forth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;circling to th’ end again;  
And there is nothing from his heat  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that hidden doth remain.

<sup>7</sup> GOD’s law is perfect, and converts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the soul in sin that lies:  
GOD’s testimony is most sure,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and makes the simple wise.

<sup>8</sup> The statutes of the LORD are right,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and do rejoice the heart:  
The LORD’s command is pure, and doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;light to the eyes impart.

<sup>9</sup> Unspotted is the fear of GOD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and doth endure for ever:  
The judgments of the LORD are true  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and righteous altogether.

<sup>10</sup> They more than gold, yea, much fine gold,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to be desirèd are:  
Than honey, honey from the comb  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that droppeth, sweeter far.

<sup>11</sup> Moreover, they thy servant warn  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;how he his life should frame:  
A great reward provided is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for them that keep the same.

<sup>12</sup> Who can his errors understand?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O cleanse thou me within  
<sup>13</sup> From secret faults. Thy servant keep  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from all presumptuous sin:

And do not suffer them to have  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;dominion over me:  
Then rïghteous and innocent  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I from much sin shall be.

<sup>14</sup> The words which from my mouth proceed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the thoughts sent from my heart,  
Accept, O LORD, for thou my strength  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and my Redeemer art.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 20

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> JEHOVAH hear thee in the day  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when trouble he doth send:  
And let the name of Jacob’s God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thee from all ill defend.

<sup>2</sup> O let him help send from above,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;out of his sanctuary:  
From Zion, his own holy hill,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let him give strength to thee.

<sup>3</sup> Let him remember all thy gifts,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;accept thy sacrifice:  
<sup>4</sup> Grant thee thine heart’s wish, and fulfil  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy thoughts and counsel wise.

<sup>5</sup> In thy salvation we will joy;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in our God’s name we will  
Display our banners: and the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy prayers all fulfil.

<sup>6</sup> Now know I GOD his king doth save:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he from his holy heav’n  
Will hear him, with the saving strength  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by his own right hand giv’n.

<sup>7</sup> In chariots some put confidence,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;some horses trust upon:  
But we remember will the name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of our LORD God alone.

<sup>8</sup> We rise, and upright stand, when they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are bowèd down, and fall.  
<sup>9</sup> Deliver, LORD; and let the King  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;us hear, when we do call.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 21

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> The king in thy great strength, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall very joyful be:  
In thy salvätion rejoice  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;how veh’mently shall he!

<sup>2</sup> Thou hast bestowèd upon him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all that his heart would have;  
And thou from him didst not withhold  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whate’er his lips did crave.

<sup>3</sup> For thou with blessings him prevent’st  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of goodness manifold;  
And thou hast set upon his head  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a crown of purest gold.

<sup>4</sup> When he desirèd life of thee,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou life to him didst give;  
Ev’n such a length of days, that he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for evermore should live.

<sup>5</sup> In that salvation wrought by thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his glory is made great;  
Honour and comely majesty  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou hast upon him set.

<sup>6</sup> Because that thou for evermore  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;most blessèd hast him made;  
And thou hast with thy countenance  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;made him exceeding glad.

<sup>7</sup> Because the king upon the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his confidence doth lay;  
And through the grace of the Most High  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall not be moved away.

<sup>8</sup> Thine hand shall all those men find out  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that en’mies are to thee;  
Ev’n thy right hand shall find out those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of thee that haters be.

<sup>9</sup> Like fiery ov’n thou shalt them make,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when kindled is thine ire;  
GOD shall them swallow in his wrath,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;devour them shall the fire.

<sup>10</sup> Their fruit from earth thou shalt destroy,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their seed men from among:  
<sup>11</sup> For they beyond their might ’gainst thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did plot mischief and wrong.

<sup>12</sup> Thou therefore shalt make them turn back,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when thou thy shafts shalt place  
Upon thy strings, made ready all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to fly against their face.

<sup>13</sup> In thy great pow’r and strength, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be thou exalted high;  
So shall we sing with joyful hearts,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy power praise shall we.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 22

*To the chief Musician upon Aijeleth Shahar, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> My God, my God, why hast thou me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;forsaken? why so far  
Art thou from helping me, and from  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my words that roaring are?

<sup>2</sup> All day, my God, to thee I cry,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;yet am not heard by thee;  
And in the season of the night  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I cannot silent be.

<sup>3</sup> But thou art holy, thou that dost  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;inhabit Isr’el’s praise.  
<sup>4</sup> Our fathers hoped in thee, they hoped,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and thou didst them release.

<sup>5</sup> When unto thee they sent their cry,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to them deliv’rance came:  
Because they put their trust in thee,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they were not put to shame.

<sup>6</sup> But as for me, a worm I am,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and as no man am prized:  
Reproach of men I am, and by  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the people am despised.

<sup>7</sup> All that me see laugh me to scorn;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shoot out the lip do they;  
They nod and shake their heads at me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and, mocking, thus do say,

<sup>8</sup> This man did trust in GOD, that he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;would free him by his might:  
Let him deliver him, sith he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;had in him such delight.

<sup>9</sup> But thou art he out of the womb  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that didst me safely take;  
When I was on my mother’s breasts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou me to hope didst make.

<sup>10</sup> And I was cast upon thy care,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n from the womb till now;  
And from my mother’s belly, Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my God and guide art thou.

<sup>11</sup> Be not far off, for grief is near,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and none to help is found.  
<sup>12</sup> Bulls many compass me, strong bulls  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of Bashan me surround.

<sup>13</sup> Their mouths they opened wide on me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon me gape did they,  
Like to a lion ravening  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and roaring for his prey.

<sup>14</sup> Like water I’m poured out, my bones  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all out of joint do part:  
Amidst my bowels, as the wax,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;so melted is my heart.

<sup>15</sup> My strength is like a potsherd dried;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my tongue it cleaveth fast  
Unto my jaws; and to the dust  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of death thou brought me hast.

<sup>16</sup> For dogs have compassed me about:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the wicked, that did meet  
In their assembly, me inclosed;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they pierced my hands and feet.

<sup>17</sup> I all my bones may tell; they do  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon me look and stare.  
<sup>18</sup> Upon my vesture lots they cast,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and clothes among them share.

<sup>19</sup> But be not far, O LORD, my strength;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;haste to give help to me.  
<sup>20</sup> From sword my soul, from pow’r of dogs  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my darling set thou free.

<sup>21</sup> Out of the roaring lion’s mouth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do thou me shield and save:  
For from the horns of unicorns  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;an ear to me thou gave.

<sup>22</sup> I will show forth thy name unto  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;those that my brethren are;  
Amidst the congregätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy praise I will declare.

<sup>23</sup> Praise ye the LORD, who do him fear;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;him glorify all ye  
The seed of Jacob: fear him all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that Isr’el’s children be.

<sup>24</sup> For he despised not nor abhorred  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;th’ afflicted’s misery;  
Nor from him hid his face, but heard  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when he to him did cry.

<sup>25</sup> Within the congregation great  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my praise shall be of thee;  
My vows before them that him fear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be performed by me.

<sup>26</sup> The meek shall eat, and shall be filled;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they also praise shall give  
Unto the LORD that do him seek:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;your heart shall ever live.

<sup>27</sup> All ends of th’ earth remember shall,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and turn the LORD unto;  
All kindreds of the nätions  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to him shall homage do:

<sup>28</sup> Because the kingdom to the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth appertain as his;  
Likewise among the nätions  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the Governor he is.

<sup>29</sup> Earth’s fat ones eat, and worship shall:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all who to dust descend  
Shall bow to him; none of them can  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his soul from death defend.

<sup>30</sup> A seed shall service do to him;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto the Lord it shall  
Be for a generätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;reckoned in ages all.

<sup>31</sup> They shall come, and they shall declare  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his truth and righteousness  
Unto a people yet unborn,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and that he hath done this.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 23

*A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> The LORD’s my shepherd, I’ll not want.  
<sup>2</sup> He makes me down to lie  
In pastures green: he leadeth me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the quiet waters by.

<sup>3</sup> My soul he doth restore again;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and me to walk doth make  
Within the paths of righteousness,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n for his own name’s sake.

<sup>4</sup> Yea, though I walk in death’s dark vale,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;yet will I fear none ill:  
For thou art with me; and thy rod  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and staff me comfort still.

<sup>5</sup> My table thou hast furnishèd  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in presence of my foes;  
My head thou dost with oil anoint,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and my cup overflows.

<sup>6</sup> Goodness and mercy all my life  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall surely follow me:  
And in GOD’s house for evermore  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my dwelling-place shall be.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 24

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> The earth belongs unto the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and all that it contains;  
The world that is inhabited,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and all that there remains.

<sup>2</sup> For the foundätions thereof  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he on the seas did lay,  
And he hath it establishèd  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon the floods to stay.

<sup>3</sup> Who is the man that shall ascend  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;into the hill of GOD?  
Or who within his holy place  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall have a firm abode?

<sup>4</sup> Whose hands are clean, whose heart is pure,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and unto vanity  
Who hath not lifted up his soul,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor sworn deceitfully.

<sup>5</sup> He from th’ ETERNAL shall receive  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the blessing him upon,  
And righteousness, ev’n from the God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of his salvätion.

<sup>6</sup> This is the generätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that after him enquire,  
O Jacob, who do seek thy face  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with their whole heart’s desire.

<sup>7</sup> Ye gates, lift up your heads on high;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ye doors that last for aye,  
Be lifted up, that so the King  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of glory enter may.

<sup>8</sup> But who of glory is the King?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The mighty LORD is this;  
Ev’n that same LORD, that great in might  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and strong in battle is.

<sup>9</sup> Ye gates, lift up your heads; ye doors,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doors that do last for aye,  
Be lifted up, that so the King  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of glory enter may.

<sup>10</sup> But who is he that is the King  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of glory? who is this?  
The LORD of hosts, and none but he,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the King of glory is.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 25

*A Psalm of David.*

### Version 1

*S.M.*

<sup>1</sup> To thee I lift my soul:  
<sup>2</sup> O LORD, I trust in thee:  
My God, let me not be asham’d,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor foes triumph o’er me.

<sup>3</sup> Let none that wait on thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be put to shame at all;  
But those that without cause transgress,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let shame upon them fall.

<sup>4</sup> Show me thy ways, O LORD;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy paths, O teach thou me:  
<sup>5</sup> And do thou lead me in thy truth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;therein my teacher be:

For thou art God that dost  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to me salvation send,  
And I upon thee all the day  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;expecting do attend.

<sup>6</sup> Thy tender mercies, LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I pray thee to remember,  
And loving-kindnesses; for they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;have been of old for ever.

<sup>7</sup> My sins and faults of youth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do thou, O LORD, forget:  
After thy mercy think on me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and for thy goodness great.

<sup>8</sup> GOD good and upright is:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the way he’ll sinners show.  
<sup>9</sup> The meek in judgment he will guide,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and make his path to know.

<sup>10</sup> The whole paths of the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are truth and mercy sure,  
To those that do his cov’nant keep,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and testimonies pure.

<sup>11</sup> Now, for thine own name’s sake,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O LORD, I thee entreat  
To pardon mine iniquity;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for it is very great.

<sup>12</sup> What man is he that fears  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD, and doth him serve?  
Him shall he teach the way that he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall choose, and still observe.

<sup>13</sup> His soul shall dwell at ease;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and his posterity  
Shall flourish still, and of the earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;inheritors shall be.

<sup>14</sup> With those that fear him is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the secret of the LORD;  
The knowledge of his covènant  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he will to them afford.

<sup>15</sup> Mine eyes upon the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;continually are set;  
For he it is that shall bring forth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my feet out of the net.

<sup>16</sup> Turn unto me thy face,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and to me mercy show;  
Because that I am desolate,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and am brought very low.

<sup>17</sup> My heart’s griefs are increased:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;me from distress relieve.  
<sup>18</sup> See mine affliction and my pain,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and all my sins forgive.

<sup>19</sup> Consider thou my foes,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;because they many are;  
And it a cruel hatred is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which they against me bear.

<sup>20</sup> O do thou keep my soul,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do thou deliver me:  
And let me never be ashamed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;because I trust in thee.

<sup>21</sup> Let uprightness and truth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;keep me, who thee attend.  
<sup>22</sup> Redemption, Lord, to Israel  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from all his troubles send.

---

### Version 2

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> To thee I lift my soul, O LORD:  
<sup>2</sup> my God, I trust in thee:  
Let me not be ashamed; let not  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my foes triumph o’er me.

<sup>3</sup> Yea, let thou none ashamèd be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that do on thee attend:  
Ashamèd let them be, O Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who without cause offend.

<sup>4</sup> Thy ways, LORD, show; teach me thy paths:  
<sup>5</sup> lead me in truth, teach me:  
For of my safety thou art God;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all day I wait on thee.

<sup>6</sup> Thy mercies, that most tender are,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do thou, O LORD, remember,  
And loving-kindnesses; for they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;have been of old for ever.

<sup>7</sup> Let not the errors of my youth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor sins, remembered be:  
In mercy, for thy goodness’ sake,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O LORD, remember me.

<sup>8</sup> The LORD is good and gräcious,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he upright is also:  
He therefore sinners will instruct  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in ways that they should go.

<sup>9</sup> The meek and lowly he will guide  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in judgment just alway:  
To meek and poor afflicted ones  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he’ll clearly teach his way.

<sup>10</sup> The whole paths of the LORD our God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are truth and mercy sure,  
To such as keep his covènant,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and testimonies pure.

<sup>11</sup> Now, for thine own name’s sake, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I humbly thee entreat  
To pardon mine iniquity;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for it is very great.

<sup>12</sup> What man fears GOD? him shall he teach  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the way that he shall choose.  
<sup>13</sup> His soul shall dwell at ease; his seed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the earth, as heirs, shall use.

<sup>14</sup> The secret of the LORD is with  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;such as do fear his name;  
And he his holy covènant  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;will manifest to them.

<sup>15</sup> Towards the LORD my waiting eyes  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;continually are set;  
For he it is that shall bring forth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my feet out of the net.

<sup>16</sup> O turn thee unto me, O God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;have mercy me upon;  
Because I solitary am,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and in afflïction.

<sup>17</sup> Enlarged the griefs are of mine heart;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;me from distress relieve.  
<sup>18</sup> See mine affliction and my pain,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and all my sins forgive.

<sup>19</sup> Consider thou mine enemies,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;because they many are;  
And it a cruel hatred is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which they against me bear.

<sup>20</sup> O do thou keep my soul; O God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do thou deliver me:  
Let me not be ashamed; for I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do put my trust in thee.

<sup>21</sup> O let integrity and truth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;keep me, who thee attend.  
<sup>22</sup> Redemption, Lord, to Israel  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from all his troubles send.
