## Psalm 26

*A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Judge me, O LORD, for I have walked  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in mine integrity:  
I trusted also in the LORD;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;slide therefore shall not I.

<sup>2</sup> Examine me, and do me prove;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;try heart and reins, O GOD:  
<sup>3</sup> For thy love is before mine eyes,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy truth’s paths I have trod.

<sup>4</sup> With persons vain I have not sat,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor with dissemblers gone:  
<sup>5</sup> Th’ assembly of ill men I hate;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to sit with such I shun.

<sup>6</sup> Mine hands in innocence, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I’ll wash and purify;  
So to thine holy altar go,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and compass it will I:

<sup>7</sup> That I, with voice of thanksgiving,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;may publish and declare,  
And tell of all thy mighty works,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that great and wondrous are.

<sup>8</sup> The habitation of thy house,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;LORD, I have lovèd well;  
Yea, in that place I do delight  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;where doth thine honour dwell.

<sup>9</sup> With sinners gather not my soul,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and such as blood would spill:  
<sup>10</sup> Whose hands mischievous plots, right hand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;corrupting bribes do fill.

<sup>11</sup> But as for me, I will walk on  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in mine integrity:  
Do thou redeem me, and, O Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be merciful to me.

<sup>12</sup> My foot upon an even place  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth stand with steadfastness:  
Within the congregätions  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;th’ ETERNAL I will bless.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 27

*A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> The LORD’s my light and saving health,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who shall make me dismayed?  
My life’s strength is the LORD, of whom  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;then shall I be afraid?

<sup>2</sup> When as mine enemies and foes,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;most wicked persons all,  
To eat my flesh against me rose,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they stumbled and did fall.

<sup>3</sup> Against me though an host encamp,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my heart yet fearless is:  
Though war against me rise, I will  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be confident in this.

<sup>4</sup> One thing I of the LORD desired,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and will seek to obtain,  
That all days of my life I may  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within GOD’s house remain;

That I the beauty of the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;behold may and admire,  
And that I in his holy place  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;may rev’rently enquire.

<sup>5</sup> For he in his pavilion shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;me hide in evil days;  
In secret of his tent me hide,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and on a rock me raise.

<sup>6</sup> And now, ev’n at this present time,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mine head shall lifted be  
Above all those that are my foes,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and round encompass me:

Therefore unto his tabernacle  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I’ll sacrifices bring  
Of joyfulness; I’ll sing, yea, I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to GOD will praises sing.

<sup>7</sup> O LORD, give ear unto my voice,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when I do cry to thee;  
Upon me also mercy have,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and do thou answer me.

<sup>8</sup> When thou didst say, Seek ye my face,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;then unto thee reply  
Thus did my heart, Above all things  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy face, LORD, seek will I.

<sup>9</sup> Far from me hide not thou thy face;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;put not away from thee  
Thy servant in thy wrath: thou hast  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;an helper been to me.

O God of my salvätion,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;leave me not, nor forsake:  
<sup>10</sup> Though me my parents both should leave,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD will me up take.

<sup>11</sup> O LORD, instruct me in thy way,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to me a leader be  
In a plain path, because of those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that hatred bear to me.

<sup>12</sup> Give me not to mine en’mies’ will;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for witnesses that lie  
Against me risen are, and such  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as breathe out cruelty.

<sup>13</sup> I fainted had, unless that I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;believed had to see  
The LORD’s own goodness in the land  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of them that living be.

<sup>14</sup> Wait on the LORD, and be thou strong,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and he shall strength afford  
Unto thine heart; yea, do thou wait,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I say, upon the LORD.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 28

*A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> To thee I’ll cry, O LORD, my rock;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hold not thy peace to me;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Lest like those that to pit descend  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I by thy silence be.

<sup>2</sup> The voice hear of my humble pray’rs,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when unto thee I cry;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;When to thine holy oracle  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I lift mine hands on high.

<sup>3</sup> With ill men draw me not away  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that work iniquity;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;That speak peace to their friends, while in  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their hearts doth mischief lie.

<sup>4</sup> Give them according to their deeds  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and ills endeavourèd:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And as their handiworks deserve,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to them be renderèd.

<sup>5</sup> God shall not build, but them destroy,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who would not understand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The LORD’s own works, nor did regard  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the doing of his hand.

<sup>6</sup> For ever blessèd be the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for graciously he heard  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The voice of my petïtions,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and prayers did regard.

<sup>7</sup> The LORD’s my strength and shield; my  
heart  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon him did rely;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And I am helpèd: hence my heart  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth joy exceedingly.

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And with my song I will him praise.  
<sup>8</sup> Their strength is GOD alone:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;He also is the saving strength  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of his anointed one.

<sup>9</sup> O thine own people do thou save,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;bless thine inheritance;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Them also do thou feed, and them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for evermore advance.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 29

*A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Give ye unto the LORD, ye sons  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that of the mighty be,  
All strength and glory to the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with cheerfulness give ye.

<sup>2</sup> Unto the LORD the glory give  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that to his name is due;  
And in the beauty of holiness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto JEHOVAH bow.

<sup>3</sup> The LORD’s voice on the waters is;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the God of majesty  
Doth thunder, and on multitudes  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of waters sitteth he.

<sup>4</sup> A pow’rful voice it is that comes  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;out from the LORD most high;  
The voice of that great LORD is full  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of glorious majesty.

<sup>5</sup> The voice of the ETERNAL doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;asunder cedars tear;  
Yea, God the LORD doth cedars break  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that Lebanon doth bear.

<sup>6</sup> He makes them like a calf to skip,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n that great Lebanon,  
And, like to a young unicorn,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the mountain Sirion.

<sup>7</sup> God’s voice divides the flames of fire;  
<sup>8</sup> the desert it doth shake:  
The LORD doth make the wilderness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of Kadesh all to quake.

<sup>9</sup> GOD’s voice doth make the hinds to calve,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it makes the forest bare:  
And in his temple everyone  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his glory doth declare.

<sup>10</sup> The LORD sits on the floods; the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sits King, and ever shall.  
<sup>11</sup> The LORD will give his people strength,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and with peace bless them all.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 30

*A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> LORD, I will thee extol, for thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hast lifted me on high,  
And over me thou to rejoice  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mad’st not mine enemy.

<sup>2</sup> O thou who art the LORD my God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I in distress to thee,  
With loud cries lifted up my voice,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and thou hast healèd me.

<sup>3</sup> O LORD, my soul thou hast brought up,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and rescued from the grave;  
That I to pit should not go down,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;alive thou didst me save.

<sup>4</sup> O ye that are his holy ones,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sing praise unto the LORD;  
And give unto him thanks, when ye  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his holiness record.

<sup>5</sup> For but a moment lasts his wrath;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;life in his favour lies:  
Weeping may for a night endure,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;at morn doth joy arise.

<sup>6</sup> In my prosperity I said,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that nothing shall me move.  
<sup>7</sup> O LORD, thou hast my mountain made  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to stand strong by thy love:

But when that thou, O gracious God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;didst hide thy face from me,  
Then quickly was my prosp’rous state  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;turned into misery.

<sup>8</sup> Wherefore unto the LORD my cry  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I causèd to ascend:  
My humble supplicätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I to the LORD did send.

<sup>9</sup> What profit is there in my blood,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when I go down to pit?  
Shall unto thee the dust give praise?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy truth declare shall it?

<sup>10</sup> Hear, LORD, have mercy; help me, LORD:  
<sup>11</sup> Thou turnèd hast my sadness  
To dancing; yea, my sackcloth loosed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and girded me with gladness;

<sup>12</sup> That sing thy praise my glory may,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and never silent be.  
O LORD my God, for evermore  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I will give thanks to thee.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 31

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> In thee, O LORD, I put my trust,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shamed let me never be;  
According to thy righteousness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do thou deliver me.

<sup>2</sup> Bow down thine ear to me, with speed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;send me deliverance:  
To save me, my strong rock be thou,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and my house of defence.

<sup>3</sup> Because thou art my rock, and thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I for my fortress take;  
Therefore do thou me lead and guide,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n for thine own name’s sake.

<sup>4</sup> And sith thou art my strength, therefore  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;pull me out of the net,  
Which they in subtlety for me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;so privily have set.

<sup>5</sup> Into thine hands I do commit  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my spirit: for thou art he,  
O thou, JEHOVAH, God of truth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that hast redeemèd me.

<sup>6</sup> Those that do lying vanities  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;regard, I have abhorred:  
But as for me, my confidence  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is fixèd on the LORD.

<sup>7</sup> I’ll in thy mercy gladly joy:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for thou my miseries  
Considered hast; thou hast my soul  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;known in adversities:

<sup>8</sup> And thou hast not inclosèd me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within the en’my’s hand;  
And by thee have my feet been made  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in a large room to stand.

<sup>9</sup> O LORD, upon me mercy have,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for trouble is on me:  
Mine eye, my belly, and my soul,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with grief consumèd be.

<sup>10</sup> Because my life with grief is spent,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my years with sighs and groans:  
My strength doth fail; and for my sin  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;consumèd are my bones.

<sup>11</sup> I was a scorn to all my foes,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and to my friends a fear;  
And specially reproached of those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that were my neighbours near:

When they me saw they from me fled.  
<sup>12</sup> Ev’n so I am forgot,  
As men are out of mind when dead:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I’m like a broken pot.

<sup>13</sup> For slanders I of many heard;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;fear compassed me, while they  
Against me did consult, and plot  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to take my life away.

<sup>14</sup> But as for me, O LORD, my trust  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon thee I did lay;  
And I to thee, Thou art my God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did confidently say.

<sup>15</sup> My times are wholly in thine hand:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do thou deliver me  
From their hands that mine enemies  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and persecutors be.

<sup>16</sup> Thy countenance to shine do thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon thy servant make:  
Unto me give salvätion,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for thy great mercies’ sake.

<sup>17</sup> Let me not be ashamed, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for on thee called I have:  
Let wicked men be shamed, let them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be silent in the grave.

<sup>18</sup> To silence put the lying lips,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that grievous things do say,  
And hard reports, in pride and scorn,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on righteous men do lay.

<sup>19</sup> How great’s the goodness thou for them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that fear thee keep’st in store,  
And wrought’st for them that trust in thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the sons of men before!

<sup>20</sup> In secret of thy presence thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shalt hide them from man’s pride:  
From strife of tongues thou closely shalt,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as in a tent, them hide.

<sup>21</sup> All praise and thanks be to the LORD;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for he hath magnified  
His wondrous love to me within  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a city fortified.

<sup>22</sup> For from thine eyes cut off I am,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I in my haste had said;  
My voice yet heard’st thou, when to thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with cries my moan I made.

<sup>23</sup> O love the LORD, all ye his saints;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;because the LORD doth guard  
The faithful, and he plenteously  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;proud doers doth reward.

<sup>24</sup> Be of good courage, and he strength  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto your heart shall send,  
All ye whose hope and confidence  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth on the LORD depend.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 32

*A Psalm of David, Maschil.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O blessèd is the man to whom  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is freely pardonèd  
All the transgression he hath done,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whose sin is coverèd.

<sup>2</sup> Blessed is the man to whom the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;imputeth not his sin,  
And in whose spirit there is no guile,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor fraud is found therein.

<sup>3</sup> When as I did refrain my speech,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and silent was my tongue,  
My bones then waxèd old, because  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I roarèd all day long.

<sup>4</sup> For upon me both day and night  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thine hand did heavy lie,  
So that my moisture turnèd is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in summer’s drought thereby.

<sup>5</sup> I thereupon have unto thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my sin acknowledgèd,  
And likewise mine iniquity  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I have not coverèd:

I will confess unto the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my trespasses, said I;  
And of my sin thou freely didst  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;forgive th’ iniquity.

<sup>6</sup> For this shall ev’ry godly one  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his prayer make to thee;  
In such a time he shall thee seek,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as found thou mayest be.

Surely, when floods of waters great  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do swell up to the brim,  
They shall not overwhelm his soul,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor once come near to him.

<sup>7</sup> Thou art my hiding-place, thou shalt  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from trouble keep me free;  
Thou with songs of deliverance  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;about shalt compass me.

<sup>8</sup> I will instruct thee, and thee teach  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the way that thou shalt go;  
And, with mine eye upon thee set,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I will direction show.

<sup>9</sup> Then be not like the horse or mule,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which do not understand;  
Whose mouth, lest they come near to thee,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a bridle must command.

<sup>10</sup> Unto the man that wicked is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his sorrows shall abound;  
But him that trusteth in the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mercy shall compass round.

<sup>11</sup> Ye righteous, in the LORD be glad,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in him do ye rejoice:  
All ye that upright are in heart,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for joy lift up your voice.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 33

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Ye righteous, in the LORD rejoice;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it comely is and right,  
That upright men, with thankful voice,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;should praise the Lord of might.

<sup>2</sup> Praise GOD with harp, and unto him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sing with the psaltery;  
Upon a ten-stringed instrument  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;make ye sweet melody.

<sup>3</sup> A new song to him sing, and play  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with loud noise skilfully;  
<sup>4</sup> For right is GOD’s word, all his works  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are done in verity.

<sup>5</sup> To judgment and to righteousness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a love he beareth still;  
The loving-kindness of the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the earth throughout doth fill.

<sup>6</sup> The heavens by the word of GOD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did their beginning take;  
And by the breathing of his mouth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he all their hosts did make.

<sup>7</sup> The waters of the seas he brings  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;together as an heap;  
And in storehouses, as it were,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he layeth up the deep.

<sup>8</sup> Let earth, and all that live therein,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with rev’rence fear the LORD;  
Let all the world’s inhabitants  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;dread him with one accord.

<sup>9</sup> For he did speak the word, and done  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it was without delay;  
Establishèd it firmly stood,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whatever he did say.

<sup>10</sup> GOD doth the counsel bring to nought  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which heathen folk do take;  
And what the people do devise  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of none effect doth make.

<sup>11</sup> O but the counsel of the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth stand for ever sure;  
And of his heart the purposes  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from age to age endure.

<sup>12</sup> That nation blessèd is, whose God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;JEHOVAH is, and those  
A blessèd people are, whom for  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his heritage he chose.

<sup>13</sup> The LORD from heav’n sees and beholds  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all sons of men full well:  
<sup>14</sup> He views all from his dwelling-place  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that in the earth do dwell.

<sup>15</sup> He forms their hearts alike, and all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their doings he observes.  
<sup>16</sup> Great hosts save not a king, much strength  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;no mighty man preserves.

<sup>17</sup> An horse for preservätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is a deceitful thing;  
And by the greatness of his strength  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;can no deliv’rance bring.

<sup>18</sup> Behold, on those that do him fear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD doth set his eye;  
Ev’n those who on his mercy do  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with confidence rely.

<sup>19</sup> From death to free their soul, in dearth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;life unto them to yield.  
<sup>20</sup> Our soul doth wait upon the LORD;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he is our help and shield.

<sup>21</sup> Sith in his holy name we trust,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our heart shall joyful be.  
<sup>22</sup> LORD, let thy mercy be on us,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as we do hope in thee.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 34

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> GOD will I bless all times; his praise  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my mouth shall still express.  
<sup>2</sup> My soul shall boast in GOD: the meek  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall hear with joyfulness.

<sup>3</sup> Extol the LORD with me, let us  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;exalt his name together.  
<sup>4</sup> I sought the LORD, he heard, and did  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;me from all fears deliver.

<sup>5</sup> They looked to him, and lightened were:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;not shamèd were their faces.  
<sup>6</sup> This poor man cried, GOD heard, and saved  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;him from all his distresses.

<sup>7</sup> The angel of the LORD encamps,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and round encompasseth  
All those about that do him fear,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and them delivereth.

<sup>8</sup> O taste and see that GOD is good:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who trusts in him is blessed.  
<sup>9</sup> Fear GOD his saints: none that him fear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be with want oppressed.

<sup>10</sup> The lions young may hungry be,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and they may lack their food:  
But they that truly seek the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall not lack any good.

<sup>11</sup> O children, hither do ye come,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and unto me give ear;  
I shall you teach to understand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;how ye the LORD should fear.

<sup>12</sup> What man is he that life desires,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to see good would live long?  
<sup>13</sup> Thy lips refrain from speaking guile,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and from ill words thy tongue.

<sup>14</sup> Depart from ill, do good, seek peace,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;pursue it earnestly.  
<sup>15</sup> GOD’s eyes are on the just; his ears  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are open to their cry.

<sup>16</sup> The face of GOD is set against  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;those that do wickedly,  
That he may quite out from the earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cut off their memory.

<sup>17</sup> The righteous cry unto the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he unto them gives ear;  
And they out of their troubles all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by him delivered are.

<sup>18</sup> The LORD is ever nigh to them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that be of broken spirit;  
To them he safety doth afford  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that are in heart contrite.

<sup>19</sup> The troubles that afflict the just  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in number many be;  
But yet at length out of them all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD doth set him free.

<sup>20</sup> He carefully his bones doth keep,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whatever can befall;  
That not so much as one of them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;can broken be at all.

<sup>21</sup> Ill shall the wicked slay; laid waste  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be who hate the just.  
<sup>22</sup> The LORD redeems his servants’ souls;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;none perish that him trust.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 35

*A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Plead, LORD, with those that plead; and  
fight  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with those that fight with me.  
<sup>2</sup> Of shield and buckler take thou hold,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;stand up mine help to be.

<sup>3</sup> Draw also out the spear, and do  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;against them stop the way  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;That me pursue: unto my soul,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I’m thy salvation, say.

<sup>4</sup> Let them confounded be and shamed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that for my soul have sought:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Who plot my hurt turned back be they,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and to confusion brought.

<sup>5</sup> Let them be like unto the chaff  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that flies before the wind;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And let the angel of the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;pursue them hard behind.

<sup>6</sup> With darkness cover thou their way,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and let it slipp’ry prove;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And let the angel of the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;pursue them from above.

<sup>7</sup> For without cause have they for me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their net hid in a pit,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;They also have without a cause  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for my soul diggèd it.

<sup>8</sup> Let ruin seize him unawares;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his net he hid withal  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Himself let catch; and in the same  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;destruction let him fall.

<sup>9</sup> My soul in GOD shall joy; and glad  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in his salvation be:  
<sup>10</sup> And all my bones shall say, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who is like unto thee,

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Which dost the poor set free from him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that is for him too strong;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The poor and needy from the man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that spoils and does him wrong?

<sup>11</sup> False witnesses rose; to my charge  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;things I not knew they laid.  
<sup>12</sup> They, to the spoiling of my soul,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;me ill for good repaid.

<sup>13</sup> But as for me, when they were sick,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in sackcloth sad I mourned:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;My humbled soul did fast, my prayer  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;into my bosom turned.

<sup>14</sup> Myself I did behave as he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;had been my friend or brother;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I heavily bowed down, as one  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that mourneth for his mother.

<sup>15</sup> But in my trouble they rejoiced,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;gath’ring themselves together;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Yea, abjects vile together did  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;themselves against me gather:

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I knew it not; they did me tear,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and quiet would not be.  
<sup>16</sup> With mocking hypocrites, at feasts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they gnashed their teeth at me.

<sup>17</sup> How long, Lord, look’st thou on? from those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;destructions they intend  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Rescue my soul, from lions young  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my darling do defend.

<sup>18</sup> I will give thanks to thee, O Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within th’ assembly great;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And where much people gathered are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy praises forth will set.

<sup>19</sup> Let not my wrongful enemies  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;proudly rejoice o’er me;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Nor who me hate without a cause,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let them wink with the eye.

<sup>20</sup> For peace they do not speak at all;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but crafty plots prepare  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Against all those within the land  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that meek and quiet are.

<sup>21</sup> With mouths set wide, they ’gainst me said,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Ha, ha! our eye doth see.  
<sup>22</sup> LORD, thou hast seen, hold not thy peace;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Lord, be not far from me.

<sup>23</sup> Stir up thyself; wake, that thou may’st  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;judgment to me afford,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Ev’n to my cause, O thou that art  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my only God and Lord.

<sup>24</sup> O LORD my God, do thou me judge  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;after thy righteousness;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And let them not their joy ’gainst me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;triumphantly express:

<sup>25</sup> Nor let them say within their hearts,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Ah, we would have it thus;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Nor suffer them to say, that he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is swallowed up by us.

<sup>26</sup> Shamed and confounded be they all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that at my hurt are glad;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Let those against me that do boast  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with shame and scorn be clad.

<sup>27</sup> Let them that love my righteous cause  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be glad, shout, and not cease  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;To say, The LORD be magnified,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who loves his servant’s peace.

<sup>28</sup> Thy righteousness shall also be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;declarèd by my tongue;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The praises that belong to thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;speak shall it all day long.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 36

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm of David, the servant of the Lord.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> The wicked man’s transgrëssion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within my heart thus says,  
Undoubtedly the fear of God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is not before his eyes.

<sup>2</sup> Because himself he flattereth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in his own blinded eye,  
Until the hatefulness be found  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of his iniquity.

<sup>3</sup> Words from his mouth proceeding are,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;fraud and iniquity:  
He to be wise, and to do good,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hath left off utterly.

<sup>4</sup> He mischief, lying on his bed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;most cunningly doth plot:  
He sets himself in ways not good,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ill he abhorreth not.

<sup>5</sup> Thy mercy, LORD, is in the heav’ns;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy truth doth reach the clouds:  
<sup>6</sup> Thy justice is like mountains great;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy judgments deep as floods:

LORD, thou preservest man and beast.  
<sup>7</sup> How precious is thy grace!  
Therefore in shadow of thy wings  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;men’s sons their trust shall place.

<sup>8</sup> They with the fatness of thy house  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be well satisfied;  
From rivers of thy pleasures thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wilt drink to them provide.

<sup>9</sup> Because of life the fountain pure  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;remains alone with thee;  
And in that purest light of thine  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;we clearly light shall see.

<sup>10</sup> Thy loving-kindness unto them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;continue that thee know;  
And still on men upright in heart  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy righteousness bestow.

<sup>11</sup> Let not the foot of cruel pride  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;come, and against me stand;  
And let me not removèd be,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Lord, by the wicked’s hand.

<sup>12</sup> There fall’n are they, and ruinèd,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that work iniquities:  
Cast down they are, and never shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be able to arise.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 37

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> For evil doers fret thou not  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thyself unquietly;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Nor do thou envy bear to those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that work iniquity.

<sup>2</sup> For, even like unto the grass,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;soon be cut down shall they;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And, like the green and tender herb,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they wither shall away.

<sup>3</sup> Set thou thy trust upon the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and be thou doing good;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And so thou in the land shalt dwell,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and verily have food.

<sup>4</sup> Delight thyself in GOD; he’ll give  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thine heart’s desire to thee.  
<sup>5</sup> Thy way to GOD commit, him trust,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it bring to pass shall he.

<sup>6</sup> And, like unto the light, he shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy righteousness display;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And he thy judgment shall bring forth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;like noon-tide of the day.

<sup>7</sup> Rest in the LORD, and patiently  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wait for him: do not fret  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For him who, prosp’ring in his way,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;success in sin doth get.

<sup>8</sup> Do thou from anger cease, and wrath  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;see thou forsake also:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Fret not thyself in any wise,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that evil thou should’st do.

<sup>9</sup> For those that evil doers are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be cut off and fall:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;But those that wait upon the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the earth inherit shall.

<sup>10</sup> For yet a little while, and then  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the wicked shall not be;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;His place thou shalt consider well,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but it thou shalt not see.

<sup>11</sup> But by inheritance the earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the meek ones shall possess:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;They also shall delight themselves  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in an abundant peace.

<sup>12</sup> The wicked plots against the just,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and at him whets his teeth:  
<sup>13</sup> The Lord shall laugh at him, because  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his day he coming seeth.

<sup>14</sup> The wicked have drawn out the sword,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and bent their bow, to slay  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The poor and needy, and to kill  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;men of an upright way.

<sup>15</sup> But their own sword, which they have  
drawn,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall enter their own heart:  
Their bows which they have bent shall  
break,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and into pieces part.

<sup>16</sup> A little that a just man hath  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is more and better far  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Than is the wealth of many such  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as lewd and wicked are.

<sup>17</sup> For sinners’ arms shall broken be;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but GOD the just sustains.  
<sup>18</sup> GOD knows the just man’s days, and still  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their heritage remains.

<sup>19</sup> They shall not be ashamed when they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the evil time do see;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And when the days of famine are,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they satisfied shall be.

<sup>20</sup> But wicked men, and foes of GOD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as fat of lambs, decay;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;They shall consume, yea, into smoke  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they shall consume away.

<sup>21</sup> The wicked borrows, but the same  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;again he doth not pay;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Whereas the righteous mercy shows,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and gives his own away.

<sup>22</sup> For such as blessèd be of him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the earth inherit shall;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And they that cursèd are of him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be destroyèd all.

<sup>23</sup> A good man’s footsteps by the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are orderèd aright;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And in the way wherein he walks  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he greatly doth delight.

<sup>24</sup> Although he fall, yet shall he not  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be cast down utterly,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Because the LORD with his own hand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upholds him mightily.

<sup>25</sup> I have been young, and now am old,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;yet have I never seen  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The just man left, nor that his seed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for bread have beggars been.

<sup>26</sup> He’s ever merciful, and lends:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his seed is blessed therefore.  
<sup>27</sup> Depart from evil, and do good,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and dwell for evermore.

<sup>28</sup> For GOD loves judgment, and his saints  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;leaves not in any case;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;They are kept ever; but cut off  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be the sinner’s face.

<sup>29</sup> The just inherit shall the land,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and ever in it dwell:  
<sup>30</sup> The just man’s mouth doth wisdom speak;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his tongue doth judgment tell.

<sup>31</sup> In ’s heart the law is of his God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his steps slide not away.  
<sup>32</sup> The wicked man doth watch the just,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and seeketh him to slay.

<sup>33</sup> Yet him the LORD will not forsake,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor leave him in his hands:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The righteous will he not condemn,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when he in judgment stands.

<sup>34</sup> Wait on the LORD, and keep his way,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and thee exalt shall he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Th’ earth to inherit; when cut off  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the wicked thou shalt see.

<sup>35</sup> I saw the wicked great in power,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;spread like a green bay-tree:  
<sup>36</sup> He passed, yea, was not; him I sought,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but found he could not be.

<sup>37</sup> Mark thou the perfect, and behold  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the man of uprightness,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Because that surely of this man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the latter end is peace.

<sup>38</sup> But those men that transgressors are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be destroyed together;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The latter end of wicked men  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be cut off for ever.

<sup>39</sup> But the salvation of the just  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is from the LORD above;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;He in the time of their distress  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their stay and strength doth prove.

<sup>40</sup> The LORD shall help, and them deliver:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he shall them free and save  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;From wicked men, because in him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their confidence they have.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 38

*A Psalm of David, to bring to remembrance.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> In thy great indignätion,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O LORD, rebuke me not;  
Nor on me lay thy chast’ning hand,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in thy displeasure hot.

<sup>2</sup> For in me fast thine arrows stick,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thine hand doth press me sore:  
<sup>3</sup> And in my flesh there is no health,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor soundness any more.

This grief I have, because thy wrath  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is forth against me gone;  
And in my bones there is no rest,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for sin that I have done.

<sup>4</sup> Because gone up above mine head  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my great transgressions be;  
And, as a weighty burden, they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;too heavy are for me.

<sup>5</sup> My wounds do stink, and are corrupt;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my folly makes it so.  
<sup>6</sup> I troubled am, and much bowed down;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all day I mourning go.

<sup>7</sup> For a disease that loathsome is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;so fills my loins with pain,  
That in my weak and weary flesh  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;no soundness doth remain.

<sup>8</sup> So feeble and infirm am I,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and broken am so sore,  
That, through disquiet of my heart,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I have been made to roar.

<sup>9</sup> O Lord, all that I do desire  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is still before thine eye;  
And of my heart the secret groans  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;not hidden are from thee.

<sup>10</sup> My heart doth pant incessantly,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my strength doth quite decay;  
As for mine eyes, their wonted light  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is from me gone away.

<sup>11</sup> My lovers and my friends do stand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;at distance from my sore;  
And those do stand aloof that were  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;kinsmen and kind before.

<sup>12</sup> Yea, they that seek my life lay snares:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who seek to do me wrong  
Speak things mischievous, and deceits  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;imagine all day long.

<sup>13</sup> But, as one deaf, that heareth not,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I suffered all to pass;  
I as a dumb man did become,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whose mouth not opened was:

<sup>14</sup> As one that hears not, in whose mouth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are no reproofs at all.  
<sup>15</sup> For, LORD, I hope in thee; my God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou ’lt hear me when I call.

<sup>16</sup> For I said, Hear me, lest they should  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;rejoice o’er me with pride;  
And o’er me magnify themselves,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when as my foot doth slide.

<sup>17</sup> For I am near to halt, my grief  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is still before mine eye:  
<sup>18</sup> For I’ll declare my sin, and grieve  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for mine iniquity.

<sup>19</sup> But yet mine en’mies lively are,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and strong are they beside;  
And they that hate me wrongfully  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are greatly multiplied.

<sup>20</sup> And they for good that render ill,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as en’mies me withstood;  
Yea, ev’n for this, because that I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do follow what is good.

<sup>21</sup> Forsake me not, O LORD; my God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;far from me never be.  
<sup>22</sup> O Lord, thou my salvation art,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;haste to give help to me.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 39

*To the chief Musician, even to Jeduthan, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> I said, I will look to my ways,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;lest with my tongue I sin:  
In sight of wicked men my mouth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with bridle I’ll keep in.

<sup>2</sup> With silence I as dumb became,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I did myself restrain  
From speaking good; but then the more  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;increasèd was my pain.

<sup>3</sup> My heart within me waxèd hot;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and, while I musing was,  
The fire did burn; and from my tongue  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;these words I did let pass:

<sup>4</sup> Mine end, and measure of my days,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O LORD, unto me show  
What is the same; that I thereby  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my frailty well may know.

<sup>5</sup> Lo, thou my days an handbreadth mad’st;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mine age is in thine eye  
As nothing: sure each man at best  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is wholly vanity.

<sup>6</sup> Sure each man walks in a vain show;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they vex themselves in vain:  
He heaps up wealth, and doth not know  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to whom it shall pertain.

<sup>7</sup> And now, O Lord, what wait I for?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my hope is fixed on thee.  
<sup>8</sup> Free me from all my trespasses,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the fool’s scorn make not me.

<sup>9</sup> Dumb was I, op’ning not my mouth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;because this work was thine.  
<sup>10</sup> Thy stroke take from me; by the blow  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of thine hand I do pine.

<sup>11</sup> When with rebukes thou dost correct  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;man for iniquity,  
Thou wastes his beauty like a moth:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sure each man’s vanity.

<sup>12</sup> Attend my cry, LORD, at my tears  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and pray’rs not silent be:  
I sojourn as my fathers all,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and stranger am with thee.

<sup>13</sup> O spare thou me, that I my strength  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;recover may again,  
Before from hence I do depart,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and here no more remain.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 40

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> I waited for the LORD my God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and patiently did bear;  
At length to me he did incline  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my voice and cry to hear.

<sup>2</sup> He took me from a fearful pit,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and from the miry clay,  
And on a rock he set my feet,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;establishing my way.

<sup>3</sup> He put a new song in my mouth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our God to magnify:  
Many shall see it, and shall fear,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and on the LORD rely.

<sup>4</sup> O blessèd is the man whose trust  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon the LORD relies;  
Respecting not the proud, nor such  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as turn aside to lies.

<sup>5</sup> O LORD my God, full many are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the wonders thou hast done;  
Thy gracious thoughts to us-ward far  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;above all thoughts are gone:

In order none can reckon them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to thee: if them declare,  
And speak of them I would, they more  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;than can be numbered are.

<sup>6</sup> No sacrifice nor offering  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;didst thou at all desire;  
Mine ears thou bored: sin-off’ring thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and burnt didst not require:

<sup>7</sup> Then to the Lord these were my words,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I come, behold and see;  
Within the volume of the book  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it written is of me:

<sup>8</sup> To do thy will I take delight,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O thou my God that art;  
Yea, that most holy law of thine  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I have within my heart.

<sup>9</sup> Within the congregation great  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I righteousness did preach:  
Lo, thou dost know, O LORD, that I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;refrainèd not my speech.

<sup>10</sup> I never did within my heart  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;conceal thy righteousness;  
I thy salvation have declared,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and shown thy faithfulness:

Thy kindness, which most loving is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;concealèd have not I,  
Nor from the congregation great  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;have hid thy verity.

<sup>11</sup> Thy tender mercies, LORD, from me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O do thou not restrain;  
Thy loving-kindness, and thy truth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let them me still maintain.

<sup>12</sup> For ills past reck’ning compass me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and mine iniquities  
Such hold upon me taken have,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I cannot lift mine eyes:

They more than hairs are on mine head,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thence is my heart dismayed.  
<sup>13</sup> Be pleasèd, LORD, to rescue me;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;LORD, hasten to mine aid.

<sup>14</sup> Shamed and confounded be they all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that seek my soul to kill;  
Yea, let them backward driven be,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and shamed, that wish me ill.

<sup>15</sup> For a reward of this their shame  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;confounded let them be,  
That in this manner scoffing say,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Aha, aha! to me.

<sup>16</sup> In thee let all be glad, and joy,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who seeking thee abide;  
Who thy salvation love, say still,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The LORD be magnified.

<sup>17</sup> I’m poor and needy, yet the Lord  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of me a care doth take:  
Thou art my help and säviour,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my God, no tarrying make.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 41

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Blessèd is he that wisely doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the poor man’s case consider;  
For when the time of trouble is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD will him deliver.

<sup>2</sup> GOD will him keep, yea, save alive;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on earth he blessed shall live;  
And to his enemies’ desire  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou wilt him not up give.

<sup>3</sup> GOD will give strength when he on bed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of languishing doth mourn;  
And in his sickness sore, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou all his bed wilt turn.

<sup>4</sup> I said, O LORD, do thou extend  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy mercy unto me;  
O do thou heal my soul; for why?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I have offended thee.

<sup>5</sup> Those that to me are enemies,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of me do evil say,  
When shall he die, that so his name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;may perish quite away?

<sup>6</sup> To see me if he comes, he speaks  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;vain words: but then his heart  
Heaps mischief to it, which he tells,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when forth he doth depart.

<sup>7</sup> My haters jointly whispering,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;’gainst me my hurt devise.  
<sup>8</sup> Mischief, say they, cleaves fast to him;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he lieth, and shall not rise.

<sup>9</sup> Yea, ev’n mine own familiar friend,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on whom I did rely,  
Who ate my bread, ev’n he his heel  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;against me lifted high.

<sup>10</sup> But, LORD, be merciful to me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and up again me raise,  
That I may justly them requite  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;according to their ways.

<sup>11</sup> By this I know that certainly  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I favoured am by thee;  
Because my hateful enemy  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;triumphs not over me.

<sup>12</sup> But as for me, thou me uphold’st  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in mine integrity;  
And me before thy countenance  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou sett’st continually.

<sup>13</sup> The LORD, the God of Israel,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be blessed for ever then,  
From age to age eternally.  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Amen, yea, and amen.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

# Book II

*Psalms 42&ndash;72*

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 42

*To the chief Musician, Maschil, for the sons of Korah.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Like as the hart for water-brooks  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in thirst doth pant and bray;  
So pants my longing soul, O God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that come to thee I may.

<sup>2</sup> My soul for God, the living God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth thirst: when shall I near  
Unto thy countenance approach,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and in God’s sight appear?

<sup>3</sup> My tears have unto me been meat,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;both in the night and day,  
While unto me continually,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Where is thy God? they say.

<sup>4</sup> My soul is pourèd out in me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when this I think upon;  
Because that with the multitude  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I heretofore had gone:

With them into God’s house I went,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with voice of joy and praise;  
Yea, with the multitude that kept  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the solemn holy days.

<sup>5</sup> O why art thou cast down, my soul?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;why in me so dismayed?  
Trust God, for I shall praise him yet,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his count’nance is mine aid.

<sup>6</sup> My God, my soul’s cast down in me;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thee therefore mind I will  
From Jordan’s land, the Hermonites,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and ev’n from Mizar hill.

<sup>7</sup> At the noise of thy water-spouts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;deep unto deep doth call;  
Thy breaking waves pass over me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;yea, and thy billows all.

<sup>8</sup> His loving-kindness yet the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;command will in the day,  
His song’s with me by night; to God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by whom I live, I’ll pray:

<sup>9</sup> And I will say to God my rock,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Why me forgett’st thou so?  
Why, for my foes’ opprëssion,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thus mourning do I go?

<sup>10</sup> ’Tis as a sword within my bones,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when my foes me upbraid;  
Ev’n when by them, Where is thy God?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;’tis daily to me said.

<sup>11</sup> O why art thou cast down, my soul?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;why, thus with grief oppressed,  
Art thou disquieted in me?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in God still hope and rest:

For yet I know I shall him praise,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who graciously to me  
The health is of my countenance,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;yea, mine own God is he.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 43

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Judge me, O God, and plead my cause  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;against th’ ungodly nation;  
From the unjust and crafty man,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O be thou my salvation.

<sup>2</sup> For thou the God art of my strength;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;why thrusts thou me thee fro’?  
For th’ enemy’s opprëssion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;why do I mourning go?

<sup>3</sup> O send thy light forth and thy truth;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let them be guides to me,  
And bring me to thine holy hill,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n where thy dwellings be.

<sup>4</sup> Then will I to God’s altar go,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to God my chiefest joy:  
Yea, God, my God, thy name to praise  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my harp I will employ.

<sup>5</sup> Why art thou then cast down, my soul?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;what should discourage thee?  
And why with vexing thoughts art thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;disquieted in me?

Still trust in God; for him to praise  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;good cause I yet shall have:  
He of my count’nance is the health,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my God that doth me save.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 44

*To the chief Musician for the sons of Korah, Maschil.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O God, we with our ears have heard,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our fathers have us told,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;What works thou in their days hadst done,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n in the days of old.

<sup>2</sup> Thy hand did drive the heathen out,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and plant them in their place;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Thou didst afflict the nätions,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but them thou didst increase.

<sup>3</sup> For neither got their sword the land,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor did their arm them save;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;But thy right hand, arm, countenance;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for thou them favour gave.

<sup>4</sup> Thou art my King: for Jacob, Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;deliv’rances command.  
<sup>5</sup> Through thee we shall push down our foes,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that do against us stand:

We, through thy name, shall tread down  
those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that ris’n against us have.  
<sup>6</sup> For in my bow I shall not trust,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor shall my sword me save.

<sup>7</sup> But from our foes thou hast us saved,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our haters put to shame.  
<sup>8</sup> In God we all the day do boast,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and ever praise thy name.

<sup>9</sup> But now we are cast off by thee,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and us thou putt’st to shame;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And when our armies do go forth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou goest not with the same.

<sup>10</sup> Thou mak’st us from the enemy,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;faint-hearted, to turn back;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And they who hate us for themselves  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our spoils away do take.

<sup>11</sup> Like sheep for meat thou gavest us;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;’mong heathen cast we be.  
<sup>12</sup> Thou didst for nought thy people sell;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their price enriched not thee.

<sup>13</sup> Thou mak’st us a reproach to be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto our neighbours near;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Derision and a scorn to them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that round about us are.

<sup>14</sup> A by-word also thou dost us  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;among the heathen make;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The people, in contempt and spite,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;at us their heads do shake.

<sup>15</sup> Before me my confüsion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;continually abides;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And of my bashful countenance  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the shame me ever hides:

<sup>16</sup> For voice of him that doth reproach,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and speaketh blasphemy;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;By reason of th’ avenging foe,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and cruel enemy.

<sup>17</sup> All this is come on us, yet we  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;have not forgotten thee;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Nor falsely in thy covenant  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;behaved ourselves have we.

<sup>18</sup> Back from thy way our heart not turned;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our steps no straying made;  
<sup>19</sup> Though us thou brak’st in dragons’ place,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and cover’dst with death’s shade.

<sup>20</sup> If we God’s name forgot, or stretched  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to a strange god our hands,  
<sup>21</sup> Shall not God search this out? for he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;heart’s secrets understands.

<sup>22</sup> Yea, for thy sake we’re killed all day,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;counted as slaughter-sheep.  
<sup>23</sup> Rise, Lord, cast us not ever off;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;awake, why dost thou sleep?

<sup>24</sup> O wherefore hidest thou thy face?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;forgett’st our cause distressed,  
<sup>25</sup> And our oppression? For our soul  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is to the dust down pressed:

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Our belly also on the earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;fast cleaving, hold doth take.  
<sup>26</sup> Rise for our help, and us redeem,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n for thy mercies’ sake.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 45

*To the chief Musician upon Shoshannim, for the sons of Korah, Maschil, A Song of loves.*

### Version 1

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> My heart brings forth a goodly thing;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my words that I indite  
Concern the King: my tongue’s a pen  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of one that swift doth write.

<sup>2</sup> Thou fairer art than sons of men:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;into thy lips is store  
Of grace infused; God therefore thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hath blessed for evermore.

<sup>3</sup> O thou that art the mighty One,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy sword gird on thy thigh;  
Ev’n with thy glory excellent,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and with thy majesty.

<sup>4</sup> For meekness, truth, and righteousness,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in state ride prosp’rously;  
And thy right hand shall thee instruct  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in things that fearful be.

<sup>5</sup> Thine arrows sharply pierce the heart  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of th’ en’mies of the King;  
And under thy subjëction  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the people down do bring.

<sup>6</sup> For ever and for ever is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O God, thy throne of might;  
The sceptre of thy kingdom is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a sceptre that is right.

<sup>7</sup> Thou lovest right, and hatest ill;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for God, thy God, most high,  
Above thy fellows hath with th’ oil  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of joy anointed thee.

<sup>8</sup> Of aloes, myrrh, and cassia,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a smell thy garments had,  
Out of the iv’ry palaces,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whereby they made thee glad.

<sup>9</sup> Among thy women hon’rable  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;kings’ daughters were at hand:  
Upon thy right hand did the queen  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in gold of Ophir stand.

<sup>10</sup> O daughter, hearken and regard,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and do thine ear incline;  
Likewise forget thy father’s house,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and people that are thine.

<sup>11</sup> Then of the King desired shall be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy beauty veh’mently:  
Because he is thy Lord, do thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;him worship rev’rently.

<sup>12</sup> The daughter there of Tyre shall be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with gifts and off’rings great:  
Those of the people that are rich  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy favour shall entreat.

<sup>13</sup> Behold, the daughter of the King  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all glorious is within;  
And with embroideries of gold  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;her garments wrought have been.

<sup>14</sup> She shall be brought unto the King  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in robes with needle wrought;  
Her fellow-virgins following  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall unto thee be brought.

<sup>15</sup> They shall be brought with gladness great,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and mirth on ev’ry side,  
Into the palace of the King,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and there they shall abide.

<sup>16</sup> Instead of those thy fathers dear,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy children thou may’st take,  
And in all places of the earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;them noble princes make.

<sup>17</sup> Thy name remembered I will make  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;through ages all to be:  
The people therefore evermore  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall praises give to thee.

---

### Version 2

*S.M.*

<sup>1</sup> My heart inditing is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;good matter in a song:  
I speak the things that I have made,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which to the King belong:

My tongue shall be as quick,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his honour to indite,  
As is the pen of any scribe  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that useth fast to write.

<sup>2</sup> Thou ’rt fairest of all men;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;grace in thy lips doth flow:  
And therefore blessings evermore  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on thee doth God bestow.

<sup>3</sup> Thy sword gird on thy thigh,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou that art most of might:  
Appear in dreadful majesty,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and in thy glory bright.

<sup>4</sup> For meekness, truth, and right,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ride prosp’rously in state;  
And thy right hand shall teach to thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;things terrible and great.

<sup>5</sup> Thy shafts shall pierce their hearts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that foes are to the King;  
Whereby into subjëction  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the people thou shalt bring.

<sup>6</sup> Thy royal seat, O Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for ever shall remain:  
The sceptre of thy kingdom doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all righteousness maintain.

<sup>7</sup> Thou lov’st right, and hat’st ill;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for God, thy God, most high,  
Above thy fellows hath with th’ oil  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of joy anointed thee.

<sup>8</sup> Of myrrh and spices sweet  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a smell thy garments had,  
Out of the iv’ry palaces,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whereby they made thee glad.

<sup>9</sup> And in thy glorious train  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;kings’ daughters waiting stand;  
And thy fair queen, in Ophir gold,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth stand at thy right hand.

<sup>10</sup> O daughter, take good heed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;incline, and give good ear;  
Thou must forget thy kindred all,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and father’s house most dear.

<sup>11</sup> Thy beauty to the King  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall then delightful be:  
And do thou humbly worship him,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;because thy Lord is he.

<sup>12</sup> The daughter then of Tyre  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;there with a gift shall be,  
And all the wealthy of the land  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall make their suit to thee.

<sup>13</sup> The daughter of the King  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all glorious is within;  
And with embroideries of gold  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;her garments wrought have been.

<sup>14</sup> She cometh to the King  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in robes with needle wrought;  
The virgins that do follow her  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall unto thee be brought.

<sup>15</sup> They shall be brought with joy,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and mirth on ev’ry side,  
Into the palace of the King,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and there they shall abide.

<sup>16</sup> And in thy fathers’ stead,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy children thou may’st take,  
And in all places of the earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;them noble princes make.

<sup>17</sup> I will show forth thy name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to generations all:  
Therefore the people evermore  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to thee give praises shall.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 46

*To the chief Musician, for the sons of Korah, A Song upon Alomoth.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> God is our refuge and our strength,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in straits a present aid;  
<sup>2</sup> Therefore, although the earth remove,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;we will not be afraid:

Though hills amidst the seas be cast;  
<sup>3</sup> Though waters roaring make,  
And troubled be; yea, though the hills  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by swelling seas do shake.

<sup>4</sup> A river is, whose streams do glad  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the city of our God;  
The holy place, wherein the Lord  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;most high hath his abode.

<sup>5</sup> God in the midst of her doth dwell;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nothing shall her remove:  
The Lord to her an helper will,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and that right early, prove.

<sup>6</sup> The heathen raged tumultuously,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the kingdoms movèd were:  
The Lord God utterèd his voice,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the earth did melt for fear.

<sup>7</sup> The LORD of hosts upon our side  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth constantly remain:  
The God of Jacob’s our refuge,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;us safely to maintain.

<sup>8</sup> Come, and behold what wondrous works  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;have by the LORD been wrought;  
Come, see what desolätions  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he on the earth hath brought.

<sup>9</sup> Unto the ends of all the earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wars into peace he turns:  
The bow he breaks, the spear he cuts,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in fire the chariot burns.

<sup>10</sup> Be still, and know that I am God;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;among the heathen I  
Will be exalted; I on earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;will be exalted high.

<sup>11</sup> Our God, who is the LORD of hosts,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is still upon our side;  
The God of Jacob our refuge  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for ever will abide.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 47

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm for the sons of Korah.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> All people, clap your hands; to God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with voice of triumph shout:  
<sup>2</sup> For dreadful is the LORD most high,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;great King the earth throughout.

<sup>3</sup> The heathen people under us  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he surely shall subdue;  
And he shall make the nätions  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;under our feet to bow.

<sup>4</sup> The lot of our inheritance  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;choose out for us shall he,  
Of Jacob, whom he lovèd well,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n the excellency.

<sup>5</sup> God is with shouts gone up, the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with trumpets sounding high.  
<sup>6</sup> Sing praise to God, sing praise, sing praise,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;praise to our King sing ye.

<sup>7</sup> For God is King of all the earth;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with knowledge praise express.  
<sup>8</sup> God rules the nations: God sits on  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his throne of holiness.

<sup>9</sup> The princes of the people are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;assembled willingly;  
Ev’n of the God of Abraham  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they who the people be.

For why? the shields that do defend  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the earth are only his:  
They to the Lord belong; yea, he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;exalted greatly is.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 48

*A Song and Psalm for the sons of Korah.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Great is the LORD, and greatly he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is to be praisèd still,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Within the city of our God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon his holy hill.

<sup>2</sup> Mount Zion stands most beautiful,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the joy of all the land;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The city of the mighty King  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on her north side doth stand.

<sup>3</sup> The Lord within her palaces  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is for a refuge known.  
<sup>4</sup> For, lo, the kings that gathered were  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;together, by have gone.

<sup>5</sup> But when they did behold the same,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they, wond’ring, would not stay;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;But, being troubled at the sight,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they thence did haste away.

<sup>6</sup> Great terror there took hold on them;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they were possessed with fear;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Their grief came like a woman’s pain,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when she a child doth bear.

<sup>7</sup> Thou Tarshish ships with east wind  
break’st:  
<sup>8</sup> As we have heard it told,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;So, in the city of the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our eyes did it behold;

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In our God’s city, which his hand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for ever stablish will.  
<sup>9</sup> We of thy loving-kindness thought,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Lord, in thy temple still.

<sup>10</sup> O Lord, according to thy name,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;through all the earth’s thy praise;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And thy right hand, O Lord, is full  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of righteousness always.

<sup>11</sup> Because thy judgments are made known,
