&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let Zion mount rejoice;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Of Judah let the daughters all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;send forth a cheerful voice.

<sup>12</sup> Walk about Zion, and go round;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the high tow’rs thereof tell:  
<sup>13</sup> Consider ye her palaces,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and mark her bulwarks well;

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;That ye may tell posterity.  
<sup>14</sup> For this God doth abide  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Our God for evermore; he will  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n unto death us guide.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 49

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm for the sons of Korah.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Hear this, all people, and give ear,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all in the world that dwell;  
<sup>2</sup> Both low and high, both rich and poor.  
<sup>3</sup> My mouth shall wisdom tell;

My heart shall knowledge meditate.  
<sup>4</sup> I will incline mine ear  
To parables, and on the harp  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my sayings dark declare.

<sup>5</sup> Amidst those days that evil be,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;why should I, fearing, doubt?  
When of my heels th’ iniquity  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall compass me about.

<sup>6</sup> Whoe’er they be that in their wealth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their confidence do pitch,  
And boast themselves, because they are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;become exceeding rich:

<sup>7</sup> Yet none of these his brother can  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;redeem by any way;  
Nor can he unto God for him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sufficient ransom pay,

<sup>8</sup> (Their soul’s redemption precious is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and it can never be,)  
<sup>9</sup> That still he should for ever live,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and not corruption see.

<sup>10</sup> For why? he seeth that wise men die,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and brutish fools also  
Do perish; and their wealth, when dead,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to others they let go.

<sup>11</sup> Their inward thought is, that their house  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and dwelling-places shall  
Stand through all ages; they their lands  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by their own names do call.

<sup>12</sup> But yet in honour shall not man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;abide continually;  
But passing hence, may be compared  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto the beasts that die.

<sup>13</sup> Thus brutish folly plainly is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their wisdom and their way;  
Yet their posterity approve  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;what they do fondly say.

<sup>14</sup> Like sheep they in the grave are laid,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and death shall them devour;  
And in the morning upright men  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall over them have power:

Their beauty from their dwelling shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;consume within the grave.  
<sup>15</sup> But from hell’s hand God will me free,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for he shall me receive.

<sup>16</sup> Be thou not then afraid when one  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;enrichèd thou dost see,  
Nor when the glory of his house  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;advancèd is on high:

<sup>17</sup> For he shall carry nothing hence  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when death his days doth end;  
Nor shall his glory after him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;into the grave descend.

<sup>18</sup> Although he his own soul did bless  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whilst he on earth did live;  
(And when thou to thyself dost well,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;men will thee praises give;)

<sup>19</sup> He to his fathers’ race shall go,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they never shall see light.  
<sup>20</sup> Man honoured wanting knowledge is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;like beasts that perish quite.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 50

*A Psalm of Asaph.*

### Version 1

*S.M.*

<sup>1</sup> The mighty God, the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hath spoken, and did call  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The earth, from rising of the sun,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to where he hath his fall.

<sup>2</sup> From out of Zion hill,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which of excellency  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And beauty the perfection is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;God shinèd gloriously.

<sup>3</sup> Our God shall surely come;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;keep silence shall not he:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Before him fire shall waste, great storms  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall round about him be.

<sup>4</sup> Unto the heavens clear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he from above shall call,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And to the earth likewise, that he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;may judge his people all.

<sup>5</sup> Together let my saints  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto me gathered be,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Those that by sacrifice have made  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a covenant with me.

<sup>6</sup> And then the heavens shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his righteousness declare:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Because the Lord himself is he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by whom men judgèd are.

<sup>7</sup> My people Isr’el hear,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;speak will I from on high,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Against thee I will testify;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;God, ev’n thy God, am I.

<sup>8</sup> I for thy sacrifice  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;no blame will on thee lay,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Nor for burnt-off’rings, which to me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou offer’dst ev’ry day.

<sup>9</sup> I’ll take no calf nor goats  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from house or fold of thine:  
<sup>10</sup> For beasts of forest, cattle all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on thousand hills, are mine.

<sup>11</sup> The fowls on mountains high  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are all to me well known;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Wild beasts which in the fields do lie,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n they are all mine own.

<sup>12</sup> Then, if I hungry were,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I would not tell it thee;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Because the world, and fulness all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thereof, belongs to me.

<sup>13</sup> Will I eat flesh of bulls?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;or goats’ blood drink will I?  
<sup>14</sup> Thanks offer thou to God, and pay  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy vows to the Most High.

<sup>15</sup> And call upon me when  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in trouble thou shalt be;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I will deliver thee, and thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my name shalt glorify.

<sup>16</sup> But to the wicked man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;God saith, My laws and truth  
Should’st thou declare? how dar’st thou take  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my cov’nant in thy mouth?

<sup>17</sup> Sith thou instruction hat’st,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which should thy ways direct;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And sith my words behind thy back  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou cast’st, and dost reject.

<sup>18</sup> When thou a thief didst see,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with him thou didst consent;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And with the vile adulterers  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;partaker on thou went.

<sup>19</sup> Thou giv’st thy mouth to ill,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy tongue deceit doth frame;  
<sup>20</sup> Thou sitt’st, and ’gainst thy brother speak’st,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy mother’s son dost shame.

<sup>21</sup> Because I silence kept,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;while thou these things hast wrought;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;That I was altogether like  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thyself, hath been thy thought;

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Yet I will thee reprove,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and set before thine eyes,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In order rankèd, thy misdeeds  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and thine iniquities.

<sup>22</sup> Now, ye that God forget,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;this carefully consider;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Lest I in pieces tear you all,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and none can you deliver.

<sup>23</sup> Whoso doth offer praise  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;me glorifies; and I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Will show him God’s salvätion,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that orders right his way.

---

### Version 2

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> The mighty God, the LORD, hath spoke,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and called the earth upon,  
Ev’n from the rising of the sun  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto his going down.

<sup>2</sup> From out of Zion, his own hill,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;where the perfection high  
Of beauty is, from thence the Lord  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hath shinèd gloriously.

<sup>3</sup> Our God shall come, and shall no more  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be silent, but speak out:  
Before him fire shall waste, great storms  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall compass him about.

<sup>4</sup> He to the heavens from above,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and to the earth below,  
Shall call, that he his judgments may  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before his people show.

<sup>5</sup> Let all my saints together be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto me gatherèd;  
Those that by sacrifice with me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a covenant have made.

<sup>6</sup> And then the heavens shall declare  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his righteousness abroad:  
Because the Lord himself doth come;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;none else is judge but God.

<sup>7</sup> Hear, O my people, and I’ll speak;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O Israèl by name,  
Against thee I will testify;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;God, ev’n thy God, I am.

<sup>8</sup> I for thy sacrifices few  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;reprove thee never will,  
Nor for burnt-off’rings to have been  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before me offered still.

<sup>9</sup> I’ll take no bullock nor he-goats  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from house nor folds of thine:  
<sup>10</sup> For beasts of forest, cattle all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on thousand hills, are mine.

<sup>11</sup> The fowls are all to me well known  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that mountains high do yield;  
And I do challenge as mine own  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the wild beasts of the field.

<sup>12</sup> If I were hungry, I would not  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to thee for need complain;  
For earth, and all its fulness, doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to me of right pertain.

<sup>13</sup> That I to eat the flesh of bulls  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;take pleasure dost thou think?  
Or that I need, to quench my thirst,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the blood of goats to drink?

<sup>14</sup> Nay, rather unto me, thy God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thanksgiving offer thou:  
To the Most High perform thy word,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and fully pay thy vow:

<sup>15</sup> And in the day of trouble great  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;see that thou call on me;  
I will deliver thee, and thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my name shalt glorify.

<sup>16</sup> But God unto the wicked saith,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Why should’st thou mention make  
Of my commands? how dar’st thou in  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy mouth my cov’nant take?

<sup>17</sup> Sith it is so that thou dost hate  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all good instrüction;  
And sith thou cast’st behind thy back,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and slight’st my words each one.

<sup>18</sup> When thou a thief didst see, then straight  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou join’dst with him in sin,  
And with the vile adulterers  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou hast partaker been.

<sup>19</sup> Thy mouth to evil thou dost give,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy tongue deceit doth frame.  
<sup>20</sup> Thou sitt’st, and ’gainst thy brother speak’st,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy mother’s son to shame.

<sup>21</sup> These things thou wickedly hast done,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and I have silent been:  
Thou thought’st that I was like thyself,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and did approve thy sin:

But I will sharply thee reprove,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and I will order right  
Thy sins and thy transgrëssions  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in presence of thy sight.

<sup>22</sup> Consider this, and be afraid,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ye that forget the Lord,  
Lest I in pieces tear you all,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when none can help afford.

<sup>23</sup> Who off’reth praise me glorifies:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I will show God’s salvation  
To him that ordereth aright  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his life and conversation.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 51

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm of David, when Nathan the prophet came unto him, after he had gone into Bathsheba.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> After thy loving-kindness, Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;have mercy upon me:  
For thy compassions great, blot out  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all mine iniquity.

<sup>2</sup> Me cleanse from sin, and throughly wash  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from mine iniquity:  
<sup>3</sup> For my transgressions I confess;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my sin I ever see.

<sup>4</sup> ’Gainst thee, thee only, have I sinned,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in thy sight done this ill;  
That when thou speak’st thou may’st be just,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and clear in judging still.

<sup>5</sup> Behold, I in iniquity  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;was formed the womb within;  
My mother also me conceived  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in guiltiness and sin.

<sup>6</sup> Behold, thou in the inward parts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with truth delighted art;  
And wisdom thou shalt make me know  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within the hidden part.

<sup>7</sup> Do thou with hyssop sprinkle me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I shall be cleansèd so;  
Yea, wash thou me, and then I shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be whiter than the snow.

<sup>8</sup> Of gladness and of joyfulness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;make me to hear the voice;  
That so these very bones which thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hast broken may rejoice.

<sup>9</sup> All mine iniquities blot out,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy face hide from my sin.  
<sup>10</sup> Create a clean heart, Lord, renew  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a right spirit me within.

<sup>11</sup> Cast me not from thy sight, nor take  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy Holy Spirit away.  
<sup>12</sup> Restore me thy salvation’s joy;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with thy free Spirit me stay.

<sup>13</sup> Then will I teach thy ways unto  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;those that transgressors be;  
And those that sinners are shall then  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be turnèd unto thee.

<sup>14</sup> O God, of my salvation God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;me from blood-guiltiness  
Set free; then shall my tongue aloud  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sing of thy righteousness.

<sup>15</sup> My closèd lips, O Lord, by thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let them be openèd;  
Then shall thy praises by my mouth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;abroad be publishèd.

<sup>16</sup> For thou desir’st not sacrifice,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;else would I give it thee;  
Nor wilt thou with burnt-offering  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;at all delighted be.

<sup>17</sup> A broken spirit is to God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a pleasing sacrifice:  
A broken and a contrite heart,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Lord, thou wilt not despise.

<sup>18</sup> Show kindness, and do good, O Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to Zion, thine own hill:  
The walls of thy Jerusalem  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;build up of thy good will.

<sup>19</sup> Then righteous off’rings shall thee please,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and off’rings burnt, which they  
With whole burnt-off’rings, and with calves,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall on thine altar lay.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 52

*To the chief Musician, Maschil, A Psalm of David, when Doeg the Edomite came and told Saul, and said unto him, David is come to the house of Ahimelech.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Why dost thou boast, O mighty man,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of mischief and of ill?  
The goodness of Almighty God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;endureth ever still.

<sup>2</sup> Thy tongue mischievous calumnies  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;deviseth subtilely,  
Like to a razor sharp to cut,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;working deceitfully.

<sup>3</sup> Ill more than good, and more than truth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou lovest to speak wrong:  
<sup>4</sup> Thou lovest all-devouring words,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O thou deceitful tongue.

<sup>5</sup> So God shall thee destroy for aye,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;remove thee, pluck thee out  
Quite from thy house, out of the land  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of life he shall thee root.

<sup>6</sup> The righteous shall it see, and fear,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and laugh at him they shall:  
<sup>7</sup> Lo, this the man is that did not  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;make God his strength at all:

But he in his abundant wealth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his confidence did place;  
And he took strength unto himself  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from his own wickedness.

<sup>8</sup> But I am in the house of God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;like to an olive green:  
My confidence for ever hath  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon God’s mercy been.

<sup>9</sup> And I for ever will thee praise,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;because thou hast done this:  
I on thy name will wait; for good  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before thy saints it is.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 53

*To the chief Musician upon Mahalath, Maschil, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> That there is not a God, the fool  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth in his heart conclude:  
They are corrupt, their works are vile,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;not one of them doth good.

<sup>2</sup> The Lord upon the sons of men  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from heav’n did cast his eyes,  
To see if any one there was  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that sought God, and was wise.

<sup>3</sup> They altogether filthy are,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they all are backward gone;  
And there is none that doeth good,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;no, not so much as one.

<sup>4</sup> These workers of iniquity,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do they not know at all,  
That they my people eat as bread,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and on God do not call?

<sup>5</sup> Ev’n there they were afraid, and stood  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with trembling, all dismayed,  
Whereas there was no cause at all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;why they should be afraid:

For God his bones that thee besieged  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hath scattered all abroad;  
Thou hast confounded them, for they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;despisèd are of God.

<sup>6</sup> Let Isr’el’s help from Zion come:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when back the Lord shall bring  
His captives, Jacob shall rejoice,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and Israèl shall sing.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 54

*To the chief Musician on Neginoth, Maschil, A Psalm of David, when the Ziphims came and said to Saul, Doth not David hide himself with us?*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Save me, O God, by thy great name,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and judge me by thy strength:  
<sup>2</sup> My prayer hear, O God; give ear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto my words at length.

<sup>3</sup> For they that strangers are to me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do up against me rise;  
Oppressors seek my soul, and God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;set not before their eyes.

<sup>4</sup> The Lord my God my helper is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;lo, therefore I am bold:  
He taketh part with everyone  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that doth my soul uphold.

<sup>5</sup> Unto mine enemies he shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mischief and ill repay:  
O for thy truth’s sake cut them off,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and sweep them clean away.

<sup>6</sup> I will a sacrifice to thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;give with free willingness;  
Thy name, O LORD, because ’tis good,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with praise I will confess.

<sup>7</sup> For he hath me delivered  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from all adversities;  
And his desire mine eye hath seen  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon mine enemies.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 55

*To the chief Musician on Neginoth, Maschil, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Lord, hear my pray’r, hide not thyself  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from my entreating voice:  
<sup>2</sup> Attend and hear me; in my plaint  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I mourn and make a noise.

<sup>3</sup> Because of th’ en’my’s voice, and for  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;lewd men’s oppression great:  
On me they cast iniquity,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and they in wrath me hate.

<sup>4</sup> Sore pained within me is my heart:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;death’s terrors on me fall.  
<sup>5</sup> On me comes trembling, fear and dread  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;o’erwhelmèd me withal.

<sup>6</sup> O that I, like a dove, had wings,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;said I, then would I flee  
Far hence, that I might find a place  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;where I in rest might be.

<sup>7</sup> Lo, then far off I wander would,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and in the desert stay;  
<sup>8</sup> From windy storm and tempest I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;would haste to ’scape away.

<sup>9</sup> O Lord, on them destruction bring,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and do their tongues divide;  
For in the city violence  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and strife I have espied.

<sup>10</sup> They day and night upon the walls  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do go about it round:  
There mischief is, and sorrow there  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in midst of it is found.

<sup>11</sup> Abundant wickedness there is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within her inward part;  
And from her streets deceitfulness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and guile do not depart.

<sup>12</sup> He was no foe that me reproached,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;then that endure I could;  
Nor hater that did ’gainst me boast,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from him me hide I would.

<sup>13</sup> But thou, man, who mine equal, guide,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and mine acquaintance wast:  
<sup>14</sup> We joined sweet counsels, to God’s house  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in company we passed.

<sup>15</sup> Let death upon them seize, and down  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let them go quick to hell;  
For wickedness doth much abound  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;among them where they dwell.

<sup>16</sup> I’ll call on God: GOD will me save.  
<sup>17</sup> I’ll pray, and make a noise  
At ev’ning, morning, and at noon;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and he shall hear my voice.

<sup>18</sup> He hath my soul deliverèd,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that it in peace might be  
From battle that against me was;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for many were with me.

<sup>19</sup> The Lord shall hear, and them afflict,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of old who hath abode:  
Because they never changes have,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;therefore they fear not God.

<sup>20</sup> ’Gainst those that were at peace with him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he hath put forth his hand:  
The covènant that he had made,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by breaking he profaned.

<sup>21</sup> More smooth than butter were his words,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;while in his heart was war;  
His speeches were more soft than oil,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and yet drawn swords they are.

<sup>22</sup> Cast thou thy burden on the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and he shall thee sustain;  
Yea, he shall cause the righteous man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unmovèd to remain.

<sup>23</sup> But thou, O Lord my God, those men  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in justice shalt o’erthrow,  
And in destruction’s dungeon dark  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;at last shalt lay them low:

The bloody and deceitful men  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall not live half their days:  
But upon thee with confidence  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I will depend always.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 56

*To the chief Musician upon Jonath-elem-rechokim, Michtam of David, when the Philistines took him in Gath.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Show mercy, Lord, to me, for man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;would swallow me outright;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;He me oppresseth, while he doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;against me daily fight.

<sup>2</sup> They daily would me swallow up  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that hate me spitefully;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For they be many that do fight  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;against me, O Most High.

<sup>3</sup> When I’m afraid I’ll trust in thee:  
<sup>4</sup> In God I’ll praise his word;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I will not fear what flesh can do,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my trust is in the Lord.

<sup>5</sup> Each day they wrest my words; their  
thoughts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;’gainst me are all for ill.  
<sup>6</sup> They meet, they lurk, they mark my steps,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;waiting my soul to kill.

<sup>7</sup> But shall they by iniquity  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;escape thy judgments so?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O God, with indignation down  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do thou the people throw.

<sup>8</sup> My wand’rings all what they have been  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou know’st, their number took;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Into thy bottle put my tears:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are they not in thy book?

<sup>9</sup> My foes shall, when I cry, turn back;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I know ’t, God is for me.  
<sup>10</sup> In God his word I’ll praise; his word  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in GOD shall praisèd be.

<sup>11</sup> In God I trust; I will not fear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;what man can do to me.  
<sup>12</sup> Thy vows upon me are, O God:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I’ll render praise to thee.

<sup>13</sup> Wilt thou not, who from death me saved,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my feet from falls keep free,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;To walk before God in the light  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of those that living be?

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 57

*To the chief Musician, Al-taschith, Michtam of David, when he fled from Saul in the cave.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Be merciful to me, O God;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy mercy unto me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Do thou extend; because my soul  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth put her trust in thee:

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Yea, in the shadow of thy wings  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my refuge I will place,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Until these sad calamities  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do wholly overpass.

<sup>2</sup> My cry I will cause to ascend  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto the Lord most high;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;To God, who doth all things for me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;perform most perfectly.

<sup>3</sup> From heav’n he shall send down, and me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from his reproach defend  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;That would devour me: God his truth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and mercy forth shall send.

<sup>4</sup> My soul among fierce lions is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I firebrands live among,  
Men’s sons, whose teeth are spears and  
darts,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a sharp sword is their tongue.

<sup>5</sup> Be thou exalted very high  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;above the heav’ns, O God;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Let thou thy glory be advanced  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;o’er all the earth abroad.

<sup>6</sup> My soul ’s bowed down; for they a net  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;have laid, my steps to snare:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Into the pit which they have digged  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for me, they fallen are.

<sup>7</sup> My heart is fixed, my heart is fixed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O God; I’ll sing and praise.  
<sup>8</sup> My glory wake; wake psalt’ry, harp;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;myself I’ll early raise.

<sup>9</sup> I’ll praise thee ’mong the people, Lord;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;’mong nations sing will I:  
<sup>10</sup> For great to heav’n thy mercy is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy truth is to the sky.

<sup>11</sup> O Lord, exalted be thy name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;above the heav’ns to stand:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Do thou thy glory far advance  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;above both sea and land.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 58

*To the chief Musician, Al-taschith, Michtam of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Do ye, O congregätion,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;indeed speak righteousness?  
O ye that are the sons of men,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;judge ye with uprightness?

<sup>2</sup> Yea, ev’n within your very hearts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ye wickedness have done;  
And ye the vi’lence of your hands  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do weigh the earth upon.

<sup>3</sup> The wicked men estrangèd are,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n from the very womb;  
They, speaking lies, do stray as soon  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as to the world they come.

<sup>4</sup> Unto a serpent’s poison like  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their poison doth appear;  
Yea, they are like the adder deaf,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that closely stops her ear;

<sup>5</sup> That so she may not hear the voice  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of one that charm her would,  
No, not though he most cunning were,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and charm most wisely could.

<sup>6</sup> Their teeth, O God, within their mouth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;break thou in pieces small;  
The great teeth break thou out, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of these young lions all.

<sup>7</sup> Let them like waters melt away,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which downward still do flow:  
In pieces cut his arrows all,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when he shall bend his bow.

<sup>8</sup> Like to a snail that melts away,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let each of them be gone;  
Like woman’s birth untimely, that  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they never see the sun.

<sup>9</sup> He shall them take away before  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;your pots the thorns can find,  
Both living, and in fury great,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as with a stormy wind.

<sup>10</sup> The righteous, when he vengeance sees,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he shall be joyful then;  
The righteous one shall wash his feet  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in blood of wicked men.

<sup>11</sup> So men shall say, The righteous man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;reward shall never miss:  
And verily upon the earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a God to judge there is.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 59

*To the chief Musician, Al-taschith, Michtam of David; when Saul sent, and they watched the house to kill him.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> My God, deliver me from those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that are mine enemies;  
And do thou me defend from those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that up against me rise.

<sup>2</sup> Do thou deliver me from them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that work iniquity;  
And give me safety from the men  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of bloody cruelty.

<sup>3</sup> For, lo, they for my soul lay wait:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the mighty do combine  
Against me, Lord; not for my fault,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor any sin of mine.

<sup>4</sup> They run, and, without fault in me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;themselves do ready make:  
Awake to meet me with thy help;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and do thou notice take.

<sup>5</sup> Awake therefore, LORD God of hosts,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou God of Israel,  
To visit heathen all: spare none  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that wickedly rebel.

<sup>6</sup> At ev’ning they go to and fro;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they make great noise and sound,  
Like to a dog, and often walk  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;about the city round.

<sup>7</sup> Behold, they belch out with their mouth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and in their lips are swords:  
For they do say thus, Who is he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that now doth hear our words?

<sup>8</sup> But thou, O LORD, shalt laugh at them,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and all the heathen mock.  
<sup>9</sup> While he’s in pow’r I’ll wait on thee;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for God is my high rock.

<sup>10</sup> He of my mercy that is God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;betimes shall me prevent;  
Upon mine en’mies God shall let  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;me see mine heart’s content.

<sup>11</sup> Them slay not, lest my folk forget;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but scatter them abroad  
By thy strong pow’r; and bring them down,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O thou our shield and God.

<sup>12</sup> For their mouth’s sin, and for the words  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that from their lips do fly,  
Let them be taken in their pride;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;because they curse and lie.

<sup>13</sup> In wrath consume them, them consume,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that so they may not be:  
And that in Jacob God doth rule  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to th’ earth’s ends let them see.

<sup>14</sup> At ev’ning let thou them return,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;making great noise and sound,  
Like to a dog, and often walk  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;about the city round.

<sup>15</sup> And let them wander up and down,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in seeking food to eat;  
And let them grudge when they shall not  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be satisfied with meat.

<sup>16</sup> But of thy pow’r I’ll sing aloud;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;at morn thy mercy praise:  
For thou to me my refuge wast,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and tow’r, in troublous days.

<sup>17</sup> O God, thou art my strength, I will  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sing praises unto thee;  
For God is my defence, a God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of mercy unto me.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 60

*To the chief Musician upon Shushan-eduth, Michtam of David, to teach; when he strove with Aram-naharaim, and with Aram-zobah, when Joab returned and smote of Edom, in the valley of Salt, twelve thousand.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O Lord, thou hast rejected us,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and scatter’d us abroad;  
Thou justly hast displeasèd been;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;return to us, O God.

<sup>2</sup> The earth to tremble thou hast made;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;therein didst breaches make:  
Do thou thereof the breaches heal,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;because the land doth shake.

<sup>3</sup> Unto thy people thou hard things  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hast showed, and on them sent;  
And thou hast causèd us to drink  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wine of astonishment.

<sup>4</sup> And yet a banner thou hast given  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to them who thee do fear;  
That it by them, because of truth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;displayèd may appear.

<sup>5</sup> That thy belovèd people may  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;delivered be from thrall,  
Save with the pow’r of thy right hand,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and hear me when I call.

<sup>6</sup> God in his holiness hath spoke;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;herein I will take pleasure:  
Shechem I will divide, and forth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;will Succoth’s valley measure.

<sup>7</sup> Gilead I claim as mine by right;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Manasseh mine shall be;  
Ephraim is of mine head the strength;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Judah gives laws for me;

<sup>8</sup> Moab’s my washing-pot; my shoe  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I’ll over Edom throw;  
And over Palestina’s land  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I will in triumph go.

<sup>9</sup> O who is he will bring me to  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the city fortified?  
O who is he that to the land  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of Edom will me guide?

<sup>10</sup> O God, which hadest us cast off,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;this thing wilt thou not do?  
Ev’n thou, O God, which didest not  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;forth with our armies go?

<sup>11</sup> Help us from trouble; for the help  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is vain which man supplies.  
<sup>12</sup> Through God we’ll do great acts; he shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;tread down our enemies.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 61

*To the chief Musician upon Neginoth, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O God, give ear unto my cry;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto my pray’r attend.  
<sup>2</sup> From th’ utmost corner of the land  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my cry to thee I’ll send.

What time my heart is overwhelmed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and in perplexity,  
Do thou me lead unto the Rock  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that higher is than I.

<sup>3</sup> For thou hast for my refuge been  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a shelter by thy pow’r;  
And for defence against my foes  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou hast been a strong tow’r.

<sup>4</sup> Within thy tabernacle I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for ever will abide;  
And under covert of thy wings  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with confidence me hide.

<sup>5</sup> For thou the vows that I did make,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O Lord my God, didst hear:  
Thou hast giv’n me the heritage  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of those thy name that fear.

<sup>6</sup> A life prolonged for many days  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou to the king shalt give;  
Like many generations be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the years which he shall live.

<sup>7</sup> He in God’s presence his abode  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for evermore shall have:  
O do thou truth and mercy both  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;prepare, that may him save.

<sup>8</sup> And so will I perpetually  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sing praise unto thy name;  
That having made my vows, I may  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;each day perform the same.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 62

*To the chief Musician, to Jeduthun, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> My soul with expectätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;depends on God indeed;  
My strength and my salvation doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from him alone proceed.

<sup>2</sup> He only my salvation is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and my strong rock is he:  
He only is my sure defence;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;much moved I shall not be.

<sup>3</sup> How long will ye against a man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;plot mischief? ye shall all  
Be slain; ye as a tott’ring fence  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be, and bowing wall.

<sup>4</sup> They only plot to cast him down  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from his excellency:  
They joy in lies; with mouth they bless,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but they curse inwardly.

<sup>5</sup> My soul, wait thou with pätience  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon thy God alone;  
On him dependeth all my hope  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and expectätion.

<sup>6</sup> He only my salvation is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and my strong rock is he;  
He only is my sure defence:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I shall not movèd be.

<sup>7</sup> In God my glory placèd is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and my salvation sure;  
In God the rock is of my strength,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my refuge most secure.

<sup>8</sup> Ye people, place your confidence  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in him continually;  
Before him pour ye out your heart:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;God is our refuge high.

<sup>9</sup> Surely mean men are vanity,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and great men are a lie;  
In balance laid, they wholly are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;more light than vanity.

<sup>10</sup> Trust ye not in opprëssion,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in robb’ry be not vain;  
On wealth set not your hearts, when as  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;increasèd is your gain.

<sup>11</sup> God hath it spoken once to me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;yea, this I heard again,  
That powèr to Almighty God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;alone doth appertain.

<sup>12</sup> Yea, mercy also unto thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;belongs, O Lord, alone:  
For thou according to his work  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;rewardest ev’ry one.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 63

*A Psalm of David, when he was in the wilderness of Judah.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Lord, thee my God, I’ll early seek:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my soul doth thirst for thee;  
My flesh longs in a dry parched land,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wherein no waters be:

<sup>2</sup> That I thy powèr may behold,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and brightness of thy face,  
As I have seen thee heretofore  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within thy holy place.

<sup>3</sup> Since better is thy love than life,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my lips thee praise shall give.  
<sup>4</sup> I in thy name will lift my hands,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and bless thee while I live.

<sup>5</sup> Ev’n as with marrow and with fat  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my soul shall fillèd be;  
Then shall my mouth with joyful lips  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sing praises unto thee:

<sup>6</sup> When I do thee upon my bed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;remember with delight,  
And when on thee I meditate  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in watches of the night.

<sup>7</sup> In shadow of thy wings I’ll joy,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for thou mine help hast been.  
<sup>8</sup> My soul thee follows hard; and me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy right hand doth sustain.

<sup>9</sup> Who seek my soul to spill shall sink  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;down to earth’s lowest room.  
<sup>10</sup> They by the sword shall be cut off,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and foxes’ prey become.

<sup>11</sup> Yet shall the king in God rejoice,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and each one glory shall  
That swear by him; but stopped shall be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the mouth of liars all.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 64

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> When I to thee my prayer make,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Lord, to my voice give ear;  
My life save from the enemy,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of whom I stand in fear.

<sup>2</sup> Me from their secret counsel hide  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who do live wickedly;  
From insurrection of those men  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that work iniquity:

<sup>3</sup> Who do their tongues with malice whet,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and make them cut like swords;  
In whose bent bows are arrows set,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n sharp and bitter words:

<sup>4</sup> That they may at the perfect man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in secret aim their shot;  
Yea, suddenly they dare at him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to shoot, and fear it not.

<sup>5</sup> In ill encourage they themselves,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and their snares close do lay:  
Together conference they have;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Who shall them see? they say.

<sup>6</sup> They have searched out iniquities,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a perfect search they keep:  
Of each of them the inward thought,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and very heart, is deep.

<sup>7</sup> God shall an arrow shoot at them,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and wound them suddenly:  
<sup>8</sup> So their own tongue shall them confound;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all who them see shall fly.

<sup>9</sup> And on all men a fear shall fall,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;God’s works they shall declare;  
For they shall wisely notice take  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;what these his doings are.

<sup>10</sup> In God the righteous shall rejoice,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and trust upon his might;  
Yea, they shall greatly glory all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in heart that are upright.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 65

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm and Song of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Praise waits for thee in Zion, Lord:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to thee vows paid shall be.  
<sup>2</sup> O thou that hearer art of prayer,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all flesh shall come to thee.

<sup>3</sup> Iniquities, I must confess,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;prevail against me do:  
But as for our transgrëssions,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;them purge away shalt thou.

<sup>4</sup> Bless’d is the man whom thou dost choose,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and mak’st approach to thee,  
That he within thy courts, O Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;may still a dweller be:

We surely shall be satisfied  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with thy abundant grace,  
And with the goodness of thy house,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n of thy holy place.

<sup>5</sup> O God of our salvätion,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou, in thy righteousness,  
By fearful works unto our pray’rs  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thine answer dost express:

Therefore the ends of all the earth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and those afar that be  
Upon the sea, their confidence,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O Lord, will place in thee.

<sup>6</sup> Who, being girt with pow’r, sets fast  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by his great strength the hills.  
<sup>7</sup> Who noise of seas, noise of their waves,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and people’s tumult, stills.

<sup>8</sup> Those in the utmost parts that dwell  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are at thy signs afraid:  
Th’ outgoings of the morn and ev’n  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by thee are joyful made.

<sup>9</sup> The earth thou visit’st wat’ring it;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou mak’st it rich to grow  
With God’s full flood; thou corn prepar’st,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when thou provid’st it so.

<sup>10</sup> Her rigs thou wat’rest plenteously,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;her furrows settelest:  
With show’rs thou dost her mollify,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;her spring by thee is blest.

<sup>11</sup> So thou the year most lib’rally  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;dost with thy goodness crown;  
And all thy paths abundantly  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on us drop fatness down.

<sup>12</sup> They drop upon the pastures wide,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that do in deserts lie;  
The little hills on every side  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;rejoice right pleasantly.

<sup>13</sup> With flocks the pastures clothèd be,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the vales with corn are clad;  
And now they shout and sing to thee,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for thou hast made them glad.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 66

*To the chief Musician, A Song or Psalm.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> All lands to God, in joyful sounds,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;aloft your voices raise.  
<sup>2</sup> Sing forth the honour of his name,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and glorious make his praise.

<sup>3</sup> Say unto God, How terrible  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in all thy works art thou!  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Through thy great pow’r thy foes to thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be constrained to bow.

<sup>4</sup> All on the earth shall worship thee,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they shall thy praise proclaim  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In songs: they shall sing cheerfully  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto thy holy name.

<sup>5</sup> Come, and the works that God hath  
wrought  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with admiration see:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In’s working to the sons of men  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;most terrible is he.

<sup>6</sup> Into dry land the sea he turned,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and they a passage had;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Ev’n marching through the flood on foot,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;there we in him were glad.

<sup>7</sup> He ruleth ever by his pow’r;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his eyes the nations see:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O let not the rebellious ones  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;lift up themselves on high.

<sup>8</sup> Ye people, bless our God; aloud  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the voice speak of his praise:  
<sup>9</sup> Our soul in life who safe preserves,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our foot from sliding stays.

<sup>10</sup> For thou didst prove and try us, Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as men do silver try;  
<sup>11</sup> Brought’st us into the net, and mad’st  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;bands on our loins to lie.

<sup>12</sup> Thou hast caus’d men ride o’er our heads;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and though that we did pass  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Through fire and water, yet thou brought’st  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;us to a wealthy place.

<sup>13</sup> I’ll bring burnt-off’rings to thy house;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to thee my vows I’ll pay,  
<sup>14</sup> Which my lips uttered, my mouth spake,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when trouble on me lay.

<sup>15</sup> Burnt-sacrifices of fat rams  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with incense I will bring;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Of bullocks and of goats I will  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;present an offering.

<sup>16</sup> All that fear God, come, hear, I’ll tell  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;what he did for my soul.  
<sup>17</sup> I with my mouth unto him cried,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my tongue did him extol.

<sup>18</sup> If in my heart I sin regard,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the Lord me will not hear:  
<sup>19</sup> But surely God me heard, and to  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my prayèr’s voice gave ear.

<sup>20</sup> O let the Lord, our gracious God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for ever blessèd be,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Who turnèd not my pray’r from him,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor yet his grace from me.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 67

*To the chief Musician on Neginoth, A Psalm or Song.*

### Version 1

*S.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Lord, bless and pity us,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shine on us with thy face:  
<sup>2</sup> That th’ earth thy way, and nations all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;may know thy saving grace.

<sup>3</sup> Let people praise thee, Lord;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let people all thee praise.  
<sup>4</sup> O let the nätions be glad,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in songs their voices raise:

Thou ’lt justly people judge,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on earth rule nations all.  
<sup>5</sup> Let people praise thee, Lord; let them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;praise thee, both great and small.

<sup>6</sup> The earth her fruit shall yield,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our God shall blessing send.  
<sup>7</sup> God shall us bless; men shall him fear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto earth’s utmost end.

---

### Version 2

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Lord, unto us be merciful,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do thou us also bless;  
And graciously cause shine on us  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the brightness of thy face:

<sup>2</sup> That so thy way upon the earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to all men may be known;  
Also among the nations all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy saving health be shewn.

<sup>3</sup> O let the people praise thee, Lord;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let people all thee praise.  
<sup>4</sup> O let the nätions be glad,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and sing for joy always:

For rightly thou shalt people judge,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and nations rule on earth.  
<sup>5</sup> Let people praise thee, Lord; let all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the folk praise thee with mirth.

<sup>6</sup> Then shall the earth yield her increase;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;God, our God, bless us shall.  
<sup>7</sup> God shall us bless; and of the earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the ends shall fear him all.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 68

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm or Song of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Let God arise, and scatterèd  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let all his en’mies be;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And let all those that do him hate  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before his presence flee.

<sup>2</sup> As smoke is driv'n, so drive thou them;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as fire melts wax away,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Before God’s face let wicked men  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;so perish and decay.

<sup>3</sup> But let the rïghteous be glad:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let them before God’s sight  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Be very joyful; yea, let them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;rejoice with all their might.

<sup>4</sup> To God sing, to his name sing praise;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;extol him with your voice,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;That rides on heav’n, by his name JAH,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before his face rejoice.

<sup>5</sup> Because the Lord a father is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto the fatherless;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;God is the widow’s judge, within  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his place of holiness.

<sup>6</sup> God doth the solitary set  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in fam’lies: and from bands  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The chained doth free; but rebels do  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;inhabit parchèd lands.

<sup>7</sup> O God, what time thou didst go forth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before thy people’s face;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And when through the great wilderness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy glorious marching was;

<sup>8</sup> Then at God’s presence shook the earth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;then drops from heaven fell;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This Sinai shook before the Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the God of Israel.

<sup>9</sup> O God, thou to thine heritage  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;didst send a plenteous rain,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Whereby thou, when it weary was,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;didst it refresh again.

<sup>10</sup> Thy congregation then did make  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their habitation there:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Of thine own goodness for the poor,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O God, thou didst prepare.

<sup>11</sup> The Lord himself did give the word,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the word abroad did spread;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Great was the company of them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the same who publishèd.

<sup>12</sup> Kings of great armies foilèd were,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and forced to flee away;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And women, who remained at home,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did distribute the prey.

<sup>13</sup> Though ye have lain among the pots,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;like doves ye shall appear,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Whose wings with silver, and with gold  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whose feathers covered are.

<sup>14</sup> When there th’ Almighty scattered kings,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;like Salmon’s snow ’twas white.  
<sup>15</sup> God’s hill is like to Bashan hill,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;like Bashan hill for height.

<sup>16</sup> Why do ye leap, ye mountains high?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;this is the hill where God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Desires to dwell; yea, God in it  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for aye will make abode.

<sup>17</sup> God’s chariots twenty thousand are,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thousands of angels strong;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In ’s holy place God is, as in  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mount Sinai, them among.

<sup>18</sup> Thou hast, O Lord, most glorious,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ascended up on high;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And in triumph victorious led  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;captive captivity:

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Thou hast receivèd gifts for men,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for such as did rebel;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Yea, ev’n for them, that God the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in midst of them might dwell.

<sup>19</sup> Bless’d be the Lord, who is to us  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of our salvation God;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Who daily with his benefits  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;us plenteously doth load.

<sup>20</sup> He of salvation is the God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who is our God most strong;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And unto GOD the Lord from death  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the issues do belong.

<sup>21</sup> But surely God shall wound the head  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of those that are his foes;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The hairy scalp of him that still  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on in his trespass goes.

<sup>22</sup> God said, My people I will bring  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;again from Bashan hill;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Yea, from the sea’s devouring depths  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;them bring again I will;

<sup>23</sup> That in the blood of enemies  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy foot imbrued may be,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And of thy dogs dipped in the same  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the tongues thou mayest see.

<sup>24</sup> Thy goings they have seen, O God;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the steps of majesty  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Of my God, and my mighty King,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within the sanctuary.

<sup>25</sup> Before went singers, players next  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on instruments took way;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And them among the damsels were  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that did on timbrels play.

<sup>26</sup> Within the congregätions  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;bless God with one accord:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;From Isr’el’s fountain do ye bless  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and praise the mighty Lord.

<sup>27</sup> With their prince, little Benjamin,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;princes and council there  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Of Judah were, there Zabulon’s  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and Napht’li’s princes were.

<sup>28</sup> Thy God commands thy strength; make  
strong  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;what thou wrought’st for us, Lord.  
<sup>29</sup> For thy house at Jerusalem  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;kings shall thee gifts afford.

<sup>30</sup> The spearmen’s host, the multitude  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of bulls, which fiercely look,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Those calves which people have forth sent,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O Lord our God, rebuke,

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Till everyone submit himself,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and silver pieces bring:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The people that delight in war  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;disperse, O God and King.

<sup>31</sup> Those that be princes great shall then  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;come out of Egypt lands;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And Ethiopia to God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall soon stretch out her hands.

<sup>32</sup> O all ye kingdoms of the earth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sing praises to this King;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For he is Lord that ruleth all,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto him praises sing.

<sup>33</sup> To him that rides on heav’ns of heav’ns,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which he of old did found;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Lo, he sends out his voice, a voice  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in might that doth abound.

<sup>34</sup> Strength unto God do ye ascribe;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for his excellency  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Is over Israèl, his strength  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is in the clouds most high.

<sup>35</sup> Thou ’rt from thy temple dreadful, Lord;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Isr’el’s own God is he,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Who gives his people strength and pow’r:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O let God blessèd be.

## Psalm 69

*To the chief Musician upon Shoshannim, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Save me, O God, because the floods  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do so environ me,  
That ev’n unto my very soul  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;come in the waters be.

<sup>2</sup> I downward in deep mire do sink,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;where standing there is none:  
I am into deep waters come,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;where floods have o’er me gone.

<sup>3</sup> I weary with my crying am,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my throat is also dried;  
Mine eyes do fail, while for my God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I waiting do abide.

<sup>4</sup> Those men that do without a cause  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;bear hatred unto me,  
Than are the hairs upon my head  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in number more they be:

They that would me destroy, and are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mine en’mies wrongfully,  
Are mighty: so what I took not,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to render forced was I.

<sup>5</sup> Lord, thou my folly know’st, my sins  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;not covered are from thee.  
<sup>6</sup> Let none that wait on thee be shamed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Lord God of hosts, for me.

O Lord, the God of Israel,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let none, who search do make,  
And seek thee, be at any time  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;confounded for my sake.

<sup>7</sup> For I have borne reproach for thee,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my face is hid with shame.  
<sup>8</sup> To brethren strange, to mother’s sons  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;an alien I became.

<sup>9</sup> Because the zeal did eat me up,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which to thine house I bear;  
And the reproaches cast at thee,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon me fallen are.

<sup>10</sup> My tears and fasts, t’ afflict my soul,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;were turnèd to my shame.  
<sup>11</sup> When sackcloth I did wear, to them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a proverb I became.

<sup>12</sup> The men that in the gate do sit  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;against me evil spake;  
They also that vile drunkards were  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of me their song did make.

<sup>13</sup> But, in an acceptàble time,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my pray’r, LORD, is to thee:  
In truth of thy salvation, Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and mercy great, hear me.

<sup>14</sup> Deliver me out of the mire,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from sinking do me keep;  
Free me from those that do me hate,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and from the waters deep.

<sup>15</sup> Let not the flood on me prevail,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whose water overflows;  
Nor deep me swallow, nor the pit  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;her mouth upon me close.

<sup>16</sup> Hear me, O LORD, because thy love  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and kindness is most good;  
Turn unto me, according to  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy mercies’ multitude.

<sup>17</sup> Nor from thy servant hide thy face:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I’m troubled, soon attend.  
<sup>18</sup> Draw near my soul, and it redeem;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;me from my foes defend.

<sup>19</sup> To thee is my reproach well known,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my shame, and my disgrace:  
Those that mine adversaries be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are all before thy face.

<sup>20</sup> Reproach hath broke my heart; I’m full  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of grief: I looked for one  
To pity me, but none I found;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;comforters found I none.

<sup>21</sup> They also bitter gall did give  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto me for my meat:  
They gave me vinegar to drink,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when as my thirst was great.

<sup>22</sup> Before them let their table prove  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a snare; and do thou make  
Their welfare and prosperity  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a trap themselves to take.

<sup>23</sup> Let thou their eyes so darkened be,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that sight may them forsake;  
And let their loins be made by thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;continually to shake.

<sup>24</sup> Thy fury pour thou out on them,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and indignätion;  
And let thy wrathful anger, Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;fast hold take them upon.

<sup>25</sup> All waste and desolate let be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their habitätion;  
And in their tabernacles all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;inhabitants be none.

<sup>26</sup> Because him they do persecute,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whom thou didst smite before;  
They talk unto the grief of those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whom thou hast wounded sore.

<sup>27</sup> Add thou iniquity unto  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their former wickedness;  
And do not let them come at all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;into thy righteousness.

<sup>28</sup> Out of the book of life let them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be razed and blotted quite;  
Among the just and rïghteous  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let not their names be writ.

<sup>29</sup> But now become exceeding poor  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and sorrowful am I:  
By thy salvation, O my God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let me be set on high.

<sup>30</sup> The name of God I with a song  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;most cheerfully will praise;  
And I, in giving thanks to him,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his name shall highly raise.

<sup>31</sup> This to the LORD a sacrifice  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;more gräcious shall prove  
Than bullock, ox, or any beast  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that hath both horn and hoof.

<sup>32</sup> When this the humble men shall see,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it joy to them shall give:  
O all ye that do seek the Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;your hearts shall ever live.

<sup>33</sup> For GOD the poor hears, and will not  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his prisoners contemn.  
<sup>34</sup> Let heav’n, and earth, and seas, him praise,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and all that move in them.

<sup>35</sup> For God will Judah’s cities build,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and he will Zion save,  
That they may dwell therein, and it  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in sure possession have.

<sup>36</sup> And they that are his servants’ seed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;inherit shall the same;  
So shall they have their dwelling there  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that love his blessèd name.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 70

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm of David, to bring to remembrance.*

### Version 1

*S.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Lord, haste me to deliver;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with speed, LORD, succour me.  
<sup>2</sup> Let them that for my soul do seek  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shamed and confounded be:

Turned back be they, and shamed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that in my hurt delight.  
<sup>3</sup> Turned back be they, Ha, ha! that say,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their shaming to requite.

<sup>4</sup> In thee let all be glad,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and joy that seek for thee:  
Let them who thy salvation love  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;say still, God praisèd be.

<sup>5</sup> I poor and needy am;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;come, Lord, and make no stay:  
My help thou and deliv’rer art;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O LORD, make no delay.

---

### Version 2

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Make haste, O God, me to preserve;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with speed, LORD, succour me.  
<sup>2</sup> Let them that for my soul do seek  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shamed and confounded be:

Let them be turnèd back, and shamed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that in my hurt delight.  
<sup>3</sup> Turned back be they, Ha, ha! that say,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their shaming to requite.

<sup>4</sup> O Lord, in thee let all be glad,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and joy that seek for thee:  
Let them who thy salvation love  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;say still, God praisèd be.

<sup>5</sup> But I both poor and needy am;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;come, Lord, and make no stay:  
My help thou and deliv’rer art;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O LORD, make no delay.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 71

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O LORD, my hope and confidence  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is placed in thee alone;  
Then let thy servant never be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;put to confüsion.

<sup>2</sup> And let me, in thy righteousness,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from thee deliv’rance have;  
Cause me escape, incline thine ear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto me, and me save.

<sup>3</sup> Be thou my dwelling-rock, to which  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I ever may resort:  
Thou gav’st commandment me to save,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for thou ’rt my rock and fort.

<sup>4</sup> Free me, my God, from wicked hands,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hands cruel and unjust:  
<sup>5</sup> For thou, O Lord GOD, art my hope,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and from my youth my trust.

<sup>6</sup> Thou from the womb didst hold me up;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou art the same that me  
Out of my mother’s bowels took;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I ever will praise thee.

<sup>7</sup> To many I a wonder am;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but thou ’rt my refuge strong.  
<sup>8</sup> Filled let my mouth be with thy praise  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and honour all day long.

<sup>9</sup> O do not cast me off, when as  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;old age doth overtake me;  
And when my strength decayèd is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;then do not thou forsake me.

<sup>10</sup> For those that are mine enemies  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;against me speak with hate;  
And they together counsel take  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that for my soul lay wait.

<sup>11</sup> They said, God leaves him; him pursue  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and take: none will him save.  
<sup>12</sup> Be thou not far from me, my God:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy speedy help I crave.

<sup>13</sup> Confound, consume them, that unto  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my soul are enemies:  
Clothed be they with reproach and shame  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that do my hurt devise.

<sup>14</sup> But I with expectätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;will hope continually;  
And yet with praises more and more  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I will thee magnify.

<sup>15</sup> Thy justice and salvätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my mouth abroad shall show,  
Ev’n all the day; for I thereof  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the numbers do not know.

<sup>16</sup> And I will constantly go on  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in strength of GOD the Lord;  
And thine own righteousness, ev’n thine  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;alone, I will record.

<sup>17</sup> For even from my youth, O God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by thee I have been taught;  
And hitherto I have declared  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the wonders thou hast wrought.

<sup>18</sup> And now, Lord, leave me not, when I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;old and grey-headed grow:  
Till to this age thy strength and pow’r  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to all to come I show.

<sup>19</sup> And thy most perfect righteousness,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O Lord, is very high,  
Who has so great things done: O God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who is like unto thee?

<sup>20</sup> Thou, Lord, who great adversities,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and sore, to me didst show,  
Shalt quicken, and bring me again  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from depths of earth below.

<sup>21</sup> My greatness and my pow’r thou wilt  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;increase, and far extend:  
On ev’ry side against all grief  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou wilt me comfort send.

<sup>22</sup> Thee, ev’n thy truth, I’ll also praise,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my God, with psaltery:  
Thou Holy One of Israel,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with harp I’ll sing to thee.

<sup>23</sup> My lips shall much rejoice in thee,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when I thy praises sound;  
My soul, which thou redeemèd hast,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in joy shall much abound.

<sup>24</sup> My tongue thy justice shall proclaim,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;continuing all day long;  
For they confounded are, and shamed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that seek to do me wrong.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)
