## Psalm 72

*A Psalm for Solomon.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O Lord, thy judgments give the king,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his son thy righteousness.  
<sup>2</sup> With right he shall thy people judge,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy poor with uprightness.

<sup>3</sup> The lofty mountains shall bring forth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto the people peace;  
Likewise the little hills the same  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall do by righteousness.

<sup>4</sup> The people’s poor ones he shall judge,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the needy’s children save;  
And those shall he in pieces break  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who them oppressèd have.

<sup>5</sup> They shall thee fear, while sun and moon  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do last, through ages all.  
<sup>6</sup> Like rain on mown grass he shall drop,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;or show’rs on earth that fall.

<sup>7</sup> The just shall flourish in his days,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and prosper in his reign:  
He shall, while doth the moon endure,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;abundant peace maintain.

<sup>8</sup> His large and great dominion shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from sea to sea extend:  
It from the river shall reach forth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto earth’s utmost end.

<sup>9</sup> They in the wilderness that dwell  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;bow down before him must;  
And they that are his enemies  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall lick the very dust.

<sup>10</sup> The kings of Tarshish, and the isles,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to him shall presents bring;  
And unto him shall offer gifts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sheba’s and Seba’s king.

<sup>11</sup> Yea, all the mighty kings on earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before him down shall fall;  
And all the nations of the world  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do service to him shall.

<sup>12</sup> For he the needy shall preserve,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when he to him doth call;  
The poor also, and him that hath  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;no help of man at all.

<sup>13</sup> The poor man and the indigent  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in mercy he shall spare;  
He shall preserve alive the souls  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of those that needy are.

<sup>14</sup> Both from deceit and violence  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their soul he shall set free;  
And in his sight right prëcious  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and dear their blood shall be.

<sup>15</sup> Yea, he shall live, and giv’n to him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be of Sheba’s gold:  
For him still shall they pray, and he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall daily be extolled.

<sup>16</sup> Of corn an handful in the earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on tops of mountains high,  
With prosp’rous fruit shall shake, like trees  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on Lebanon that be.

The city shall be flourishing,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;her citizens abound  
In number shall, like to the grass  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that grows upon the ground.

<sup>17</sup> His name for ever shall endure;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;last like the sun it shall:  
Men shall be blessed in him, and blessed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all nations shall him call.

<sup>18</sup> Now blessèd be the LORD our God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the God of Israel,  
For he alone doth wondrous works,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in glory that excel.

<sup>19</sup> And blessèd be his glorious name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to all eternity:  
The whole earth let his glory fill.  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Amen, so let it be.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

# Book III

*Psalms 73&ndash;89*

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 73

*A Psalm of Asaph.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Yet God is good to Israel,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to each pure-hearted one.  
<sup>2</sup> But as for me, my steps near slipped,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my feet were almost gone.

<sup>3</sup> For I envìous was, and grudged  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the foolish folk to see,  
When I perceived the wicked sort  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;enjoy prosperity.

<sup>4</sup> For still their strength continueth firm;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their death of bands is free.  
<sup>5</sup> They are not toiled like other men,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor plagued, as others be.

<sup>6</sup> Therefore their pride, like to a chain,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;them compasseth about;  
And, as a garment, violence  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth cover them throughout.

<sup>7</sup> Their eyes stand out with fat; they have  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;more than their hearts could wish.  
<sup>8</sup> They are corrupt; their talk of wrong  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;both lewd and lofty is.

<sup>9</sup> They set their mouth against the heav’ns  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in their blasphemous talk;  
And their reproaching tongue throughout  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the earth at large doth walk.

<sup>10</sup> His people oftentimes for this  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;look back, and turn about;  
Sith waters of so full a cup  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to these are pourèd out.

<sup>11</sup> And thus they say, How can it be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that God these things doth know?  
Or, Can there in the Highest be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;knowledge of things below?

<sup>12</sup> Behold, these are the wicked ones,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;yet prosper at their will  
In worldly things; they do increase  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in wealth and riches still.

<sup>13</sup> I verily have done in vain  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my heart to purify;  
To no effect in innocence  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;washèd my hands have I.

<sup>14</sup> For daily, and all day throughout,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;great plagues I suffered have;  
Yea, ev’ry morning I of new  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did chastisement receive.

<sup>15</sup> If in this manner foolishly  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to speak I would intend,  
Thy children’s generätion,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;behold, I should offend.

<sup>16</sup> When I this thought to know, it was  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;too hard a thing for me;  
<sup>17</sup> Till to God’s sanctuary I went,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;then I their end did see.

<sup>18</sup> Assuredly thou didst them set  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a slipp’ry place upon;  
Them suddenly thou castedst down  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;into destrüction.

<sup>19</sup> How in a moment suddenly  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to ruin brought are they!  
With fearful terrors utterly  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they are consumed away.

<sup>20</sup> Ev’n like unto a dream, when one  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from sleeping doth arise;  
So thou, O Lord, when thou awak’st,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their image shalt despise.

<sup>21</sup> Thus grievèd was my heart in me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and me my reins oppressed:  
<sup>22</sup> So rude was I, and ignorant,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and in thy sight a beast.

<sup>23</sup> Nevertheless continually,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O Lord, I am with thee:  
Thou dost me hold by my right hand,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and still upholdest me.

<sup>24</sup> Thou, with thy counsel, while I live,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wilt me conduct and guide;  
And to thy glory afterward  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;receive me to abide.

<sup>25</sup> Whom have I in the heavens high  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but thee, O Lord, alone?  
And in the earth whom I desire  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;besides thee there is none.

<sup>26</sup> My flesh and heart doth faint and fail,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but God doth fail me never:  
For of my heart God is the strength  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and pörtion for ever.

<sup>27</sup> For, lo, they that are far from thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for ever perish shall;  
Them that a whoring from thee go  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou hast destroyèd all.

<sup>28</sup> But surely it is good for me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that I draw near to God:  
In GOD I trust, that all thy works  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I may declare abroad.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 74

*Maschil of Asaph.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O God, why hast thou cast us off?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is it for evermore?  
Against thy pasture-sheep why doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thine anger smoke so sore?

<sup>2</sup> O call to thy rememberance  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy congregätion,  
Which thou hast purchasèd of old;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;still think the same upon:

The rod of thine inheritance,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which thou redeemèd hast,  
This Zion hill, wherein thou hadst  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy dwelling in times past.

<sup>3</sup> To these long desolätions  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy feet lift, do not tarry;  
For all the ills thy foes have done  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within thy sanctuary.

<sup>4</sup> Amidst thy congregätions  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thine enemies do roar:  
Their ensigns they set up for signs  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of triumph thee before.

<sup>5</sup> A man was famous, and was had  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in estimätion,  
According as he lifted up  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his axe thick trees upon.

<sup>6</sup> But all at once with axes now  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and hammers they go to,  
And down the carvèd work thereof  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they break, and quite undo.

<sup>7</sup> They firèd have thy sanctuary,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and have defiled the same,  
By casting down unto the ground  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the place where dwelt thy name.

<sup>8</sup> Thus said they in their hearts, Let us  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;destroy them out of hand:  
They burnt up all the synagogues  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of God within the land.

<sup>9</sup> Our signs we do not now behold;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;there is not us among  
A prophet more, nor any one  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that knows the time how long.

<sup>10</sup> How long, Lord, shall the enemy  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thus in reproach exclaim?  
And shall the adversary thus  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;always blaspheme thy name?

<sup>11</sup> Thy hand, ev’n thy right hand of might,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;why dost thou thus draw back?  
O from thy bosom pluck it out  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for our deliv’rance’ sake.

<sup>12</sup> For certainly God is my King,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n from the times of old,  
Working in midst of all the earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;salvation manifold.

<sup>13</sup> The sea, by thy great pow’r, to part  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;asunder thou didst make;  
And thou the dragons’ heads, O Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within the waters brake.

<sup>14</sup> The leviathan’s head thou brak’st  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in pieces, and didst give  
Him to be meat unto the folk  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in wilderness that live.

<sup>15</sup> Thou clav’st the fountain and the flood,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which did with streams abound:  
Thou dri’dst the mighty waters up  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto the very ground.

<sup>16</sup> Thine only is the day, O Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thine also is the night;  
And thou alone preparèd hast  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the sun and shining light.

<sup>17</sup> By thee the borders of the earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;were settled everywhere:  
The summer and the winter both  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by thee created were.

<sup>18</sup> That th’ enemy reproachèd hath,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O keep it in record;  
And that the foolish people have  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;blasphemed thy name, O LORD.

<sup>19</sup> Unto the multitude do not  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy turtle’s soul deliver:  
The congregation of thy poor  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do not forget for ever.

<sup>20</sup> Unto thy cov’nant have respect;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for earth’s dark places be  
Full of the habitätions  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of horrid cruelty.

<sup>21</sup> O let not those that be oppressed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;return again with shame:  
Let those that poor and needy are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;give praise unto thy name.

<sup>22</sup> Do thou, O God, arise and plead  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the cause that is thine own:  
Remember how thou art reproached  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;still by the foolish one.

<sup>23</sup> Do not forget the voice of those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that are thine enemies:  
Of those the tumult ever grows  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that do against thee rise.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 75

*To the chief Musician, Al-taschith, A Psalm or Song of Asaph.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> To thee, O God, do we give thanks,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;we do give thanks to thee;  
Because thy wondrous works declare  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy great name near to be.

<sup>2</sup> I purpose, when I shall receive  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the congregätion,  
That I shall judgment uprightly  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;render to everyone.

<sup>3</sup> Dissolvèd is the land, with all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that in the same do dwell;  
But I the pillars thereof do  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;bear up, and stablish well.

<sup>4</sup> I to the foolish people said,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Do not deal foolishly;  
And unto those that wicked are,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Lift not your horn on high.

<sup>5</sup> Lift not your horn on high, nor speak  
<sup>6</sup> with stubborn neck. But know,  
That not from east, nor west, nor south,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;promötion doth flow.

<sup>7</sup> But God is judge; he puts down one,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and sets another up.  
<sup>8</sup> For in the hand of GOD most high  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of red wine is a cup:

’Tis full of mixture, he pours forth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and makes the wicked all  
Wring out the bitter dregs thereof;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;yea, and they drink them shall.

<sup>9</sup> But I for ever will declare,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I Jacob’s God will praise.  
<sup>10</sup> All horns of lewd men I’ll cut off;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but just men’s horns will raise.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 76

*To the chief Musician on Neginoth, A Psalm or Song of Asaph.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> In Judah’s land God is well known,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his name ’s in Isr’el great:  
<sup>2</sup> In Salem is his tabernacle,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in Zion is his seat.

<sup>3</sup> There arrows of the bow he brake,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the shield, the sword, the war.  
<sup>4</sup> More glorious thou than hills of prey,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;more excellent art far.

<sup>5</sup> Those that were stout of heart are spoiled,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they slept their sleep outright;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And none of those their hands did find,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that were the men of might.

<sup>6</sup> When thy rebuke, O Jacob’s God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;had forth against them past,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Their horses and their chariots both  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;were in a deep sleep cast.

<sup>7</sup> Thou, Lord, ev’n thou art he that should  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be feared; and who is he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;That may stand up before thy sight,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;if once thou angry be?

<sup>8</sup> From heav’n thou judgment caused be  
heard;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the earth was still with fear,  
<sup>9</sup> When God to judgment rose, to save  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all meek on earth that were.

<sup>10</sup> Surely the very wrath of man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto thy praise redounds:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Thou to the remnant of his wrath  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wilt set restraining bounds.

<sup>11</sup> Vow to the LORD your God, and pay:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all ye that near him be,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Bring gifts and presents unto him;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for to be feared is he.

<sup>12</sup> By him the spirits shall be cut off  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of those that princes are:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Unto the kings that are on earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he fearful doth appear.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 77

*To the chief Musician, to Jeduthun, A Psalm of Asaph.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Unto the Lord I with my voice,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I unto God did cry;  
Ev’n with my voice, and unto me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his ear he did apply.

<sup>2</sup> I in my trouble sought the Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my sore by night did run,  
And ceasèd not; my grievèd soul  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did consolation shun.

<sup>3</sup> I to remembrance God did call,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;yet trouble did remain;  
And overwhelmed my spirit was,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whilst I did sore complain.

<sup>4</sup> Mine eyes, debarred from rest and sleep,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou makest still to wake;  
My trouble is so great that I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unable am to speak.

<sup>5</sup> The days of old to mind I called,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and oft did think upon  
The times and ages that are past  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;full many years agone.

<sup>6</sup> By night my song I call to mind,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and commune with my heart;  
My spirit did carefully enquire  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;how I might ease my smart.

<sup>7</sup> For ever will the Lord cast off,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and gracious be no more?  
<sup>8</sup> For ever is his mercy gone?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;fails his word evermore?

<sup>9</sup> Is ’t true that to be gräcious  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the Lord forgotten hath?  
And that his tender mercies he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hath shut up in his wrath?

<sup>10</sup> Then did I say, That surely this  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is mine infirmity:  
I’ll mind the years of the right hand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of him that is most High.

<sup>11</sup> Yea, I remember will the works  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;performèd by the LORD:  
The wonders done of old by thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I surely will record.

<sup>12</sup> I also will of all thy works  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my meditation make;  
And of thy doings to discourse  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;great pleasure I will take.

<sup>13</sup> O God, thy way most holy is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within thy sanctuary;  
And what God is so great in power  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as is our God most high?

<sup>14</sup> Thou art the God that wonders do’st  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by thy right hand most strong:  
Thy mighty pow’r thou hast declared  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the nations among.

<sup>15</sup> To thine own people with thine arm  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou didst redemption bring;  
To Jacob’s sons, and to the tribes  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of Joseph that do spring.

<sup>16</sup> The waters, Lord, perceivèd thee,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the waters saw thee well;  
And they for fear aside did flee;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the depths on trembling fell.

<sup>17</sup> The clouds in water forth were poured,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sound loudly did the sky;  
And swiftly through the world abroad  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thine arrows fierce did fly.

<sup>18</sup> Thy thunder’s voice alongst the heaven  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a mighty noise did make;  
By lightnings lightened was the world,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;th’ earth tremble did and shake.

<sup>19</sup> Thy way is in the sea, and in  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the waters great thy path;  
Yet are thy footsteps hid, O Lord;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;none knowledge thereof hath.

<sup>20</sup> Thy people thou didst safely lead,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;like to a flock of sheep;  
By Moses’ hand and Aaron’s thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;didst them conduct and keep.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 78

*Maschil of Asaph.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Attend, my people, to my law;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thereto give thou an ear;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The words that from my mouth proceed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;attentively do hear.

<sup>2</sup> My mouth shall speak a parable,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and sayings dark of old;  
<sup>3</sup> The same which we have heard and known,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and us our fathers told.

<sup>4</sup> We also will them not conceal  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from their posterity;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Them to the generätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to come declare will we:

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The praises of the LORD our God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and his almighty strength,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The wondrous works that he hath done,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;we will show forth at length.

<sup>5</sup> His testimony and his law  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in Isr’el he did place,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And charged our fathers it to show  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to their succeeding race;

<sup>6</sup> That so the race which was to come  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;might well them learn and know;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And sons unborn, who should arise,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;might to their sons them show:

<sup>7</sup> That they might set their hope in God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and suffer not to fall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;His mighty works out of their mind,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but keep his precepts all:

<sup>8</sup> And might not, like their fathers, be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a stiff rebellious race;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;A race not right in heart; with God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whose spirit not steadfast was.

<sup>9</sup> The sons of Ephraim, who nor bows  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor other arms did lack,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;When as the day of battle was,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they faintly turnèd back.

<sup>10</sup> They brake God’s cov’nant, and refused  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in his commands to go;  
<sup>11</sup> His works and wonders they forgot,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which he to them did show.

<sup>12</sup> Things marvellous he brought to pass;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their fathers them beheld  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Within the land of Egypt done,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;yea, ev’n in Zoàn’s field.

<sup>13</sup> By him divided was the sea,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he caused them through to pass;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And made the waters so to stand,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as like an heap it was.

<sup>14</sup> With cloud by day, with light of fire  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all night, he did them guide.  
<sup>15</sup> In desert rocks he clave, and drink,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as from great depths, supplied.

<sup>16</sup> He from the rock brought streams, like  
floods  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;made waters to run down.  
<sup>17</sup> Yet sinning more, in desert they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;provoked the Highest One.

<sup>18</sup> For in their heart they tempted God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and, speaking with mistrust,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;They greedily did meat require  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to satisfy their lust.

<sup>19</sup> Against the Lord himself they spake,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and, murmuring, said thus,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;A table in the wilderness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;can God prepare for us?

<sup>20</sup> Behold, he smote the rock, and thence  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;came streams and waters great;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;But can he give his people bread?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and send them flesh to eat?

<sup>21</sup> The LORD did hear, and waxèd wroth;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;so kindled was a flame  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;’Gainst Jacob, and ’gainst Israel  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;up indignation came.

<sup>22</sup> For they believed not God, nor trust  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in his salvation had;  
<sup>23</sup> Though clouds above he did command,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and heav’n’s doors open made,

<sup>24</sup> And manna rained on them, and gave  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;them corn of heav’n to eat.  
<sup>25</sup> Man angels’ food did eat; to them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he to the full sent meat.

<sup>26</sup> And in the heaven he did cause  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;an eastern wind to blow;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And by his powèr he let out  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the southern wind to go.

<sup>27</sup> Then flesh as thick as dust he made  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to rain down them among;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And feathered fowls, like as the sand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which lieth the shore along.

<sup>28</sup> At his command amidst their camp  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;these show’rs of flesh down fell,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;All round about the tabernacles  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and tents where they did dwell.

<sup>29</sup> So they did eat abundantly,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and had of meat their fill;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For he did give to them what was  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their own desire and will.

<sup>30</sup> They from their lust had not estranged  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their heart and their desire;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;But while the meat was in their mouths,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which they did so require,

<sup>31</sup> God’s wrath upon them came, and slew  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the fattest of them all;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;So that the choice of Israel,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;o’erthrown by death, did fall.

<sup>32</sup> Yet, notwithstanding of all this,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they sinnèd still the more;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And though he had great wonders wrought,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;believed him not therefor:

<sup>33</sup> Wherefore their days in vanity  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he did consume and waste;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And by his wrath their wretched years  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;away in trouble past.

<sup>34</sup> But when he slew them, then they did  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to seek him show desire;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Yea, they returned, and after God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;right early did enquire.

<sup>35</sup> And that the Lord had been their Rock  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they did remember then;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Ev’n that the high almighty God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;had their Redeemer been.

<sup>36</sup> Yet with their mouth they flattered him,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and spake but feignèdly;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And they unto the God of truth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with their false tongues did lie.

<sup>37</sup> For though their words were good, their  
heart  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with him was not sincere;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Unsteadfast and perfidious  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they in his cov’nant were.

<sup>38</sup> But, full of pity, he forgave  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their sin, them did not slay;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Nor stirred up all his wrath, but oft  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his anger turned away.

<sup>39</sup> For that they were but fading flesh  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to mind he did recall;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;A wind that passeth soon away,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and not returns at all.

<sup>40</sup> How often did they him provoke  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within the wilderness!  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And in the desert did him grieve  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with their rebelliousness!

<sup>41</sup> Yea, turning back, they tempted God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and limits set upon  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Him, who in midst of Isr’el is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the only Holy One.

<sup>42</sup> They did not call to mind his pow’r,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;not yet the day when he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Delivered them out of the hand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of their fierce enemy;

<sup>43</sup> Nor how great signs in Egypt land  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he openly had wrought;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;What miracles in Zoàn’s field  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his hand to pass had brought.

<sup>44</sup> How lakes and rivers everywhere  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he turnèd into blood;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;So that nor man nor beast could drink  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of standing lake or flood.

<sup>45</sup> He brought among them swarms of flies,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which did them sore annoy;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And divers kinds of filthy frogs  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he sent them to destroy.

<sup>46</sup> He to the caterpillar gave  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the fruits of all their soil;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Their labours he delivered up  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto the locusts’ spoil.

<sup>47</sup> Their vines with hail, their sycamores  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he with the frost did blast:  
<sup>48</sup> Their beasts to hail he gave; their flocks  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hot thunderbolts did waste.

<sup>49</sup> Fierce burning wrath he on them cast,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and indignation strong,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And troubles sore, by sending forth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ill angels them among.

<sup>50</sup> He to his wrath made way; their soul  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from death he did not save;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;But over to the pestilence  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the lives of them he gave.

<sup>51</sup> In Egypt land the first-born all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he smote down everywhere;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Among the tents of Ham, ev’n these  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;chief of their strength that were.

<sup>52</sup> But his own people, like to sheep,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thence to go forth he made;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And he, amidst the wilderness,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;them, as a flock, did lead.

<sup>53</sup> And he them safely on did lead,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;so that they did not fear;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Whereas their en’mies by the sea  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;quite overwhelmèd were.

<sup>54</sup> To borders of his sanctuary  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the Lord his people led,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Ev’n to the mount which his right hand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for them had purchasèd.

<sup>55</sup> The nätions of Canàan,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by his almighty hand,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Before their face he did expel  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;out of their native land;

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Which for inheritance to them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by line he did divide,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And made the tribes of Israel  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within their tents abide.

<sup>56</sup> Yet God Most High they did provoke,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and tempted ever still;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And to observe his test’monies  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did not incline their will:

<sup>57</sup> But, like their fathers, turnèd back,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and dealt unfaithfully:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Aside they turnèd, like a bow  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that shoots deceitfully.

<sup>58</sup> For they to anger did provoke  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;him with their places high;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And with their graven images  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;moved him to jealousy.

<sup>59</sup> When God heard this, he waxèd wroth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and much loathed Isr’el then:  
<sup>60</sup> So Shiloh’s tent he left, the tent  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which he had placed with men.

<sup>61</sup> And he his strength deliverèd  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;into captivity;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;He left his glory in the hand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of his proud enemy.

<sup>62</sup> His people also he gave o’er  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto the sword’s fierce rage:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;So sore his wrath inflamèd was  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;against his heritage.

<sup>63</sup> The fire consumed their choice young men;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their maids no marriage had;  
<sup>64</sup> And when their priests fell by the sword,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their wives no mourning made.

<sup>65</sup> But then the Lord arose, as one  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that doth from sleep awake;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And like a giant that, by wine  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;refreshed, a shout doth make:

<sup>66</sup> Upon his en’mies’ hinder parts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he made his stroke to fall;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And so upon them he did put  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a shame perpetuàl.

<sup>67</sup> Moreover, he the tabernacle  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of Joseph did refuse;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The mighty tribe of Ephraim  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he would in no wise choose:

<sup>68</sup> But he did choose Jehudah’s tribe  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to be the rest above;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And of mount Zion he made choice,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which he so much did love.

<sup>69</sup> And he his sanctuary built  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;like to a palace high,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Like to the earth which he did found  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to perpetuity.

<sup>70</sup> Of David, that his servant was,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he also choice did make,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And even from the folds of sheep  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;was pleasèd him to take:

<sup>71</sup> From waiting on the ewes with young,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he brought him forth to feed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Israèl, his inheritance,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his people, Jacob’s seed.

<sup>72</sup> So after the integrity  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he of his heart them fed;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And by the good skill of his hands  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;them wisely governèd.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 79

*A Psalm of Asaph.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O God, the heathen entered have  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thine heritage; by them  
Defilèd is thy house: on heaps  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they laid Jerusalem.

<sup>2</sup> The bodies of thy servants they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;have cast forth to be meat  
To rav’nous fowls; thy dear saints’ flesh  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they gave to beasts to eat.

<sup>3</sup> Their blood about Jerusalem  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;like water they have shed;  
And there was none to bury them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when they were slain and dead.

<sup>4</sup> Unto our neighbours a reproach  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;most base become are we;  
A scorn and laughingstock to them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that round about us be.

<sup>5</sup> How long, LORD, shall thine anger last?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wilt thou still keep the same?  
And shall thy fervent jealousy  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;burn like unto a flame?

<sup>6</sup> On heathen pour thy fury forth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that have thee never known,  
And on those kingdoms which thy name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;have never called upon.

<sup>7</sup> For these are they who Jacob have  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;devourèd cruelly;  
And they his habitätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;have causèd waste to lie.

<sup>8</sup> Against us mind not former sins;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy tender mercies show;  
Let them prevent us speedily,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for we’re brought very low.

<sup>9</sup> For thy name’s glory help us, Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who hast our Saviour been:  
Deliver us; for thy name’s sake,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O purge away our sin.

<sup>10</sup> Why say the heathen, Where’s their God?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let him to them be known;  
When those who shed thy servants’ blood  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are in our sight o’erthrown.

<sup>11</sup> O let the pris’ner’s sighs ascend  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before thy sight on high;  
Preserve those in thy mighty pow’r  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that are designed to die.

<sup>12</sup> And to our neighbours’ bosom cause  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it sev’n-fold rendered be,  
Ev’n the reproach wherewith they have,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O Lord, reproachèd thee.

<sup>13</sup> So we thy folk, and pasture-sheep,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall give thee thanks always;  
And unto generations all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;we will show forth thy praise.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 80

*To the chief musician upon Shoshannim, Eduth, A Psalm of Asaph.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Hear, Isr’el’s Shepherd! like a flock  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou that dost Joseph guide;  
Shine forth, O thou that dost between  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the cherubims abide.

<sup>2</sup> In Ephraim’s and Benjamin’s,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and in Manasseh’s sight,  
O come for our salvätion;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;stir up thy strength and might.

<sup>3</sup> Turn us again, O Lord our God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and upon us vouchsafe  
To make thy countenance to shine,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and so we shall be safe.

<sup>4</sup> O LORD of hosts, almighty God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;how long shall kindled be  
Thy wrath against the prayer made  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by thine own folk to thee?

<sup>5</sup> Thou tears of sorrow giv’st to them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;instead of bread to eat;  
Yea, tears instead of drink thou giv’st  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to them in measure great.

<sup>6</sup> Thou makest us a strife unto  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our neighbours round about;  
Our enemies among themselves  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;at us do laugh and flout.

<sup>7</sup> Turn us again, O God of hosts,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and upon us vouchsafe  
To make thy countenance to shine,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and so we shall be safe.

<sup>8</sup> A vine from Egypt brought thou hast,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by thine outstretchèd hand;  
And thou the heathen out didst cast  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to plant it in their land.

<sup>9</sup> Before it thou a room didst make,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;where it might grow and stand;  
Thou causedst it deep root to take,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and it did fill the land.

<sup>10</sup> The mountains veiled were with its shade,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as with a covering;  
Like goodly cedars were the boughs  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which out from it did spring.

<sup>11</sup> Upon the one hand to the sea  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;her boughs she did out send;  
On th’ other side unto the flood  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;her branches did extend.

<sup>12</sup> Why hast thou then thus broken down,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and ta’en her hedge away?  
So that all passengers do pluck,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and make of her a prey.

<sup>13</sup> The boar who from the forest comes  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth waste it at his pleasure;  
The wild beast of the field also  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;devours it out of measure.

<sup>14</sup> O God of hosts, we thee beseech,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;return now unto thine;  
Look down from heav’n in love, behold,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and visit this thy vine:

<sup>15</sup> This vineyard, which thine own right hand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hath planted us among;  
And that same branch, which for thyself  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou hast made to be strong.

<sup>16</sup> Burnt up it is with flaming fire,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it also is cut down:  
They utterly are perishèd,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when as thy face doth frown.

<sup>17</sup> O let thy hand be still upon  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the Man of thy right hand,  
The Son of man, whom for thyself  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou madest strong to stand.

<sup>18</sup> So henceforth we will not go back,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor turn from thee at all:  
O do thou quicken us, and we  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon thy name will call.

<sup>19</sup> Turn us again, LORD God of hosts,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and upon us vouchsafe  
To make thy countenance to shine,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and so we shall be safe.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 81

*To the chief Musician upon Gittith, A Psalm of Asaph.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Sing loud to God our strength; with joy  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to Jacob’s God do sing.  
<sup>2</sup> Take up a psalm, the pleasant harp,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;timbrel and psalt’ry bring.

<sup>3</sup> Blow trumpets at new-moon, what day  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our feast appointed is:  
<sup>4</sup> For charge to Isr’el, and a law  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of Jacob’s God was this.

<sup>5</sup> To Joseph this a test’mony  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he made, when Egypt land  
He travelled through, where speech I heard  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I did not understand.

<sup>6</sup> His shoulder I from burdens took,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his hands from pots did free.  
<sup>7</sup> Thou didst in trouble on me call,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and I delivered thee:

In secret place of thundering  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I did thee answer make;  
And at the streams of Meribah  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of thee a proof did take.

<sup>8</sup> O thou, my people, give an ear,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I’ll testify to thee;  
To thee, O Isr’el, if thou wilt  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but hearken unto me.

<sup>9</sup> In midst of thee there shall not be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;any strange god at all;  
Nor unto any god unknown  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou bowing down shalt fall.

<sup>10</sup> I am the LORD thy God, which did  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from Egypt land thee guide;  
I’ll fill thy mouth abundantly,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do thou it open wide.

<sup>11</sup> But yet my people to my voice  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;would not attentive be;  
And ev’n my chosen Israel  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he would have none of me.

<sup>12</sup> So to the lust of their own hearts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I them deliverèd;  
And then in counsels of their own  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they vainly wanderèd.

<sup>13</sup> O that my people had me heard,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Isr’el my ways had chose!  
<sup>14</sup> I had their en’mies soon subdued,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my hand turned on their foes.

<sup>15</sup> The haters of the LORD to him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;submission should have feigned;  
But as for them, their time should have  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for evermore remained.

<sup>16</sup> He should have also fed them with  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the finest of the wheat;  
Of honey from the rock thy fill  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I should have made thee eat.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 82

*A Psalm of Asaph.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> In gods’ assembly God doth stand;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he judgeth gods among.  
<sup>2</sup> How long, accepting persons vile,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;will ye give judgment wrong?

<sup>3</sup> Defend the poor and fatherless;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to poor oppressed do right.  
<sup>4</sup> The poor and needy ones set free;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;rid them from ill men’s might.

<sup>5</sup> They know not, nor will understand;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in darkness they walk on:  
All the foundations of the earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;out of their course are gone.

<sup>6</sup> I said that ye are gods, and are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sons of the Highest all:  
<sup>7</sup> But ye shall die like men, and as  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;one of the princes fall.

<sup>8</sup> O God, do thou raise up thyself,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the earth to judgment call:  
For thou, as thine inheritance,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shalt take the nations all.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 83

*A Song or Psalm of Asaph.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Keep not, O God, we thee entreat,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O keep not silence now:  
Do thou not hold thy peace, O God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and still no more be thou.

<sup>2</sup> For, lo, thine enemies a noise  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;tumultuously have made;  
And they that haters are of thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;have lifted up the head.

<sup>3</sup> Against thy chosen people they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do crafty counsel take:  
And they against thy hidden ones  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do consultations make.

<sup>4</sup> Come, let us cut them off, said they,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from being a nätion,  
That of the name of Isr’el may  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;no more be mëntion.

<sup>5</sup> For with joint heart they plot, in league  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;against thee they combine.  
<sup>6</sup> The tents of Edom, Ishm’elites,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Moab’s and Hagar’s line;

<sup>7</sup> Gebal, and Ammon, Amalek,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Philistines, those of Tyre;  
<sup>8</sup> And Assur joined with them, to help  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Lot’s children they conspire.

<sup>9</sup> Do to them as to Midian,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Jabin at Kison strand;  
<sup>10</sup> And Sis’ra, which at En-dor fell,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as dung to fat the land.

<sup>11</sup> Like Oreb and like Zeèb make  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their noble men to fall;  
Like Zeba and Zalmunna like,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;make thou their princes all;

<sup>12</sup> Who said, For our possëssion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let us God’s houses take.  
<sup>13</sup> My God, them like a wheel, as chaff  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before the wind, them make.

<sup>14</sup> As fire consumes the wood, as flame  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth mountains set on fire,  
<sup>15</sup> Chase and affright them with the storm  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and tempest of thine ire.

<sup>16</sup> Their faces fill with shame, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that they may seek thy name.  
<sup>17</sup> Let them confounded be, and vexed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and perish in their shame:

<sup>18</sup> That men may know that thou, to whom  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;alone doth appertain  
The name JEHOVAH, dost most high  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;o’er all the earth remain.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 84

*To the chief Musician upon Gittith, A Psalm for the sons of Korah.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> How lovely is thy dwelling-place,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O LORD of hosts, to me!  
The tabernacles of thy grace  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;how pleasant, LORD, they be!

<sup>2</sup> My thirsty soul longs veh’mently,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;yea faints, thy courts to see:  
My very heart and flesh cry out,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O living God, for thee.

<sup>3</sup> Behold, the sparrow findeth out  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;an house wherein to rest;  
The swallow also for herself  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hath purchasèd a nest;

Ev’n thine own altars, where she safe  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;her young ones forth may bring,  
O thou almighty LORD of hosts,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who art my God and King.

<sup>4</sup> Bless’d are they in thy house that dwell,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they ever give thee praise.  
<sup>5</sup> Bless’d is the man whose strength thou art,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in whose heart are thy ways:

<sup>6</sup> Who passing thorough Baca’s vale,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;therein do dig up wells;  
Also the rain that falleth down  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the pools with water fills.

<sup>7</sup> So they from strength unwearied go  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;still forward unto strength,  
Until in Zion they appear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before the Lord at length.

<sup>8</sup> LORD God of hosts, my prayèr hear;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O Jacob’s God, give ear.  
<sup>9</sup> See God our shield, look on the face  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of thine anointed dear.

<sup>10</sup> For in thy courts one day excels  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a thousand; rather in  
My God’s house will I keep a door,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;than dwell in tents of sin.

<sup>11</sup> For God the LORD’s a sun and shield:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he’ll grace and glory give;  
And will withhold no good from them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that uprightly do live.

<sup>12</sup> O thou that art the LORD of hosts,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that man is truly blessed,  
Who by assured confidence  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on thee alone doth rest.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 85

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm for the sons of Korah.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O LORD, thou hast been fav’rable  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to thy belovèd land:  
Jacob’s captivity thou hast  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;recalled with mighty hand.

<sup>2</sup> Thou pardonèd thy people hast  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all their iniquities;  
Thou all their trespasses and sins  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hast covered from thine eyes.

<sup>3</sup> Thou took’st off all thine ire, and turn’dst  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from thy wrath’s furiousness.  
<sup>4</sup> Turn us, God of our health, and cause  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy wrath ’gainst us to cease.

<sup>5</sup> Shall thy displeasure thus endure  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;against us without end?  
Wilt thou to generations all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thine anger forth extend?

<sup>6</sup> That in thee may thy people joy,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wilt thou not us revive?  
<sup>7</sup> Show us thy mercy, LORD, to us  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do thy salvation give.

<sup>8</sup> I’ll hear what God the LORD will speak:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to his folk he’ll speak peace,  
And to his saints; but let them not  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;return to foolishness.

<sup>9</sup> To them that fear him surely near  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is his salvätion;  
That glory in our land may have  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;her habitätion.

<sup>10</sup> Truth met with mercy, righteousness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and peace kissed mutually:  
<sup>11</sup> Truth springs from earth, and righteousness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;looks down from heaven high.

<sup>12</sup> Yea, what is good the LORD shall give;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our land shall yield increase:  
<sup>13</sup> Justice, to set us in his steps,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall go before his face.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 86

*A Prayer of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O LORD, do thou bow down thine ear,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and hear me graciously;  
Because I sore afflicted am,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and am in poverty.

<sup>2</sup> Because I’m holy, let my soul  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by thee preservèd be:  
O thou my God, thy servant save,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that puts his trust in thee.

<sup>3</sup> Sith unto thee I daily cry,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be merciful to me.  
<sup>4</sup> Rejoice thy servant’s soul; for, Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I lift my soul to thee.

<sup>5</sup> For thou art gräcious, O Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and ready to forgive;  
And rich in mercy, all that call  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon thee to relieve.

<sup>6</sup> Hear, LORD, my pray’r; unto the voice  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of my request attend:  
<sup>7</sup> In troublous times I’ll call on thee;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for thou wilt answer send.

<sup>8</sup> Lord, there is none among the gods  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that may with thee compare;  
And like the works which thou hast done,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;not any work is there.

<sup>9</sup> All nations whom thou mad’st shall come  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and worship rev’rently  
Before thy face; and they, O Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy name shall glorify.

<sup>10</sup> Because thou art exceeding great,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and works by thee are done  
Which are to be admired; and thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;art God thyself alone.

<sup>11</sup> Teach me thy way, and in thy truth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O Lord, then walk will I;  
Unite my heart, that I thy name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;may fear continually.

<sup>12</sup> O Lord my God, with all my heart  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to thee I will give praise;  
And I the glory will ascribe  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto thy name always:

<sup>13</sup> Because thy mercy toward me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in greatness doth excel;  
And thou delivered hast my soul  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;out from the lowest hell.

<sup>14</sup> O God, the proud against me rise,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and vi’lent men have met,  
That for my soul have sought; and thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before them have not set.

<sup>15</sup> But thou art full of pity, Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a God most gräcious,  
Long-suffering, and in thy truth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and mercy plentèous.

<sup>16</sup> O turn to me thy countenance,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and mercy on me have;  
Thy servant strengthen, and the son  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of thine own handmaid save.

<sup>17</sup> Show me a sign for good, that they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which do me hate may see,  
And be ashamed; because thou, LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;didst help and comfort me.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 87

*A Psalm or Song for the sons of Korah.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Upon the hills of holiness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he his foundation sets.  
<sup>2</sup> GOD, more than Jacob’s dwellings all,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;delights in Zion’s gates.

<sup>3</sup> Things glorious are said of thee,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou city of the Lord.  
<sup>4</sup> Rahab and Babel I, to those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that know me, will record:

Behold ev’n Tyrus, and with it  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the land of Palestine,  
And likewise Ethiopia;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;this man was born therein.

<sup>5</sup> And it of Zion shall be said,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This man and that man there  
Was born; and he that is most High  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;himself shall stablish her.

<sup>6</sup> When GOD the people writes, he’ll count  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that this man born was there.  
<sup>7</sup> There be that sing and play; and all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my well-springs in thee are.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 88

*A Song or Psalm for the sons of Korah, to the chief Musician upon Mahalath Leannoth, Maschil of Heman the Ezrahite.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> LORD God, my Saviour, day and night  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before thee cried have I.  
<sup>2</sup> Before thee let my prayèr come;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;give ear unto my cry.

<sup>3</sup> For troubles great do fill my soul;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my life draws nigh the grave.  
<sup>4</sup> I’m counted with those that go down  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to pit, and no strength have.

<sup>5</sup> Ev’n free among the dead, like them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that slain in grave do lie;  
Cut off from thy hand, whom no more  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou hast in memory.

<sup>6</sup> Thou hast me laid in lowest pit,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in deeps and darksome caves.  
<sup>7</sup> Thy wrath lies hard on me, thou hast  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;me pressed with all thy waves.

<sup>8</sup> Thou hast put far from me my friends,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou mad’st them to abhor me;  
And I am so shut up, that I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;find no evasion for me.

<sup>9</sup> By reason of afflïction  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mine eye mourns dolefully:  
To thee, LORD, do I call, and stretch  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my hands continually.

<sup>10</sup> Wilt thou show wonders to the dead?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall they rise, and thee bless?  
<sup>11</sup> Shall in the grave thy love be told?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in death thy faithfulness?

<sup>12</sup> Shall thy great wonders in the dark,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;or shall thy righteousness  
Be known to any in the land  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of deep forgetfulness?

<sup>13</sup> But, LORD, to thee I cried; my pray’r  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;at morn prevent shall thee.  
<sup>14</sup> Why, LORD, dost thou cast off my soul,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and hid’st thy face from me?

<sup>15</sup> Distressed am I, and from my youth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I ready am to die;  
Thy terrors I have borne, and am  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;distracted fearfully.

<sup>16</sup> The dreadful fierceness of thy wrath  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;quite over me doth go:  
Thy terrors great have cut me off,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they did pursue me so.

<sup>17</sup> For round about me ev’ry day,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;like water, they did roll;  
And, gathering together, they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;have compassèd my soul.

<sup>18</sup> My friends thou hast put far from me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and him that did me love;  
And those that mine acquaintance were  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to darkness didst remove.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 89

*Maschil of Ethan the Ezrahite.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> GOD’s mercies I will ever sing;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and with my mouth I shall  
Thy faithfulness make to be known  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to generations all.

<sup>2</sup> For mercy shall be built, said I,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for ever to endure;  
Thy faithfulness, ev’n in the heav’ns,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou wilt establish sure.

<sup>3</sup> I with my chosen One have made  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a cov’nant graciously;  
And to my servant, whom I loved,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to David sworn have I;

<sup>4</sup> That I thy seed establish shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for ever to remain,  
And will to generations all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy throne build and maintain.

<sup>5</sup> The praises of thy wonders, LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the heavens shall express;  
And in the congregätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of saints thy faithfulness.

<sup>6</sup> For who in heaven with the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;may once himself compare?  
Who is like GOD among the sons  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of those that mighty are?

<sup>7</sup> Great fear in meeting of the saints  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is due unto the Lord;  
And he of all about him should  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with rev’rence be adored.

<sup>8</sup> O thou that art the LORD of hosts,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;what Lord in mightiness  
Is like to thee? who compassed round  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;art with thy faithfulness.

<sup>9</sup> Ev’n in the raging of the sea  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou over it dost reign;  
And when the waves thereof do swell,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou stillest them again.

<sup>10</sup> Rahab in pieces thou didst break,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;like one that slaughtered is;  
And with thy mighty arm thou hast  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;dispersed thine enemies.

<sup>11</sup> The heav’ns are thine, thou for thine own  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the earth dost also take;  
The world, and fulness of the same,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy pow’r did found and make.

<sup>12</sup> The north and south from thee alone  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their first beginning had;  
Both Tabor mount and Hermon hill  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall in thy name be glad.

<sup>13</sup> Thou hast an arm that’s full of pow’r,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy hand is great in might;  
And thy right hand exceedingly  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;exalted is in height.

<sup>14</sup> Justice and judgment of thy throne  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are made the dwelling-place;  
Mercy, accompanied with truth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall go before thy face.

<sup>15</sup> O greatly blessed the people are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the joyful sound that know;  
In brightness of thy face, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they ever on shall go.

<sup>16</sup> They in thy name shall all the day  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;rejoice exceedingly;  
And in thy righteousness shall they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;exalted be on high.

<sup>17</sup> Because the glory of their strength  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth only stand in thee;  
And in thy favour shall our horn  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and pow’r exalted be.

<sup>18</sup> For GOD is our defence; and he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to us doth safety bring:  
The Holy One of Israel  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is our almighty King.

<sup>19</sup> In vision to thy Holy One  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou saidst, I help upon  
A strong one laid; out of the folk  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I raised a chosen one;

<sup>20</sup> Ev’n David, I have found him out  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a servant unto me;  
And with my holy oil my King  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;anointed him to be.

<sup>21</sup> With whom my hand shall stablished be;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mine arm shall make him strong.  
<sup>22</sup> On him the foe shall not exact,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor son of mischief wrong.

<sup>23</sup> I will beat down before his face  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all his malicious foes;  
I will them greatly plague who do  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with hatred him oppose.

<sup>24</sup> My mercy and my faithfulness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with him yet still shall be;  
And in my name his horn and pow’r  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;men shall exalted see.

<sup>25</sup> His hand and pow’r shall reach afar;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I’ll set it in the sea;  
And his right hand establishèd  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall in the rivers be.

<sup>26</sup> Thou art my Father, he shall cry,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou art my God alone;  
And he shall say, Thou art the Rock  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of my salvätion.

<sup>27</sup> I’ll make him my first-born, more high  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;than kings of any land.  
<sup>28</sup> My love I’ll ever keep for him,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my cov’nant fast shall stand.

<sup>29</sup> His seed I by my pow’r will make  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for ever to endure;  
And, as the days of heav’n, his throne  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall stable be, and sure.

<sup>30</sup> But if his children shall forsake  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my laws, and go astray,  
And in my judgments shall not walk,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but wander from my way:

<sup>31</sup> If they my laws break, and do not  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;keep my commändments;  
<sup>32</sup> I’ll visit then their faults with rods,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their sins with chastisements.

<sup>33</sup> Yet I’ll not take my love from him,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor false my promise make.  
<sup>34</sup> My cov’nant I’ll not break, nor change  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;what with my mouth I spake.

<sup>35</sup> Once by my holiness I sware,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to David I’ll not lie;  
<sup>36</sup> His seed and throne shall, as the sun,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before me last for aye.

<sup>37</sup> It, like the moon, shall ever be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;established steadfastly;  
And like to that which in the heav’n  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth witness faithfully.

<sup>38</sup> But thou, displeasèd, hast cast off,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou didst abhor and loathe;  
With him that thine anointed is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou hast been very wroth.

<sup>39</sup> Thou hast thy servant’s covenant  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;made void, and quite cast by;  
Thou hast profaned his crown, while it  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cast on the ground doth lie.

<sup>40</sup> Thou all his hedges hast broke down,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his strongholds down hast torn.  
<sup>41</sup> He to all passers-by a spoil,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to neighbours is a scorn.

<sup>42</sup> Thou hast set up his foes’ right hand;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mad’st all his en’mies glad:  
<sup>43</sup> Turned his sword’s edge, and him to stand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in battle hast not made.

<sup>44</sup> His glory thou hast made to cease,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his throne to ground down cast;  
<sup>45</sup> Shortened his days of youth, and him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with shame thou covered hast.

<sup>46</sup> How long, LORD, wilt thou hide thyself?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for ever, in thine ire?  
And shall thine indignation  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;burn like unto a fire?

<sup>47</sup> Remember, Lord, how short a time  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I shall on earth remain:  
O wherefore is it so that thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hast made all men in vain?

<sup>48</sup> What man is he that liveth here,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and death shall never see?  
Or from the powèr of the grave  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;what man his soul shall free?

<sup>49</sup> Thy former loving-kindnesses,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O Lord, where be they now?  
Those which in truth and faithfulness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to David sworn hast thou?

<sup>50</sup> Mind, Lord, thy servant’s sad reproach;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;how I in bosom bear  
The scornings of the people all,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who strong and mighty are.

<sup>51</sup> Wherewith thy raging enemies  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;reproached, O LORD, think on;  
Wherewith they have reproached the steps  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of thine anointed one.

<sup>52</sup> All blessing to the LORD our God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let be ascribèd then:  
For evermore so let it be.  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Amen, yea, and amen.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)
