# Book IV

*Psalms 90&ndash;106*

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 90

*A Prayer of Moses the man of God.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Lord, thou hast been our dwelling-place  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in generations all.  
<sup>2</sup> Before thou ever hadst brought forth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the mountains great or small;

Ere ever thou hadst formed the earth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and all the world abroad;  
Ev’n thou from everlasting art  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to everlasting God.

<sup>3</sup> Thou dost unto destrüction  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;man that is mortal turn;  
And unto them thou say’st, Again,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ye sons of men, return.

<sup>4</sup> Because a thousand years appear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;no more before thy sight  
Than yesterday, when it is past,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;or than a watch by night.

<sup>5</sup> As with an overflowing flood  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou carriest them away:  
They like a sleep are, like the grass  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that grows at morn are they.

<sup>6</sup> At morn it flourishes and grows,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cut down at ev’n doth fade.  
<sup>7</sup> For by thine anger we’re consumed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy wrath makes us afraid.

<sup>8</sup> Our sins thou and iniquities  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;dost in thy presence place,  
And sett’st our secret faults before  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the brightness of thy face.

<sup>9</sup> For in thine anger all our days  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do pass on to an end;  
And as a tale that hath been told,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;so we our years do spend.

<sup>10</sup> Threescore and ten years do sum up  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our days and years, we see;  
Or if, by reason of more strength,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in some fourscore they be:

Yet doth the strength of such old men  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but grief and labour prove;  
For it is soon cut off, and we  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;fly hence, and soon remove.

<sup>11</sup> Who knows the powèr of thy wrath?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;according to thy fear  
<sup>12</sup> So is thy wrath: Lord, teach thou us  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our end in mind to bear;

And so to count our days, that we  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our hearts may still apply  
To learn thy wisdom and thy truth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that we may live thereby.

<sup>13</sup> Turn yet again to us, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;how long thus shall it be?  
Let it repent thee now for those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that servants are to thee.

<sup>14</sup> O with thy tender mercies, Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;us early satisfy;  
So we rejoice shall all our days,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and still be glad in thee.

<sup>15</sup> According as the days have been,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wherein we grief have had,  
And years wherein we ill have seen,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;so do thou make us glad.

<sup>16</sup> O let thy work and pow’r appear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy servants’ face before;  
And show unto their children dear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy glory evermore:

<sup>17</sup> And let the beauty of the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our God be us upon:  
Our handiworks establish thou,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;establish them each one.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 91

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> He that doth in the secret place  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of the most High reside,  
Under the shade of him that is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;th’ Almighty shall abide.

<sup>2</sup> I of the LORD my God will say,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;He is my refuge still,  
He is my fortress, and my God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and in him trust I will.

<sup>3</sup> Assuredly he shall thee save,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and give deliverance  
From subtle fowler’s snare, and from  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the noisome pestilence.

<sup>4</sup> His feathers shall thee hide; thy trust  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;under his wings shall be:  
His faithfulness shall be a shield  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and buckler unto thee.

<sup>5</sup> Thou shalt not need to be afraid  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for terrors of the night;  
Nor for the arrow that doth fly  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by day, while it is light;

<sup>6</sup> Nor for the pestilence, that walks  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in darkness secretly;  
Nor for destruction, that doth waste  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;at noon-day openly.

<sup>7</sup> A thousand at thy side shall fall,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on thy right hand shall lie  
Ten thousand dead; yet unto thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it shall not once come nigh.

<sup>8</sup> Only thou with thine eyes shalt look,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and a beholder be;  
And thou therein the just reward  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of wicked men shalt see.

<sup>9</sup> Because the LORD, who constantly  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my refuge is alone,  
Ev’n the most High, is made by thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy habitätion;

<sup>10</sup> No plague shall near thy dwelling come;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;no ill shall thee befall:  
<sup>11</sup> For thee to keep in all thy ways  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his angels charge he shall.

<sup>12</sup> They in their hands shall bear thee up,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;still waiting thee upon;  
Lest thou at any time should’st dash  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy foot against a stone.

<sup>13</sup> Upon the adder thou shalt tread,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and on the lion strong;  
Thy feet on dragons trample shall,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and on the lions young.

<sup>14</sup> Because on me he set his love,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I’ll save and set him free;  
Because my great name he hath known,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I will him set on high.

<sup>15</sup> He’ll call on me, I’ll answer him;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I will be with him still  
In trouble, to deliver him,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and honour him I will.

<sup>16</sup> With length of days unto his mind  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I will him satisfy;  
I also my salvätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;will cause his eyes to see.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 92

*A Psalm or Song for the sabbath day.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> To render thanks unto the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it is a comely thing,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And to thy name, O thou most High,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;due praise aloud to sing.

<sup>2</sup> Thy loving-kindness to show forth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when shines the morning light;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And to declare thy faithfulness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with pleasure ev’ry night,

<sup>3</sup> On a ten-stringèd instrument,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon the psaltery,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And on the harp with solemn sound,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and grave sweet melody.

<sup>4</sup> For thou, LORD, by thy mighty works  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hast made my heart right glad;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And I will triumph in the works  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which by thine hands were made.

<sup>5</sup> How great, LORD, are thy works! each  
thought  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of thine a deep it is:  
<sup>6</sup> A brutish man it knoweth not;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;fools understand not this.

<sup>7</sup> When those that lewd and wicked are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;spring quickly up like grass,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And workers of iniquity  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do flourish all apace;

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;It is that they for ever may  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;destroyèd be and slain:  
<sup>8</sup> But thou, O LORD, art the most High,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for ever to remain.

<sup>9</sup> For, lo, thine enemies, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thine en’mies perish shall;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The workers of iniquity  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be dispersèd all.

<sup>10</sup> But thou shalt, like unto the horn  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of th’ unicorn, exalt  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;My horn on high: thou with fresh oil  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;anoint me also shalt.

<sup>11</sup> Mine eyes shall also my desire  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;see on mine enemies;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Mine ears shall of the wicked hear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that do against me rise.

<sup>12</sup> But like the palm-tree flourishing  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be the righteous one;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;He shall like to the cedar grow  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that is in Lebanon.

<sup>13</sup> Those that within the house of GOD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are planted by his grace,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;They shall grow up, and flourish all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in our God’s holy place.

<sup>14</sup> And in old age, when others fade,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they fruit still forth shall bring;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;They shall be fat, and full of sap,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and aye be flourishing;

<sup>15</sup> To show that upright is the LORD:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he is a rock to me;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And he from all unrighteousness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is altogether free.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 93

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> The LORD doth reign, and clothed is he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with majesty most bright;  
His works do show him clothed to be,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and girt about with might.

The world is also stablishèd,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that it cannot depart.  
<sup>2</sup> Thy throne is fixed of old, and thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from everlasting art.

<sup>3</sup> The floods, O LORD, have lifted up,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they lifted up their voice;  
The floods have lifted up their waves,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and made a mighty noise.

<sup>4</sup> But yet the LORD, that is on high,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is more of might by far  
Than noise of many waters is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;or great sea-billows are.

<sup>5</sup> Thy testimonies every one  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in faithfulness excel;  
And holiness for ever, LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thine house becometh well.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 94

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O LORD God, unto whom alone  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all vengeance doth belong;  
O mighty God, who vengeance own’st,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shine forth, avenging wrong.

<sup>2</sup> Lift up thyself, thou of the earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the sov’reign Judge that art;  
And unto those that are so proud  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a due reward impart.

<sup>3</sup> How long, O mighty GOD, shall they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who lewd and wicked be,  
How long shall they who wicked are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thus triumph haughtily?

<sup>4</sup> How long shall things most hard by them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be utterèd and told?  
And all that work iniquity  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to boast themselves be bold?

<sup>5</sup> Thy folk they break in pieces, LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thine heritage oppress:  
<sup>6</sup> The widow they and stranger slay,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and kill the fatherless.

<sup>7</sup> Yet say they, GOD it shall not see  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor God of Jacob know.  
<sup>8</sup> Ye brutish people! understand;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;fools! when wise will ye grow?

<sup>9</sup> The Lord did plant the ear of man,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and hear then shall not he?  
He only formed the eye, and then  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall he not clearly see?

<sup>10</sup> He that the nations doth correct,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall he not chastise you?  
He knowledge unto man doth teach,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and shall himself not know?

<sup>11</sup> Man’s thoughts to be but vanity  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD doth well discern.  
<sup>12</sup> Bless’d is the man thou chast’nest, LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and mak’st thy law to learn:

<sup>13</sup> That thou may’st give him rest from days  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of sad adversity,  
Until the pit be digged for those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that work iniquity.

<sup>14</sup> For sure the LORD will not cast off  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;those that his people be,  
Neither his own inheritance  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;quit and forsake will he:

<sup>15</sup> But judgment unto righteousness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall yet return again;  
And all shall follow after it  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that are right-hearted men.

<sup>16</sup> Who will rise up for me against  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;those that do wickedly?  
Who will stand up for me ’gainst those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that work iniquity?

<sup>17</sup> Unless the LORD had been my help  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when I was sore oppressed,  
Almost my soul had in the house  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of silence been at rest.

<sup>18</sup> When I had utterèd this word,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(my foot doth slip away),  
Thy mercy held me up, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy goodness did me stay.

<sup>19</sup> Amidst the multitude of thoughts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which in my heart do fight,  
My soul, lest it be overcharged,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy comforts do delight.

<sup>20</sup> Shall of iniquity the throne  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;have fellowship with thee,  
Which mischief, cunningly contrived,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth by a law decree?

<sup>21</sup> Against the righteous souls they join,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they guiltless blood condemn.  
<sup>22</sup> But of my refuge God’s the rock,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and my defence from them.

<sup>23</sup> On them their own iniquity  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the Lord shall bring and lay,  
And cut them off in their own sin;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our LORD God shall them slay.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 95

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O come, let us sing to the LORD:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;come, let us every one  
A joyful noise make to the Rock  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of our salvätion.

<sup>2</sup> Let us before his presence come  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with praise and thankful voice;  
Let us sing psalms to him with grace,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and make a joyful noise.

<sup>3</sup> For GOD, a great God, and great King,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;above all gods he is.  
<sup>4</sup> Depths of the earth are in his hand,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the strength of hills is his.

<sup>5</sup> To him the spacious sea belongs,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for he the same did make;  
The dry land also from his hands  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;its form at first did take.

<sup>6</sup> O come, and let us worship him,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let us bow down withal,  
And on our knees before the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our Maker let us fall.

<sup>7</sup> For he’s our God, the people we  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of his own pasture are,  
And of his hand the sheep; to-day,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;if ye his voice will hear,

<sup>8</sup> Then harden not your hearts, as in  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the provocätion,  
As in the desert, on the day  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of the tentätion:

<sup>9</sup> When me your fathers tempt’d and proved,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and did my working see;  
<sup>10</sup> Ev’n for the space of forty years  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;this race hath grievèd me.

I said, This people errs in heart,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my ways they do not know:  
<sup>11</sup> To whom I sware in wrath, that to  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my rest they should not go.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 96

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O sing a new song to the LORD:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sing all the earth to GOD.  
<sup>2</sup> To GOD sing, bless his name, show still  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his saving health abroad.

<sup>3</sup> Among the heathen nätions  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his glory do declare;  
And unto all the people show  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his works that wondrous are.

<sup>4</sup> For great’s the LORD, and greatly he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is to be magnified;  
Yea, worthy to be feared is he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;above all gods beside.

<sup>5</sup> For all the gods are idols dumb,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which blinded nations fear;  
But our God is the LORD, by whom  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the heav’ns created were.

<sup>6</sup> Great honour is before his face,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and majesty divine;  
Strength is within his holy place,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and there doth beauty shine.

<sup>7</sup> Do ye ascribe unto the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of people ev’ry tribe,  
Glory do ye unto the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and mighty pow’r ascribe.

<sup>8</sup> Give ye the glory to the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that to his name is due;  
Come ye into his courts, and bring  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;an offering with you.

<sup>9</sup> In beauty of his holiness,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O do the LORD adore;  
Likewise let all the earth throughout  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;tremble his face before.

<sup>10</sup> Among the heathen say, GOD reigns;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the world shall steadfastly  
Be fixed from moving; he shall judge  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the people righteously.

<sup>11</sup> Let heav’ns be glad before the Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and let the earth rejoice;  
Let seas, and all that is therein,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cry out, and make a noise.

<sup>12</sup> Let fields rejoice, and everything  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that springeth of the earth:  
Then woods and ev’ry tree shall sing  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with gladness and with mirth

<sup>13</sup> Before the LORD; because he comes,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to judge the earth comes he:  
He’ll judge the world with righteousness,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the people faithfully.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 97

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> GOD reigneth, let the earth be glad,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and isles rejoice each one.  
<sup>2</sup> Dark clouds him compass; and in right  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with judgment dwells his throne.

<sup>3</sup> Fire goes before him, and his foes  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it burns up round about:  
<sup>4</sup> His lightnings lighten did the world;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;earth saw, and shook throughout.

<sup>5</sup> Hills at the presence of the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;like wax, did melt away;  
Ev’n at the presence of the Lord  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of all the earth, I say.

<sup>6</sup> The heav’ns declare his righteousness,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all men his glory see.  
<sup>7</sup> All who serve graven images,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;confounded let them be.

Who do of idols boast themselves,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let shame upon them fall:  
Ye that are callèd gods, see that  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ye do him worship all.

<sup>8</sup> Zion did hear, and joyful was,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;glad Judah’s daughters were;  
They much rejoiced, O LORD, because  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy judgments did appear.

<sup>9</sup> For thou, O LORD, art high above  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all things on earth that are;  
Above all other gods thou art  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;exalted very far.

<sup>10</sup> Hate ill, all ye that love the LORD:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his saints’ souls keepeth he;  
And from the hands of wicked men  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he sets them safe and free.

<sup>11</sup> For all those that be rïghteous  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sown is a joyful light,  
And gladness sown is for all those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that are in heart upright.

<sup>12</sup> Ye righteous, in the LORD rejoice;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;express your thankfulness,  
When ye into your memory  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do call his holiness.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 98

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O sing a new song to the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for wonders he hath done:  
His right hand and his holy arm  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;him victory hath won.

<sup>2</sup> The LORD God his salvätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hath causèd to be known;  
His justice in the heathen’s sight  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he openly hath shown.

<sup>3</sup> He mindful of his grace and truth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to Isr’el’s house hath been;  
And the salvation of our God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all ends of th’ earth have seen.

<sup>4</sup> Let all the earth unto the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;send forth a joyful noise;  
Lift up your voice aloud to him,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sing praises, and rejoice.

<sup>5</sup> With harp, with harp, and voice of psalms,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto JEHOVAH sing:  
<sup>6</sup> With trumpets, cornets, gladly sound  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before the LORD the King.

<sup>7</sup> Let seas and all their fulness roar;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the world, and dwellers there;  
<sup>8</sup> Let floods clap hands, and let the hills  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;together joy declare

<sup>9</sup> Before the LORD; because he comes,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to judge the earth comes he:  
He’ll judge the world with righteousness,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his folk with equity.

## Psalm 99

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Th’ eternal LORD doth reign as king,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let all the people quake;  
He sits between the cherubims,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let th’ earth be mov’d and shake.

<sup>2</sup> The LORD in Zion great and high  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;above all people is;  
<sup>3</sup> Thy great and dreadful name (for it  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is holy) let them bless.

<sup>4</sup> The king’s strength also judgment loves;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou settlest equity:  
Just judgment thou dost execute  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in Jacob righteously.

<sup>5</sup> The LORD our God exalt on high,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and rev’rently do ye  
Before his footstool worship him:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the Holy One is he.

<sup>6</sup> Moses and Aaron ’mong his priests,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Samuel, with them that call  
Upon his name: these called on GOD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and he them answered all.

<sup>7</sup> Within the pillar of the cloud  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he unto them did speak:  
The testimonies he them taught,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and laws, they did not break.

<sup>8</sup> Thou answer’dst them, O LORD our God;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou wast a God that gave  
Pardon to them, though on their deeds  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou wouldest vengeance have.

<sup>9</sup> Do ye exalt the LORD our God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and at his holy hill  
Do ye him worship: for the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our God is holy still.

## Psalm 100

*A Psalm of praise.*

### Version 1

*L.M.*

<sup>1</sup> All people that on earth do dwell,  
Sing to the LORD with cheerful voice.  
<sup>2</sup> Him serve with mirth, his praise forth tell,  
Come ye before him and rejoice.

<sup>3</sup> Know that the LORD is God indeed;  
Without our aid he did us make:  
We are his flock, he doth us feed,  
And for his sheep he doth us take.

<sup>4</sup> O enter then his gates with praise,  
Approach with joy his courts unto:  
Praise, laud, and bless his name always,  
For it is seemly so to do.

<sup>5</sup> For why? the LORD our God is good,  
His mercy is for ever sure;  
His truth at all times firmly stood,  
And shall from age to age endure.

---

### Version 2

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O all ye lands, unto the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;make ye a joyful noise.  
<sup>2</sup> Serve GOD with gladness, him before  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;come with a singing voice.

<sup>3</sup> Know ye the LORD that he is God;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;not we, but he us made:  
We are his people, and the sheep  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within his pasture fed.

<sup>4</sup> Enter his gates and courts with praise,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to thank him go ye thither:  
To him express your thankfulness,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and bless his name together.

<sup>5</sup> Because the LORD our God is good,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his mercy faileth never;  
And to all generätions  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his truth endureth ever.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 101

*A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> I mercy will and judgment sing,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;LORD, I will sing to thee.  
<sup>2</sup> With wisdom in a perfect way  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall my behaviour be.

O when, in kindness unto me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wilt thou be pleased to come?  
I with a perfect heart will walk  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within my house at home.

<sup>3</sup> I will endure no wicked thing  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before mine eyes to be:  
I hate their work that turn aside,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it shall not cleave to me.

<sup>4</sup> A stubborn and a froward heart  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;depart quite from me shall;  
A person giv’n to wickedness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I will not know at all.

<sup>5</sup> I’ll cut him off that slandereth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his neighbour privily:  
The haughty heart I will not bear,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor him that looketh high.

<sup>6</sup> Upon the faithful of the land  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mine eyes shall be, that they  
May dwell with me: he shall me serve  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that walks in perfect way.

<sup>7</sup> Who of deceit a worker is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in my house shall not dwell;  
And in my presence shall he not  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;remain that lies doth tell.

<sup>8</sup> Yea, all the wicked of the land  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;early destroy will I;  
All from GOD’s city to cut off  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that work iniquity.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 102

*A Prayer of the afflicted, when he is overwhelmed, and poureth out his complaint before the Lord.*

### Version 1

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O LORD, unto my pray’r give ear,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my cry let come to thee;  
<sup>2</sup> And in the day of my distress  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hide not thy face from me.

Give ear to me; what time I call,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to answer me make haste:  
<sup>3</sup> For, as an hearth, my bones are burnt,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my days, like smoke, do waste.

<sup>4</sup> My heart within me smitten is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and it is witherèd  
Like very grass; so that I do  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;forget to eat my bread.

<sup>5</sup> By reason of my groaning voice  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my bones cleave to my skin.  
<sup>6</sup> Like pelican in wilderness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;forsaken I have been:

I like an owl in desert am,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that nightly there doth moan;  
<sup>7</sup> I watch, and like a sparrow am  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on the house-top alone.

<sup>8</sup> My bitter en’mies all the day  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;reproaches cast on me;  
And, being mad at me, with rage  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;against me sworn they be.

<sup>9</sup> For why? I ashes eaten have  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;like bread, in sorrows deep;  
My drink I also mingled have  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with tears that I did weep.

<sup>10</sup> Thy wrath and indignätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did cause this grief and pain;  
For thou hast lift me up on high,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and cast me down again.

<sup>11</sup> My days are like unto a shade,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which doth declining pass;  
And I am dried and witherèd,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n like unto the grass.

<sup>12</sup> But thou, LORD, everlasting art,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and thy remembrance shall  
Continually endure, and be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to generations all.

<sup>13</sup> Thou shalt arise, and mercy have  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon thy Zion yet;  
The time to favour her is come,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the time that thou hast set.

<sup>14</sup> For in her rubbish and her stones  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy servants pleasure take;  
Yea, they the very dust thereof  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do favour for her sake.

<sup>15</sup> So shall the heathen people fear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD’s most holy name;  
And all the kings on earth shall dread  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy glory and thy fame.

<sup>16</sup> When Zion by the mighty LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;built up again shall be,  
In glory then and majesty  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to men appear shall he.

<sup>17</sup> The prayèr of the destitute  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he surely will regard;  
Their prayèr will he not despise,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by him it shall be heard.

<sup>18</sup> For generations yet to come  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;this shall be on record:  
So shall the people that shall be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;created praise the LORD.

<sup>19</sup> He from his sanctuary’s height  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hath downward cast his eye;  
And from his glorious throne in heav’n  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD the earth did spy;

<sup>20</sup> That of the mournful prisoner  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the groanings he might hear,  
To set them free that unto death  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by men appointed are:

<sup>21</sup> That they in Zion may declare  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD’s most holy name,  
And publish in Jerusalem  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the praises of the same;

<sup>22</sup> When as the people gather shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in troops with one accord,  
When kingdoms shall assembled be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to serve the highest LORD.

<sup>23</sup> My wonted strength and force he hath  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;abated in the way,  
And he my days hath shortenèd:  
<sup>24</sup> Thus therefore did I say,

My God, in mid-time of my days  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;take thou me not away:  
From age to age eternally  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy years endure and stay.

<sup>25</sup> The firm foundation of the earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of old time thou hast laid;  
The heavens also are the work  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which thine own hands have made.

<sup>26</sup> Thou shalt for evermore endure,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but they shall perish all;  
Yea, ev’ry one of them wax old,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;like to a garment, shall:

Thou, as a vesture, shalt them change,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and they shall changèd be:  
<sup>27</sup> But thou the same art, and thy years  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are to eternity.

<sup>28</sup> The children of thy servants shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;continually endure;  
And in thy sight, O Lord, their seed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be established sure.

---

### Version 2

*L.M.*

<sup>1</sup> LORD, hear my pray’r, and let my cry  
Have speedy access unto thee;  
<sup>2</sup> In day of my calamity  
O hide not thou thy face from me.

Hear when I call to thee; that day  
An answer speedily return:  
<sup>3</sup> My days, like smoke, consume away,  
And, as an hearth, my bones do burn.

<sup>4</sup> My heart is wounded very sore,  
And witherèd, like grass doth fade:  
I am forgetful grown therefore  
To take and eat my daily bread.

<sup>5</sup> By reason of my smart within,  
And voice of my most grievous groans,  
My flesh consumèd is, my skin,  
All parched, doth cleave unto my bones.

<sup>6</sup> The pelican of wilderness,  
The owl in desert, I do match;  
<sup>7</sup> And, sparrow-like, companionless,  
Upon the house’s top, I watch.

<sup>8</sup> I all day long am made a scorn,  
Reproached by my malicious foes:  
The madmen are against me sworn,  
The men against me that arose.

<sup>9</sup> For I have ashes eaten up,  
To me as if they had been bread;  
And with my drink I in my cup  
Of bitter tears a mixture made.

<sup>10</sup> Because thy wrath was not appeased,  
And dreadful indignätion:  
Therefore it was that thou me raised,  
And thou again didst cast me down.

<sup>11</sup> My days are like a shade alway,  
Which doth declining swiftly pass;  
And I am witherèd away,  
Much like unto the fading grass.

<sup>12</sup> But thou, O LORD, shalt still endure,  
From change and all mutation free,  
And to all generations sure  
Shall thy remembrance ever be.

<sup>13</sup> Thou shalt arise, and mercy yet  
Thou to mount Zion shalt extend:  
Her time for favour which was set,  
Behold, is now come to an end.

<sup>14</sup> Thy saints take pleasure in her stones,  
Her very dust to them is dear.  
<sup>15</sup> All heathen lands and kingly thrones  
On earth thy glorious name shall fear.

<sup>16</sup> GOD in his glory shall appear,  
When Zion he builds and repairs.  
<sup>17</sup> He shall regard and lend his ear  
Unto the needy’s humble pray’rs:

Th’ afflicted’s pray’r he will not scorn.  
<sup>18</sup> All times this shall be on record:  
And generations yet unborn  
Shall praise and magnify the LORD.

<sup>19</sup> He from his holy place looked down,  
The earth he viewed from heav’n on high;  
<sup>20</sup> To hear the pris’ner’s mourning groan,  
And free them that are doomed to die;

<sup>21</sup> That Zion, and Jerus’lem too,  
His name and praise may well record,  
<sup>22</sup> When people and the kingdoms do  
Assemble all to praise the LORD.

<sup>23</sup> My strength he weakened in the way,  
My days of life he shortenèd.  
<sup>24</sup> My God, O take me not away  
In mid-time of my days, I said:

Thy years throughout all ages last.  
<sup>25</sup> Of old thou hast establishèd  
The earth’s foundation firm and fast:  
Thy mighty hands the heav’ns have made.

<sup>26</sup> They perish shall, as garments do,  
But thou shalt evermore endure;  
As vestures, thou shalt change them so;  
And they shall all be changèd sure:

<sup>27</sup> But from all changes thou art free;  
Thy endless years do last for aye.  
<sup>28</sup> Thy servants, and their seed who be,  
Established shall before thee stay.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 103

*A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O thou my soul, bless God the LORD;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and all that in me is  
Be stirrèd up his holy name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to magnify and bless.

<sup>2</sup> Bless, O my soul, the LORD thy God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and not forgetful be  
Of all his gracious benefits  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he hath bestowed on thee.

<sup>3</sup> All thine iniquities who doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;most graciously forgive:  
Who thy diseases all and pains  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth heal, and thee relieve.

<sup>4</sup> Who doth redeem thy life, that thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to death may’st not go down;  
Who thee with loving-kindness doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and tender mercies crown:

<sup>5</sup> Who with abundance of good things  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth satisfy thy mouth;  
So that, ev’n as the eagle’s age,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;renewèd is thy youth.

<sup>6</sup> GOD righteous judgment executes  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for all oppressèd ones.  
<sup>7</sup> His ways to Moses, he his acts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;made known to Isr’el’s sons.

<sup>8</sup> The LORD our God is merciful,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and he is gräcious,  
Long-suffering, and slow to wrath,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in mercy plenteous.

<sup>9</sup> He will not chide continually,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor keep his anger still.  
<sup>10</sup> With us he dealt not as we sinned,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor did requite our ill.

<sup>11</sup> For as the heaven in its height  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the earth surmounteth far;  
So great to those that do him fear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his tender mercies are:

<sup>12</sup> As far as east is distant from  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the west, so far hath he  
From us removèd, in his love,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all our iniquity.

<sup>13</sup> Such pity as a father hath  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto his children dear;  
Like pity shows the LORD to such  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as worship him in fear.

<sup>14</sup> For he remembers we are dust,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and he our frame well knows.  
<sup>15</sup> Frail man, his days are like the grass,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as flow’r in field he grows:

<sup>16</sup> For over it the wind doth pass,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and it away is gone;  
And of the place where once it was  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it shall no more be known.

<sup>17</sup> But unto them that do him fear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;GOD’s mercy never ends;  
And to their children’s children still  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his righteousness extends:

<sup>18</sup> To such as keep his covenant,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and mindful are alway  
Of his most just commändments,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that they may them obey.

<sup>19</sup> The LORD preparèd hath his throne  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in heavens firm to stand;  
And everything that being hath  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his kingdom doth command.

<sup>20</sup> O ye his angels, that excel  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in strength, bless ye the LORD;  
Ye who obey what he commands,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and hearken to his word.

<sup>21</sup> O bless and magnify the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ye glorious hosts of his;  
Ye ministers, that do fulfil  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whate’er his pleasure is.

<sup>22</sup> O bless the LORD, all ye his works,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wherewith the world is stored  
In his dominions everywhere.  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;My soul, bless thou the LORD.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 104

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Bless GOD, my soul.  O LORD my God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou art exceeding great;  
With honour and with majesty  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou clothèd art in state.

<sup>2</sup> With light, as with a robe, thyself  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou coverest about;  
And, like unto a curtain, thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the heavens stretchest out.

<sup>3</sup> Who of his chambers doth the beams  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within the waters lay;  
Who doth the clouds his chariot make,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on wings of wind make way.

<sup>4</sup> Who flaming fire his ministers,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his angels spirits, doth make:  
<sup>5</sup> Who earth’s foundätions did lay,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that it should never shake.

<sup>6</sup> Thou didst it cover with the deep,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as with a garment spread:  
The waters stood above the hills,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when thou the word but said.

<sup>7</sup> But at the voice of thy rebuke  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they fled, and would not stay;  
They at thy thunder’s dreadful voice  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did haste them fast away.

<sup>8</sup> They by the mountains do ascend,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and by the valley-ground  
Descend, unto that very place  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which thou for them didst found.

<sup>9</sup> Thou hast a bound unto them set,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that they may not pass over,  
That they do not return again  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the face of earth to cover.

<sup>10</sup> He to the valleys sends the springs,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which run among the hills:  
<sup>11</sup> They to all beasts of field give drink,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wild asses drink their fills.

<sup>12</sup> By them the fowls of heav’n shall have  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their habitätion,  
Which do among the branches sing  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with delectätion.

<sup>13</sup> He from his chambers watereth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the hills, when they are dried:  
With fruit and increase of thy works  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the earth is satisfied.

<sup>14</sup> For cattle he makes grass to grow,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he makes the herb to spring  
For th’ use of man, that food to him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he from the earth may bring;

<sup>15</sup> And wine, that to the heart of man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth cheerfulness impart,  
Oil that his face makes shine, and bread  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that strengtheneth his heart.

<sup>16</sup> The trees of GOD are full of sap;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the cedars that do stand  
In Lebanon, which planted were  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by his almighty hand.

<sup>17</sup> Birds of the air upon their boughs  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do choose their nests to make;  
As for the stork, the fir-tree she  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth for her dwelling take.

<sup>18</sup> The lofty mountains for wild goats  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a place of refuge be;  
The conies also to the rocks  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do for their safety flee.

<sup>19</sup> He sets the moon in heav’n, thereby  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the seasons to discern:  
From him the sun his certain time  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of going down doth learn.

<sup>20</sup> Thou darkness mak’st, ’tis night, then beasts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of forests creep abroad.  
<sup>21</sup> The lions young roar for their prey,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and seek their meat from God.

<sup>22</sup> The sun doth rise, and home they flock,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;down in their dens they lie.  
<sup>23</sup> Man goes to work, his labour he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth to the evening ply.

<sup>24</sup> How manifold, LORD, are thy works!  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in wisdom wonderful  
Thou ev’ry one of them hast made;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;earth’s of thy riches full:

<sup>25</sup> So is this great and spacious sea,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wherein things creeping are,  
Which numbered cannot be; and beasts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;both great and small are there.

<sup>26</sup> There ships go; there thou mak’st to play  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that leviàthan great.  
<sup>27</sup> These all wait on thee, that thou may’st  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in due time give them meat.

<sup>28</sup> That which thou givest unto them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they gather for their food;  
Thine hand thou open’st lib’rally,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they fillèd are with good.

<sup>29</sup> Thou hid’st thy face; they troubled are,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their breath thou tak’st away;  
Then do they die, and to their dust  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;return again do they.

<sup>30</sup> Thy quick’ning spirit thou send’st forth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;then they created be;  
And then the earth’s decayèd face  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;renewèd is by thee.

<sup>31</sup> The glory of the mighty LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;continue shall for ever:  
The Lord JEHOVAH shall rejoice  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in all his works together.

<sup>32</sup> Earth, as affrighted, trembleth all,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;if he on it but look;  
And if the mountains he but touch,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they presently do smoke.

<sup>33</sup> I will sing to the LORD most high,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;so long as I shall live;  
And while I being have I shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to my God praises give.

<sup>34</sup> Of him my meditation shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sweet thoughts to me afford;  
And as for me, I will rejoice  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in God, my only Lord.

<sup>35</sup> From earth let sinners be consumed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let ill men no more be.  
O thou my soul, bless thou the LORD.  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Praise to the LORD give ye.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 105

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Give thanks to GOD, call on his name;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to men his deeds make known.  
<sup>2</sup> Sing ye to him, sing psalms; proclaim  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his wondrous works each one.

<sup>3</sup> See that ye in his holy name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to glory do accord;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And let the heart of everyone  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;rejoice that seeks the LORD.

<sup>4</sup> The LORD Almighty, and his strength,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with steadfast hearts seek ye:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;His blessèd and his gracious face  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;seek ye continually.

<sup>5</sup> Think on the works that he hath done,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which admiration breed;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;His wonders, and the judgments all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which from his mouth proceed;

<sup>6</sup> O ye that are of Abr’ham’s race,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his servant well approv’n;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And ye that Jacob’s children are,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whom he chose for his own.

<sup>7</sup> Because he, and he only, is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the mighty LORD our God;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And his most righteous judgments are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in all the earth abroad.

<sup>8</sup> His cov’nant he remembered hath,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that it may ever stand:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;To thousand generätions  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the word he did command.

<sup>9</sup> Which covènant he firmly made  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with faithful Abraham,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And unto Isaac, by his oath,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he did renew the same:

<sup>10</sup> And unto Jacob, for a law,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he made it firm and sure,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;A covènant to Israèl,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which ever should endure.

<sup>11</sup> He said, I’ll give Canàan’s land  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for heritage to you;  
<sup>12</sup> While they were strangers there, and few,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in number very few:

<sup>13</sup> While yet they went from land to land  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;without a sure abode;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And while through sundry kingdoms they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did wander far abroad;

<sup>14</sup> Yet, notwithstanding, suffered he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;no man to do them wrong:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Yea, for their sakes, he did reprove  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;kings, who were great and strong.

<sup>15</sup> Thus did he say, Touch ye not those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that mine anointed be,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Nor do the prophets any harm  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that do pertain to me.

<sup>16</sup> He called for famine on the land,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he brake the staff of bread:  
<sup>17</sup> But yet he sent a man before,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by whom they should be fed;

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Ev’n Joseph, whom unnaturally  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sell for a slave did they;  
<sup>18</sup> Whose feet with fetters they did hurt,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and he in irons lay;

<sup>19</sup> Until the time that his word came  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to give him liberty;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The word and purpose of the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did him in prison try.

<sup>20</sup> Then sent the king, and did command  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that he enlarged should be:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;He that the people’s ruler was  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did send to set him free.

<sup>21</sup> A lord to rule his family  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he raised him, as most fit;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;To him of all that he possessed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he did the charge commit:

<sup>22</sup> That he might at his pleasure bind  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the princes of the land;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And he might teach his senators  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wisdom to understand.

<sup>23</sup> The people then of Israèl  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;down into Egypt came;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And Jacob also sojournèd  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within the land of Ham.

<sup>24</sup> And he did greatly by his pow’r  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;increase his people there;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And stronger than their enemies  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they by his blessing were.

<sup>25</sup> Their heart he turnèd to envy  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his folk maliciously,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;With those that his own servants were  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to deal in subtlety.

<sup>26</sup> His servant Moses he did send,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Aaron his chosen one.  
<sup>27</sup> By these his signs and wonders great  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in Ham’s land were made known.

<sup>28</sup> Darkness he sent, and made it dark;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his word they did obey.  
<sup>29</sup> He turned their waters into blood,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and he their fish did slay.

<sup>30</sup> The land in plenty brought forth frogs  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in chambers of their kings.  
<sup>31</sup> His word all sorts of flies and lice  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in all their borders brings.

<sup>32</sup> He hail for rain, and flaming fire  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;into their land he sent:  
<sup>33</sup> And he their vines and fig-trees smote;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;trees of their coasts he rent.

<sup>34</sup> He spake, and caterpillars came,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;locusts did much abound;  
<sup>35</sup> Which in their land all herbs consumed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and all fruits of their ground.

<sup>36</sup> He smote all first-born in their land,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;chief of their strength each one.  
<sup>37</sup> With gold and silver brought them forth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;weak in their tribes were none.

<sup>38</sup> Egypt was glad when forth they went,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their fear on them did light.  
<sup>39</sup> He spread a cloud for covering,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and fire to shine by night.

<sup>40</sup> They asked, and he brought quails: with  
bread  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of  heav’n  he fillèd them.  
<sup>41</sup> He opened rocks, floods gushed, and ran  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in deserts like a stream.

<sup>42</sup> For on his holy promise he,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and servant Abr’ham, thought.  
<sup>43</sup> With joy his people, his elect  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with gladness, forth he brought.

<sup>44</sup> And unto them the pleasant lands  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he of the heathen gave;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;That of the people’s labour they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;inheritance might have.

<sup>45</sup> That they his statutes might observe  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;according to his word;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And that they might his laws obey.  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Give praise unto the LORD.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 106

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Give praise and thanks unto the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for bountiful is he;  
His tender mercy doth endure  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto eternity.

<sup>2</sup> GOD’s mighty works who can express?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;or show forth all his praise?  
<sup>3</sup> Blessèd are they that judgment keep,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and justly do always.

<sup>4</sup> Remember me, LORD, with that love  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which thou to thine dost bear;  
With thy salvation, O my God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to visit me draw near:

<sup>5</sup> That I thy chosen’s good may see,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and in their joy rejoice;  
And may with thine inheritance  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;triumph with cheerful voice.

<sup>6</sup> We with our fathers sinnèd have,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and of iniquity  
Too long we have the workers been;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;we have done wickedly.

<sup>7</sup> The wonders great, which thou, O Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;didst work in Egypt land,  
Our fathers, though they saw, yet them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they did not understand:

And they thy mercies’ multitude  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;kept not in memory;  
But at the sea, ev’n the Red sea,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;provoked him grievously.

<sup>8</sup> Nevertheless he savèd them,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n for his own name’s sake;  
That so he might to be well known  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his mighty powèr make.

<sup>9</sup> When he the Red Sea did rebuke,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;then drièd up it was:  
Through depths, as through the wilderness,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he safely made them pass.

<sup>10</sup> From hands of those that hated them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he did his people save;  
And from the en’my’s cruel hand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to them redemption gave.

<sup>11</sup> The waters overwhelmed their foes;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;not one was left alive.  
<sup>12</sup> Then they believed his word, and praise  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to him in songs did give.

<sup>13</sup> But soon did they his mighty works  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;forget unthankfully,  
And on his counsel and his will  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did not wait patiently;

<sup>14</sup> But much did lust in wilderness,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and God in desert tempt.  
<sup>15</sup> He gave them what they sought, but to  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their soul he leanness sent.

<sup>16</sup> And against Moses in the camp  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their envy did appear;  
At Aaron they, the saint of GOD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;envìous also were.

<sup>17</sup> Therefore the earth did open wide,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and Dathan did devour,  
And all Abiram’s company  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did cover in that hour.

<sup>18</sup> Likewise among their company  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a fire was kindled then;  
And so the hot consuming flame  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;burnt up these wicked men.

<sup>19</sup> Upon the hill of Horeb they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;an idol-calf did frame,  
A molten image they did make,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and worshippèd the same.

<sup>20</sup> And thus their glory, and their God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;most vainly changèd they  
Into the likeness of an ox  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that eateth grass or hay.

<sup>21</sup> They did forget the mighty God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that had their saviour been,  
By whom such great things brought to pass  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they had in Egypt seen.

<sup>22</sup> In Ham’s land he did wondrous works,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;things terrible did he,  
When he his mighty hand and arm  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;stretched out at the Red sea.

<sup>23</sup> Then said he, He would them destroy,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;had not, his wrath to stay,  
His chosen Moses stood in breach,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that them he should not slay.

<sup>24</sup> Yea, they despised the pleasant land,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;believèd not his word:  
<sup>25</sup> But in their tents they murmurèd,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;not heark’ning to the LORD.

<sup>26</sup> Therefore in desert them to slay  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he lifted up his hand:  
<sup>27</sup> ’Mong nations to o’erthrow their seed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and scatter in each land.

<sup>28</sup> They unto Bàal-pèor did  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;themselves associate;  
The sacrifices of the dead  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they did profanely eat.

<sup>29</sup> Thus, by their lewd invëntions,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they did provoke his ire;  
And then upon them suddenly  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the plague brake in as fire.

<sup>30</sup> Then Phin’has rose, and justice did,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and so the plague did cease;  
<sup>31</sup> That to all ages counted was  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to him for righteousness.

<sup>32</sup> And at the waters, where they strove,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they did him angry make,  
In such sort, that it farèd ill  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with Moses for their sake:

<sup>33</sup> Because they there his spirit meek  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;provokèd bitterly,  
So that he uttered with his lips  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;words unadvisedly.

<sup>34</sup> Nor, as the LORD commanded them,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did they the nations slay:  
<sup>35</sup> But with the heathen mingled were,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and learned of them their way.

<sup>36</sup> And they their idols served, which did  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a snare unto them turn.  
<sup>37</sup> Their sons and daughters they to devils  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in sacrifice did burn.

<sup>38</sup> In their own children’s guiltless blood  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their hands they did imbrue,  
Whom to Canàan’s idols they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for sacrifices slew:

So was the land defiled with blood.  
<sup>39</sup> They stained with their own way,  
And with their own invëntions  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a whoring they did stray.

<sup>40</sup> Against his people kindled was  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the wrath of GOD therefore,  
Insomuch that he did his own  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;inheritance abhor.

<sup>41</sup> He gave them to the heathen’s hand;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their foes did them command.  
<sup>42</sup> Their en’mies them oppressed, they were  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;made subject to their hand.

<sup>43</sup> He many times delivered them;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but with their counsel so  
They him provoked, that for their sin  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they were brought very low.

<sup>44</sup> Yet their affliction he beheld,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when he did hear their cry:  
<sup>45</sup> And he for them his covenant  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did call to memory;

After his mercies’ multitude  
<sup>46</sup> he did repent: And made  
Them to be pitied of all those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who did them captive lead.

<sup>47</sup> O LORD our God, us save, and gather  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the heathen from among,  
That we thy holy name may praise  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in a triumphant song.

<sup>48</sup> Blessed be JEHOVAH, Isr’el’s God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to all eternity:  
Let all the people say, Amen.  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Praise to the LORD give ye.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

# Book V

*Psalms 107&ndash;150*

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 107

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Praise GOD, for he is good: for still  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his mercies lasting be.  
<sup>2</sup> Let GOD’s redeemed say so, whom he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from th’ en’my’s hand did free;

<sup>3</sup> And gathered them out of the lands,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from north, south, east, and west.  
<sup>4</sup> They strayed in desert’s pathless way,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;no city found to rest.

<sup>5</sup> For thirst and hunger in them faints  
<sup>6</sup> their soul. When straits them press,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;They cry unto the LORD, and he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;them frees from their distress.

<sup>7</sup> Them also in a way to walk  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that right is he did guide,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;That they might to a city go,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wherein they might abide.

<sup>8</sup> O that men to the LORD would give  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;praise for his goodness then,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And for his works of wonder done  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto the sons of men!

<sup>9</sup> For he the soul that longing is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth fully satisfy;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;With goodness he the hungry soul  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth fill abundantly.

<sup>10</sup> Such as shut up in darkness deep,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and in death’s shade abide,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Whom strongly hath affliction bound,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and irons fast have tied:

<sup>11</sup> Because against the words of God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they wrought rebelliously,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And they the counsel did contemn  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of him that is Most High:

<sup>12</sup> Their heart he did bring down with grief,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they fell, no help could have.  
<sup>13</sup> In trouble then they cried to GOD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he them from straits did save.

<sup>14</sup> He out of darkness did them bring,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and from death’s shade them take;  
These bands, wherewith they had been  
bound,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;asunder quite he brake.

<sup>15</sup> O that men to the LORD would give  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;praise for his goodness then,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And for his works of wonder done  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto the sons of men!

<sup>16</sup> Because the mighty gates of brass  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in pieces he did tear,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;By him in sunder also cut  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the bars of iron were.

<sup>17</sup> Fools, for their sin, and their offence,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do sore affliction bear;  
<sup>18</sup> All kind of meat their soul abhors;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they to death’s gates draw near.

<sup>19</sup> In grief they cry to GOD; he saves  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;them from their miseries.  
<sup>20</sup> He sends his word, them heals, and them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from their destruction frees.

<sup>21</sup> O that men to the LORD would give  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;praise for his goodness then,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And for his works of wonder done  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto the sons of men!

<sup>22</sup> And let them sacrifice to him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;off’rings of thankfulness;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And let them show abroad his works  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in songs of joyfulness.

<sup>23</sup> Who go to sea in ships, and in  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;great waters trading be,  
<sup>24</sup> Within the deep these men GOD’s works  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and his great wonders see.

<sup>25</sup> For he commands, and forth in haste  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the stormy tempest flies,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Which makes the sea with rolling waves  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;aloft to swell and rise.

<sup>26</sup> They mount to heav’n, then to the depths  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they do go down again;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Their soul doth faint and melt away  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with trouble and with pain.

<sup>27</sup> They reel and stagger like one drunk,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;at their wit’s end they be:  
<sup>28</sup> Then they to GOD in trouble cry,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who them from straits doth free.

<sup>29</sup> The storm is changed into a calm  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;at his command and will;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;So that the waves, which raged before,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;now quiet are and still.

<sup>30</sup> Then are they glad, because at rest  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and quiet now they be:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;So to the haven he them brings,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which they desired to see.

<sup>31</sup> O that men to the LORD would give  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;praise for his goodness then,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And for his works of wonder done  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto the sons of men!

<sup>32</sup> Among the people gatherèd  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let them exalt his name;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Among assembled elders spread  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his most renownèd fame.

<sup>33</sup> He to dry land turns water-springs,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and floods to wilderness;  
<sup>34</sup> For sins of those that dwell therein,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;fat land to barrenness.

<sup>35</sup> The burnt and parchèd wilderness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to water-pools he brings;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The ground that was dried up before  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he turns to water-springs:

<sup>36</sup> And there, for dwelling, he a place  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth to the hungry give,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;That they a city may prepare  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;commodiously to live.

<sup>37</sup> There sow they fields, and vineyards plant,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to yield fruits of increase.  
<sup>38</sup> His blessing makes them multiply,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;lets not their beasts decrease.

<sup>39</sup> Again they are diminishèd,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and very low brought down,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Through sorrow and afflïction,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and great opprëssion.

<sup>40</sup> He upon princes pours contempt,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and causeth them to stray,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And wander in a wilderness,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wherein there is no way.

<sup>41</sup> Yet setteth he the poor on high  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from all his miseries,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And he, much like unto a flock,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth make him families.

<sup>42</sup> They that are righteous shall rejoice,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when they the same shall see;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And, as ashamèd, stop her mouth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall all iniquity.

<sup>43</sup> Whoso is wise, and will these things  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;observe, and them record,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Ev’n they shall understand the love  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and kindness of the LORD.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)
