## Psalm 108

*A Song or Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> My heart is fixed, Lord; I will sing,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and with my glory praise.  
<sup>2</sup> Awake up psaltery and harp;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;myself I’ll early raise.

<sup>3</sup> I’ll praise thee ’mong the people, LORD;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;’mong nations sing will I:  
<sup>4</sup> For above heav’n thy mercy’s great,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy truth doth reach the sky.

<sup>5</sup> Be thou above the heavens, Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;exalted gloriously;  
Thy glory all the earth above  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be lifted up on high.

<sup>6</sup> That those who thy belovèd are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;deliverèd may be,  
O do thou save with thy right hand,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and answer give to me.

<sup>7</sup> God in his holiness hath said,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Herein I will take pleasure;  
Shechem I will divide, and forth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;will Succoth’s valley measure.

<sup>8</sup> Gilead I claim as mine by right;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Manasseh mine shall be;  
Ephraim is of my head the strength;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Judah gives laws for me;

<sup>9</sup> Moab’s my washing-pot; my shoe  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I’ll over Edom throw;  
Over the land of Palestine  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I will in triumph go.

<sup>10</sup> O who is he will bring me to  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the city fortified?  
O who is he that to the land  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of Edom will me guide?

<sup>11</sup> O God, thou who hadst cast us off,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;this thing wilt thou not do?  
And wilt not thou, ev’n thou, O God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;forth with our armies go?

<sup>12</sup> Do thou from trouble give us help,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for helpless is man’s aid.  
<sup>13</sup> Through God we shall do valiantly;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our foes he shall down tread.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 109

*A Song or Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O thou the God of all my praise,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do thou not hold thy peace;  
<sup>2</sup> For mouths of wicked men to speak  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;against me do not cease:

The mouths of vile deceitful men  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;against me opened be;  
And with a false and lying tongue  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they have accusèd me.

<sup>3</sup> They did beset me round about  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with words of hateful spite;  
And though to them no cause I gave,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;against me they did fight.

<sup>4</sup> They for my love became my foes,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but I me set to pray.  
<sup>5</sup> Evil for good, hatred for love,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to me they did repay.

<sup>6</sup> Set thou the wicked over him;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and upon his right hand  
Give thou his greatest enemy,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n Satan, leave to stand.

<sup>7</sup> And when by thee he shall be judged,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let him condemnèd be;  
And let his pray’r be turned to sin,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when he shall call on thee.

<sup>8</sup> Few be his days, and in his room  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his charge another take.  
<sup>9</sup> His children let be fatherless,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his wife a widow make.

<sup>10</sup> His children let be vagabonds,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and beg continually;  
And from their places desolate  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;seek bread for their supply.

<sup>11</sup> Let covetous extortioners  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;catch all he hath away:  
Of all for which he laboured hath  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let strangers make a prey.

<sup>12</sup> Let there be none to pity him,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let there be none at all  
That on his children fatherless  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;will let his mercy fall.

<sup>13</sup> Let his posterity from earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cut off for ever be,  
And in the foll’wing age their name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be blotted out by thee.

<sup>14</sup> Let GOD his father’s wickedness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;still to remembrance call;  
And never let his mother’s sin  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be blotted out at all.

<sup>15</sup> But let them all before the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;appear continually,  
That he may wholly from the earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;cut off their memory.

<sup>16</sup> Because he mercy minded not,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but persecuted still  
The poor and needy, that he might  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the broken-hearted kill.

<sup>17</sup> As he in cursing pleasure took,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;so let it to him fall;  
As he delighted not to bless,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;so bless him not at all.

<sup>18</sup> As cursing he like clothes put on,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;into his bowels so,  
Like water, and into his bones,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;like oil, down let it go.

<sup>19</sup> Like to the garment let it be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which doth himself array,  
And for a girdle, wherewith he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is girt about alway.

<sup>20</sup> From GOD let this be their reward  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that en’mies are to me,  
And their reward that speak against  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my soul maliciously.

<sup>21</sup> But do thou, for thine own name’s sake,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O GOD the Lord, for me:  
Sith good and sweet thy mercy is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from trouble set me free.

<sup>22</sup> For I am poor and indigent,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;afflicted sore am I,  
My heart within me also is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;wounded exceedingly.

<sup>23</sup> I pass like a declining shade,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;am like the locust tossed:  
<sup>24</sup> My knees through fasting weakened are,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my flesh hath fatness lost.

<sup>25</sup> I also am a vile reproach  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto them made to be;  
And they that did upon me look  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did shake their heads at me.

<sup>26</sup> O do thou help and succour me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who art my God and LORD:  
And, for thy tender mercy’s sake,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;safety to me afford:

<sup>27</sup> That thereby they may know that this  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is thy almighty hand;  
And that thou, LORD, hast done the same,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they may well understand.

<sup>28</sup> Although they curse with spite, yet, Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;bless thou with loving voice:  
Let them ashamed be when they rise;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy servant let rejoice.

<sup>29</sup> Let thou mine adversaries all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with shame be clothèd over;  
And let their own confüsion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;them, as a mantle, cover.

<sup>30</sup> But as for me, I with my mouth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;will greatly praise the LORD;  
And I among the multitude  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his praises will record.

<sup>31</sup> For he shall stand at his right hand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who is in poverty,  
To save him from all those that would  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;condemn his soul to die.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 110

*A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> The LORD did say unto my Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sit thou at my right hand,  
Until I make thy foes a stool,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whereon thy feet may stand.

<sup>2</sup> The LORD shall out of Zion send  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the rod of thy great pow’r:  
In midst of all thine enemies  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be thou the governor.

<sup>3</sup> A willing people in thy day  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of pow’r shall come to thee,  
In holy beauties from morn’s womb;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy youth like dew shall be.

<sup>4</sup> The LORD himself hath made an oath,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and will repent him never,  
Of th’ order of Melchizedek  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou art a priest for ever.

<sup>5</sup> The glorious and mighty Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that sits at thy right hand,  
Shall, in his day of wrath, strike through  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;kings that do him withstand.

<sup>6</sup> He shall among the heathen judge,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he shall with bodies dead  
The places fill: o’er many lands  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he wound shall ev’ry head.

<sup>7</sup> The brook that runneth in the way  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with drink shall him supply;  
And, for this cause, in triumph he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall lift his head on high.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 111

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Praise ye the LORD: with my whole heart  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I will GOD’s praise declare,  
Where the assemblies of the just  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and congregations are.

<sup>2</sup> The whole works of the LORD our God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are great above all measure,  
Sought out they are of everyone  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that doth therein take pleasure.

<sup>3</sup> His work most honourable is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;most glorious and pure,  
And his untainted righteousness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for ever doth endure.

<sup>4</sup> His works most wonderful he hath  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;made to be thought upon:  
The LORD is gracious, and he is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;full of compässion.

<sup>5</sup> He giveth meat unto all those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that truly do him fear;  
And evermore his covenant  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he in his mind will bear.

<sup>6</sup> He did the power of his works  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto his people show,  
When he the heathen’s heritage  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon them did bestow.

<sup>7</sup> His handiworks are truth and right;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all his commands are sure:  
<sup>8</sup> And, done in truth and uprightness,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they evermore endure.

<sup>9</sup> He sent redemption to his folk;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his covenant for aye  
He did command: holy his name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and rev’rend is alway.

<sup>10</sup> Wisdom’s beginning is GOD’s fear:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;good understanding they  
Have all that his commands fulfil:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his praise endures for aye.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 112

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Praise ye the LORD. The man is blessed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that fears the LORD aright,  
He who in his commändments  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth greatly take delight.

<sup>2</sup> His seed and offspring powerful  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be the earth upon:  
Of upright men blessèd shall be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the generätion.

<sup>3</sup> Riches and wealth shall ever be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within his house in store;  
And his unspotted righteousness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;endures for evermore.

<sup>4</sup> Unto the upright light doth rise,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;though he in darkness be:  
Compassionate, and merciful,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and rïghteous, is he.

<sup>5</sup> A good man doth his favour show,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and doth to others lend:  
He with discretion his affairs  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;will guide unto the end.

<sup>6</sup> Surely there is not any thing  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that ever shall him move:  
The righteous man’s memorial  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall everlasting prove.

<sup>7</sup> When he shall evil tidings hear,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he shall not be afraid:  
His heart is fixed, his confidence  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon the LORD is stayed.

<sup>8</sup> His heart is firmly stablishèd,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;afraid he shall not be,  
Until upon his enemies  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he his desire shall see.

<sup>9</sup> He hath dispersed, giv’n to the poor,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his righteousness shall be  
To ages all; with honour shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his horn be raisèd high.

<sup>10</sup> The wicked shall it see, and fret,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his teeth gnash, melt away:  
What wicked men do most desire  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall utterly decay.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 113

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Praise GOD: ye servants of the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O praise, the LORD’s name praise.  
<sup>2</sup> Yea, blessèd be the name of GOD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from this time forth always.

<sup>3</sup> From rising sun to where it sets,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;GOD’s name is to be praised.  
<sup>4</sup> Above all nations GOD is high,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;’bove heav’ns his glory raised.

<sup>5</sup> Unto the LORD our God that dwells  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on high, who can compare?  
<sup>6</sup> Himself that humbleth things to see  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in heav’n and earth that are.

<sup>7</sup> He from the dust doth raise the poor,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that very low doth lie;  
And from the dunghill lifts the man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;oppressed with poverty;

<sup>8</sup> That he may highly him advance,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and with the princes set;  
With those that of his people are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the chief, ev’n princes great.

The barren woman house to keep  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he maketh, and to be  
Of sons a mother full of joy.  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Praise to the LORD give ye.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 114

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> When Isr’el out of Egypt went,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and did his dwelling change,  
When Jacob’s house went out from those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that were of language strange,

<sup>2</sup> He Judah did his sanctuary,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his kingdom Isr’el make:  
<sup>3</sup> The sea it saw, and quickly fled,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Jordan was driven back.

<sup>4</sup> Like rams the mountains, and like lambs  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the hills skipped to and fro.  
<sup>5</sup> O sea, why fledd’st thou? Jordan, back  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;why wast thou driven so?

<sup>6</sup> Ye mountains great, wherefore was it  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that ye did skip like rams?  
And wherefore was it, little hills,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that ye did leap like lambs?

<sup>7</sup> O at the presence of the Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;earth, tremble thou for fear,  
While as the presence of the God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of Jacob doth appear:

<sup>8</sup> Who from the hard and stony rock  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did standing water bring;  
And by his pow’r did turn the flint  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;into a water-spring.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 115

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Not unto us, LORD, not to us,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but do thou glory take  
Unto thy name, ev’n for thy truth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and for thy mercy’s sake.

<sup>2</sup> O wherefore should the heathen say,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Where is their God now gone?  
<sup>3</sup> But our God in the heavens is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;what pleased him he hath done.

<sup>4</sup> Their idols silver are and gold,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;work of men’s hands they be.  
<sup>5</sup> Mouths have they, but they do not speak;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and eyes, but do not see;

<sup>6</sup> Ears have they, but they do not hear;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;noses, but savour not;  
<sup>7</sup> Hands, feet, but handle not, nor walk;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor speak they through their throat.

<sup>8</sup> Like them their makers are, and all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on them their trust that build.  
<sup>9</sup> O Isr’el, trust thou in the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he is their help and shield.

<sup>10</sup> O Aaron’s house, trust in the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their help and shield is he.  
<sup>11</sup> Ye that fear God, trust in the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their help and shield he’ll be.

<sup>12</sup> The LORD of us hath mindful been,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and he will bless us still:  
He will the house of Isr’el bless,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;bless Aaron’s house he will.

<sup>13</sup> Both small and great, that fear the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he will them surely bless.  
<sup>14</sup> The LORD will you, you and your seed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;aye more and more increase.

<sup>15</sup> O blessèd are ye of the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who made the earth and heav’n.  
<sup>16</sup> The heav’n, ev’n heav’ns, are GOD’s, but he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;earth to men’s sons hath giv’n.

<sup>17</sup> The dead, nor who to silence go,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;GOD’s praise do not record.  
<sup>18</sup> But henceforth we for ever will  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;bless GOD. Praise ye the LORD.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 116

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> I love the LORD, because my voice  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and prayers he did hear.  
<sup>2</sup> I, while I live, will call on him,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who bowed to me his ear.

<sup>3</sup> Of death the cords and sorrows did  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;about me compass round;  
The pains of hell took hold on me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I grief and trouble found.

<sup>4</sup> Upon the name of God the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;then did I call, and say,  
Deliver thou my soul, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I do thee humbly pray.

<sup>5</sup> GOD merciful and righteous is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;yea, gracious is our LORD.  
<sup>6</sup> GOD saves the meek: I was brought low,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he did me help afford.

<sup>7</sup> O thou my soul, do thou return  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto thy quiet rest;  
For largely, lo, the LORD to thee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his bounty hath expressed.

<sup>8</sup> For my distressèd soul from death  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;delivered was by thee:  
Thou didst my mourning eyes from tears,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my feet from falling, free.

<sup>9</sup> I in the land of those that live  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;will walk the LORD before.  
<sup>10</sup> I did believe, therefore I spake:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I was afflicted sore.

<sup>11</sup> I said, when I was in my haste,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that all men liars be.  
<sup>12</sup> What shall I render to the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for all his gifts to me?

<sup>13</sup> I’ll of salvation take the cup,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on GOD’s name will I call:  
<sup>14</sup> I’ll pay my vows now to the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before his people all.

<sup>15</sup> Dear in GOD’s sight is his saints’ death.  
<sup>16</sup> Thy servant, LORD, am I;  
Thy servant sure, thine handmaid’s son:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my bands thou didst untie.

<sup>17</sup> Thank-off’rings I to thee will give,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and on GOD’s name will call.  
<sup>18</sup> I’ll pay my vows now to the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before his people all;

<sup>19</sup> Within the courts of GOD’s own house,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within the midst of thee,  
O city of Jerusalem.  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Praise to the LORD give ye.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 117

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O give ye praise unto the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all nätions that be;  
Likewise, ye people all, accord  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his name to magnify.

<sup>2</sup> For great to us-ward ever are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his loving-kindnesses:  
His truth endures for evermore.  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The LORD O do ye bless.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 118

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O praise the LORD, for he is good;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his mercy lasteth ever.  
<sup>2</sup> Let those of Israèl now say,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;His mercy faileth never.

<sup>3</sup> Now let the house of Aaron say,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;His mercy lasteth ever.  
<sup>4</sup> Let those that fear the LORD now say,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;His mercy faileth never.

<sup>5</sup> I in distress called on the LORD;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD did answer me:  
He in a large place did me set,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from trouble made me free.

<sup>6</sup> The mighty LORD is on my side,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I will not be afraid;  
For anything that man can do  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I shall not be dismayed.

<sup>7</sup> The LORD doth take my part with them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that help to succour me:  
Therefore on those that do me hate  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I my desire shall see.

<sup>8</sup> Better it is to trust in GOD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;than trust in man’s defence;  
<sup>9</sup> Better to trust in GOD than make  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;princes our confidence.

<sup>10</sup> The nations, joining all in one,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did compass me about:  
But in the LORD’s most holy name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I shall them all root out.

<sup>11</sup> They compassed me about; I say,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they compassed me about:  
But in the LORD’s most holy name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I shall them all root out.

<sup>12</sup> Like bees they compassed me about;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;like unto thorns that flame  
They quenchèd are: for them shall I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;destroy in GOD’s own name.

<sup>13</sup> Thou sore hast thrust, that I might fall,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but my LORD helpèd me.  
<sup>14</sup> GOD my salvation is become,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my strength and song is he.

<sup>15</sup> In dwellings of the rïghteous  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is heard the melody  
Of joy and health: the LORD’s right hand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth ever valiantly.

<sup>16</sup> The right hand of the mighty LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;exalted is on high;  
The right hand of the mighty LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth ever valiantly.

<sup>17</sup> I shall not die, but live, and shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the works of GOD discover.  
<sup>18</sup> The LORD hath me chastisèd sore,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but not to death given over.

<sup>19</sup> O set ye open unto me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the gates of righteousness;  
Then will I enter into them,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and I the LORD will bless.

<sup>20</sup> This is the gate of GOD, by it  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the just shall enter in.  
<sup>21</sup> Thee will I praise, for thou me heard’st,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and hast my safety been.

<sup>22</sup> That stone is made head cornerstone,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which builders did despise:  
<sup>23</sup> This is the doing of the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and wondrous in our eyes.

<sup>24</sup> This is the day GOD made, in it  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;we’ll joy triumphantly.  
<sup>25</sup> Save now, I pray thee, LORD; I pray,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;send now prosperity.

<sup>26</sup> Blessèd is he in GOD’s great name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that cometh us to save:  
We, from the house which to the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;pertains, you blessèd have.

<sup>27</sup> God is the LORD, who unto us  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hath made light to arise:  
Bind ye unto the altar’s horns  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with cords the sacrifice.

<sup>28</sup> Thou art my God, I’ll thee exalt;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my God, I will thee praise.  
<sup>29</sup> Give thanks to GOD, for he is good:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his mercy lasts always.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 119

### Part 1 &mdash; Aleph

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Blessèd are they that undefiled,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and straight are in the way;  
Who in the LORD’s most holy law  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do walk, and do not stray.

<sup>2</sup> Blessèd are they who to observe  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his statutes are inclined;  
And who do seek the living God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with their whole heart and mind.

<sup>3</sup> Such in his ways do walk, and they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do no iniquity.  
<sup>4</sup> Thou hast commanded us to keep  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy precepts carefully.

<sup>5</sup> O that thy statutes to observe  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou would’st my ways direct!  
<sup>6</sup> Then shall I not be shamed, when I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy precepts all respect.

<sup>7</sup> Then with integrity of heart  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thee will I praise and bless,  
When I the judgments all have learned  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of thy pure righteousness.

<sup>8</sup> That I will keep thy statutes all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;firmly resolved have I:  
O do not then, most gracious God,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;forsake me utterly.

---

### Part 2 &mdash; Beth

*C.M.*

<sup>9</sup> By what means shall a young man learn  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his way to purify?  
If he according to thy word  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thereto attentive be.

<sup>10</sup> Unfeignedly thee have I sought  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with all my soul and heart:  
O let me not from the right path  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of thy commands depart.

<sup>11</sup> Thy word I in my heart have hid,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that I offend not thee.  
<sup>12</sup> O LORD, thou ever blessèd art,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy statutes teach thou me.

<sup>13</sup> The judgments of thy mouth each one  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my lips declarèd have:  
<sup>14</sup> More joy thy testimonies’ way  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;than riches all me gave.

<sup>15</sup> I will thy holy precepts make  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my meditätion;  
And carefully I’ll have respect  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto thy ways each one.

<sup>16</sup> Upon thy statutes my delight  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall constantly be set:  
And, by thy grace, I never will  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy holy word forget.

---

### Part 3 &mdash; Gimel

*C.M.*

<sup>17</sup> With me thy servant, in thy grace,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;deal bountifully, Lord;  
That by thy favour I may live,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and duly keep thy word.

<sup>18</sup> Open mine eyes, that of thy law  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the wonders I may see.  
<sup>19</sup> I am a stranger on this earth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hide not thy laws from me.

<sup>20</sup> My soul within me breaks, and doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;much fainting still endure,  
Through longing that it hath all times  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto thy judgments pure.

<sup>21</sup> Thou hast rebuked the cursèd proud,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who from thy precepts swerve.  
<sup>22</sup> Reproach and shame remove from me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for I thy laws observe.

<sup>23</sup> Against me princes spake with spite,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;while they in council sat:  
But I thy servant did upon  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy statutes meditate.

<sup>24</sup> My comfort, and my heart’s delight,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy testimonies be;  
And they, in all my doubts and fears,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are counsellors to me.

---

### Part 4 &mdash; Daleth

*C.M.*

<sup>25</sup> My soul to dust cleaves: quicken me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;according to thy word.  
<sup>26</sup> My ways I showed, and me thou heard’st:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;teach me thy statutes, Lord.

<sup>27</sup> The way of thy commändments  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;make me aright to know;  
So all thy works that wondrous are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I shall to others show.

<sup>28</sup> My soul doth melt, and drop away,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for heaviness and grief:  
To me, according to thy word,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;give strength, and send relief.

<sup>29</sup> From me the wicked way of lies  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let far removèd be;  
And graciously thy holy law  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do thou grant unto me.

<sup>30</sup> I chosen have the perfect way  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of truth and verity:  
Thy judgments that most righteous are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before me laid have I.

<sup>31</sup> I to thy testimonies cleave;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shame do not on me cast.  
<sup>32</sup> I’ll run thy precepts’ way, when thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my heart enlargèd hast.

---

### Part 5 &mdash; He

*C.M.*

<sup>33</sup> Teach me, O LORD, the perfect way  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of thy precepts divine,  
And to observe it to the end  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I shall my heart incline.

<sup>34</sup> Give understanding unto me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;so keep thy law shall I;  
Yea, ev’n with my whole heart I shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;observe it carefully.

<sup>35</sup> In thy law’s path make me to go;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for I delight therein.  
<sup>36</sup> My heart unto thy test’monies,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and not to greed, incline.

<sup>37</sup> Turn thou away my sight and eyes  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from viewing vanity;  
And in thy good and holy way  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be pleased to quicken me.

<sup>38</sup> Confirm to me thy gracious word,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which I did gladly hear,  
Ev’n to thy servant, Lord, who is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;devoted to thy fear.

<sup>39</sup> Turn thou away my feared reproach;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for good thy judgments be.  
<sup>40</sup> Lo, for thy precepts I have longed;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in thy truth quicken me.

---

### Part 6 &mdash; Vau

*C.M.*

<sup>41</sup> Let thy sweet mercies also come  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and visit me, O LORD;  
Ev’n thy benign salvätion,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;according to thy word.

<sup>42</sup> So shall I have wherewith I may  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;give him an answer just,  
Who spitefully reproacheth me;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for in thy word I trust.

<sup>43</sup> The word of truth out of my mouth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;take thou not utterly;  
For on thy judgments rïghteous  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my hope doth still rely.

<sup>44</sup> So shall I keep for evermore  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy law continually.  
<sup>45</sup> And, sith that I thy precepts seek,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I’ll walk at liberty.

<sup>46</sup> I’ll speak thy word to kings, and I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with shame shall not be moved;  
<sup>47</sup> And will delight myself always  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in thy laws, which I loved.

<sup>48</sup> To thy commandments, which I loved,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my hands lift up I will;  
And I will also meditate  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon thy statutes still.

---

### Part 7 &mdash; Zain

*C.M.*

<sup>49</sup> Remember, Lord, thy gracious word  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou to thy servant spake,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Which, for a ground of my sure hope,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou causedst me to take.

<sup>50</sup> This word of thine my comfort is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in mine afflïction:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For in my straits I am revived  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by this thy word alone.

<sup>51</sup> The men whose hearts with pride are  
stuffed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did greatly me deride;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Yet from thy straight commändments  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I have not turned aside.

<sup>52</sup> Thy judgments rïghteous, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which thou of old forth gave,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I did remember, and myself  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by them comforted have.

<sup>53</sup> Horror took hold on me, because  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ill men thy law forsake.  
<sup>54</sup> I in my house of pilgrimage  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy laws my songs do make.

<sup>55</sup> Thy name by night, LORD, I did mind,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and I have kept thy law.  
<sup>56</sup> And this I had, because thy word  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I kept, and stood in awe.

---

### Part 8 &mdash; Cheth

*C.M.*

<sup>57</sup> Thou my sure portion art alone,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which I did choose, O LORD:  
I have resolved, and said, that I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;would keep thy holy word.

<sup>58</sup> With my whole heart I did entreat  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy face and favour free:  
According to thy gracious word  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be merciful to me.

<sup>59</sup> I thought upon my former ways,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and did my life well try;  
And to thy testimonies pure  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my feet then turnèd I.

<sup>60</sup> I did not stay, nor linger long,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as those that slothful are;  
But hastily thy laws to keep  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;myself I did prepare.

<sup>61</sup> Bands of ill men me robbed; yet I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy precepts did not slight.  
<sup>62</sup> I’ll rise at midnight thee to praise,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n for thy judgments right.

<sup>63</sup> I am companion to all those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who fear, and thee obey.  
<sup>64</sup> O LORD, thy mercy fills the earth:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;teach me thy laws, I pray.

---

### Part 9 &mdash; Teth

*C.M.*

<sup>65</sup> Well hast thou with thy servant dealt,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as thou didst promise give.  
<sup>66</sup> Good judgment me, and knowledge teach,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for I thy word believe.

<sup>67</sup> Ere I afflicted was I strayed;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but now I keep thy word.  
<sup>68</sup> Both good thou art, and good thou do’st:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;teach me thy statutes, Lord.

<sup>69</sup> The men that are puffed up with pride  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;against me forged a lie;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Yet thy commändments observe  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with my whole heart will I.

<sup>70</sup> Their hearts, through worldly ease and  
wealth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as fat as grease they be:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;But in thy holy law I take  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;delight continually.

<sup>71</sup> It hath been very good for me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that I afflicted was,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;That I might well instructed be,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and learn thy holy laws.

<sup>72</sup> The word that cometh from thy mouth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is better unto me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Than many thousands and great sums  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of gold and silver be.

---

### Part 10 &mdash; Jod

*C.M.*

<sup>73</sup> Thou mad’st and fashion’dst me: thy laws  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to know give wisdom, Lord.  
<sup>74</sup> So who thee fear shall joy to see  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;me trusting in thy word.

<sup>75</sup> That very right thy judgments are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I know, and do confess;  
And that thou hast afflicted me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in truth and faithfulness.

<sup>76</sup> O let thy kindness merciful,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I pray thee, comfort me,  
As to thy servant faithfully  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;was promisèd by thee.

<sup>77</sup> And let thy tender mercies come  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to me, that I may live;  
Because thy holy laws to me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sweet delectation give.

<sup>78</sup> Lord, let the proud ashamèd be;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for they, without a cause,  
With me perversely dealt: but I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;will muse upon thy laws.

<sup>79</sup> Let such as fear thee, and have known  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy statutes, turn to me.  
<sup>80</sup> My heart let in thy laws be sound,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that shamed I never be.

---

### Part 11 &mdash; Caph

*C.M.*

<sup>81</sup> My soul for thy salvation faints;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;yet I thy word believe.  
<sup>82</sup> Mine eyes fail for thy word: I say,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;When wilt thou comfort give?

<sup>83</sup> For like a bottle I’m become,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that in the smoke is set:  
I’m black, and parched with grief; yet I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy statutes not forget.

<sup>84</sup> How many are thy servant’s days?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when wilt thou execute  
Just judgment on these wicked men  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that do me persecute?

<sup>85</sup> The proud have diggèd pits for me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which is against thy laws.  
<sup>86</sup> Thy words all faithful are: help me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;pursued without a cause.

<sup>87</sup> They so consumed me, that on earth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my life they scarce did leave:  
Thy precepts yet forsook I not,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but close to them did cleave.

<sup>88</sup> After thy loving-kindness, Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;me quicken, and preserve:  
The testimony of thy mouth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;so shall I still observe.

---

### Part 12 &mdash; Lamed

*C.M.*

<sup>89</sup> Thy word for ever is, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in heaven settled fast;  
<sup>90</sup> Unto all generätions  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy faithfulness doth last:

The earth thou hast establishèd,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and it abides by thee.  
<sup>91</sup> This day they stand as thou ordain’dst;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for all thy servants be.

<sup>92</sup> Unless in thy most perfect law  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my soul delights had found,  
I should have perishèd, when as  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my troubles did abound.

<sup>93</sup> Thy precepts I will ne’er forget;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they quick’ning to me brought.  
Lord, I am thine; O save thou me:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy precepts I have sought.

<sup>95</sup> For me the wicked have laid wait,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;me seeking to destroy:  
But I thy testimonies true  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;consider will with joy.

<sup>96</sup> An end of all perfëction  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;here have I seen, O God:  
But as for thy commändment,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it is exceeding broad.

---

### Part 13 &mdash; Mem

*C.M.*

<sup>97</sup> O how love I thy law! it is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my study all the day:  
<sup>98</sup> It makes me wiser than my foes;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for it doth with me stay.

<sup>99</sup> Than all my teachers now I have  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;more understanding far;  
Because my meditätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy testimonies are.

<sup>100</sup> In understanding I excel  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;those that are äncients;  
For I endeavourèd to keep  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all thy commändments.

<sup>101</sup> My feet from each ill way I stayed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that I may keep thy word.  
<sup>102</sup> I from thy judgments have not swerved;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for thou hast taught me, Lord.

<sup>103</sup> How sweet unto my taste, O Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are all thy words of truth!  
Yea, I do find them sweeter far  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;than honey to my mouth.

<sup>104</sup> I through thy precepts, that are pure,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do understanding get;  
I therefore ev’ry way that’s false  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with all my heart do hate.

---

### Part 14 &mdash; Nun

*C.M.*

<sup>105</sup> Thy word is to my feet a lamp,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and to my path a light.  
<sup>106</sup> I sworn have, and I will perform,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to keep thy judgments right.

<sup>107</sup> I am with sore afflïction  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n overwhelmed, O LORD:  
In mercy raise and quicken me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;according to thy word.

<sup>108</sup> The freewill off’rings of my mouth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;accept, I thee beseech:  
And unto me thy servant, LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy judgments clearly teach.

<sup>109</sup> Though still my soul be in my hand,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy laws I’ll not forget.  
<sup>110</sup> I erred not from them, though for me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the wicked snares did set.

<sup>111</sup> I of thy testimonies have  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;above all things made choice,  
To be my heritage for aye;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for they my heart rejoice.

<sup>112</sup> I carefully inclinèd have  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my heart still to attend;  
That I thy statutes may perform  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;alway unto the end.

---

### Part 15 &mdash; Samech

*C.M.*

<sup>113</sup> I hate the thoughts of vanity,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but love thy law do I.  
<sup>114</sup> My shield and hiding-place thou art:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I on thy word rely.

<sup>115</sup> All ye that evil-doers are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from me depart away;  
For the commandments of my God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I purpose to obey.

<sup>116</sup> According to thy faithful word  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;uphold and stablish me,  
That I may live, and of my hope  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ashamèd never be.

<sup>117</sup> Hold thou me up, so shall I be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in peace and safety still;  
And to thy statutes have respect  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;continually I will.

<sup>118</sup> Thou tread’st down all that love to stray;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;false their deceit doth prove.  
<sup>119</sup> Lewd men, like dross, away thou putt’st;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;therefore thy law I love.

<sup>120</sup> For fear of thee my very flesh  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth tremble, all dismayed;  
And of thy righteous judgments, Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my soul is much afraid.

---

### Part 16 &mdash; Ain

*C.M.*

<sup>121</sup> To all men I have judgment done,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;performing justice right;  
Then let me not be left unto  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my fierce oppressors’ might.

<sup>122</sup> For good unto thy servant, Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy servant’s surety be:  
From the oppression of the proud  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do thou deliver me.

<sup>123</sup> Mine eyes do fail with looking long  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for thy salvätion,  
The word of thy pure righteousness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;while I do wait upon.

<sup>124</sup> In mercy with thy servant deal,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy laws me teach and show.  
<sup>125</sup> I am thy servant, wisdom give,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that I thy laws may know.

<sup>126</sup> ’Tis time thou work, LORD; for they have  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;made void thy law divine.  
<sup>127</sup> Therefore thy precepts more I love  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;than gold, yea, gold most fine.

<sup>128</sup> Concerning all things thy commands  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all right I judge therefore;  
And ev’ry false and wicked way  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I perfectly abhor.

---

### Part 17 &mdash; Pe

*C.M.*

<sup>129</sup> Thy statutes, Lord, are wonderful,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my soul them keeps with care.  
<sup>130</sup> The entrance of thy words gives light,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;makes wise who simple are.

<sup>131</sup> My mouth I have wide openèd,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and panted earnestly,  
While after thy commändments  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I longed exceedingly.

<sup>132</sup> Look on me, Lord, and merciful  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do thou unto me prove,  
As thou art wont to do to those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy name who truly love.

<sup>133</sup> O let my footsteps in thy word  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;aright still ordered be:  
Let no iniquity obtain  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;dominion over me.

<sup>134</sup> From man’s oppression save thou me;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;so keep thy laws I will.  
<sup>135</sup> Thy face make on thy servant shine;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;teach me thy statutes still.

<sup>136</sup> Rivers of waters from mine eyes  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did run down, when I saw  
How wicked men run on in sin,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and do not keep thy law.

---

### Part 18 &mdash; Tzaddi

*C.M.*

<sup>137</sup> O LORD, thou art most rïghteous;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy judgments are upright.  
<sup>138</sup> Thy testimonies thou command’st  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;most faithful are and right.

<sup>139</sup> My zeal hath ev’n consumèd me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;because mine enemies  
Thy holy words forgotten have,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and do thy laws despise.

<sup>140</sup> Thy word’s most pure, therefore on it  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy servant’s love is set.  
<sup>141</sup> Small, and despised I am, yet I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy precepts not forget.

<sup>142</sup> Thy righteousness is righteousness  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which ever doth endure:  
Thy holy law, Lord, also is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the very truth most pure.

<sup>143</sup> Trouble and anguish have me found,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and taken hold on me:  
Yet in my trouble my delight  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy just commandments be.

<sup>144</sup> Eternal righteousness is in  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy testimonies all:  
Lord, to me understanding give,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and ever live I shall.

---

### Part 19 &mdash; Koph

*C.M.*

<sup>145</sup> With my whole heart I cried, LORD, hear;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I will thy word obey.  
<sup>146</sup> I cried to thee; save me, and I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;will keep thy laws alway.

<sup>147</sup> I of the morning did prevent  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the dawning, and did cry:  
For all mine expectätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did on thy word rely.

<sup>148</sup> Mine eyes did timeously prevent  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the watches of the night.  
That in thy word with careful mind  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;then meditate I might.

<sup>149</sup> After thy loving-kindness hear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my voice, that calls on thee:  
According to thy judgment, LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;revive and quicken me.

<sup>150</sup> Who follow mischief they draw nigh;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they from thy law are far:  
<sup>151</sup> But thou art near, LORD; most firm truth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all thy commandments are.

<sup>152</sup> As for thy testimonies all,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of old this have I tried,  
That thou hast surely founded them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for ever to abide.

---

### Part 20 &mdash; Resh

*C.M.*

<sup>153</sup> Consider mine afflïction,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in safety do me set:  
Deliver me, O Lord, for I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy law do not forget.

<sup>154</sup> After thy word revive thou me:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;save me, and plead my cause.  
<sup>155</sup> Salvation is from sinners far;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for they seek not thy laws.

<sup>156</sup> O LORD, both great and manifold  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy tender mercies be:  
According to thy judgments just,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;revive and quicken me.

<sup>157</sup> My persecutors many are,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and foes that do combine;  
Yet from thy testimonies pure  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my heart doth not decline.

<sup>158</sup> I saw transgressors, and was grieved;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for they keep not thy word.  
<sup>159</sup> See how I love thy law! as thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;art kind, me quicken, LORD.

<sup>160</sup> From the beginning all thy word  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hath been most true and sure:  
Thy righteous judgments ev’ry one  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for evermore endure.

---

### Part 21 &mdash; Schin

*C.M.*

<sup>161</sup> Princes have persecuted me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;although no cause they saw:  
But still of thy most holy word  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my heart doth stand in awe.

<sup>162</sup> I at thy word rejoice, as one  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of spoil that finds great store.  
<sup>163</sup> Thy law I love; but lying all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I hate and do abhor.

<sup>164</sup> Sev’n times a-day it is my care  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to give due praise to thee;  
Because of all thy judgments, Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which righteous ever be.

<sup>165</sup> Great peace have they who love thy law;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;offence they shall have none.  
<sup>166</sup> I hoped for thy salvation, LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and thy commands have done.

<sup>167</sup> My soul thy testimonies pure  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;observèd carefully;  
On them my heart is set, and them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I love exceedingly.

<sup>168</sup> Thy testimonies and thy laws  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I kept with special care;  
For all my works and ways each one  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;before thee open are.

---

### Part 22 &mdash; Tau

*C.M.*

<sup>169</sup> O let my earnest pray’r and cry  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;come near before thee, LORD:  
Give understanding unto me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;according to thy word.

<sup>170</sup> Let my request before thee come:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;after thy word me free.  
<sup>171</sup> My lips shall utter praise, when thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hast taught thy laws to me.

<sup>172</sup> My tongue of thy most blessèd word  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall speak, and it confess;  
Because all thy commändments  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are perfect righteousness.

<sup>173</sup> Let thy strong hand make help to me:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy precepts are my choice.  
<sup>174</sup> I longed for thy salvation, LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and in thy law rejoice.

<sup>175</sup> O let my soul live, and it shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;give praises unto thee;  
And let thy judgments gräcious  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be helpful unto me.

<sup>176</sup> I, like a lost sheep, went astray;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy servant seek, and find:  
For thy commands I suffered not  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to slip out of my mind.

## Psalm 120

*A Song of degrees.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> In my distress to GOD I cried,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and he gave ear to me.  
<sup>2</sup> From lying lips, and guileful tongue,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O LORD, my soul set free.

<sup>3</sup> What shall be giv’n thee? or what shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be done to thee, false tongue?  
<sup>4</sup> Ev’n burning coals of juniper,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;sharp arrows of the strong.

<sup>5</sup> Woe’s me that I in Mesech am  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a sojourner so long;  
That I in tabernacles dwell  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to Kedar that belong.

<sup>6</sup> My soul with him that hateth peace  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hath long a dweller been.  
<sup>7</sup> I am for peace; but when I speak,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for battle they are keen.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 121

*A Song of degrees.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> I to the hills will lift mine eyes,  
from whence doth come mine aid.  
<sup>2</sup> My safety cometh from the LORD,  
who heav’n and earth hath made.

<sup>3</sup> Thy foot he’ll not let slide, nor will  
he slumber that thee keeps.  
<sup>4</sup> Behold, he that keeps Israel,  
he slumbers not, nor sleeps.

<sup>5</sup> The LORD thee keeps, the LORD thy shade  
on thy right hand doth stay:  
<sup>6</sup> The moon by night thee shall not smite,  
nor yet the sun by day.

<sup>7</sup> The LORD shall keep thy soul; he shall  
preserve thee from all ill.  
<sup>8</sup> Henceforth thy going out and in  
GOD keep for ever will.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 122

*A Song of degrees of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> I joyed when to the house of GOD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Go up, they said to me.  
<sup>2</sup> Jerusalem, within thy gates  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our feet shall standing be.

<sup>3</sup> Jerus’lem, as a city, is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;compactly built together:  
<sup>4</sup> Unto that place the tribes go up,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the tribes of GOD go thither:

To Isr’el’s testimony, there  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to GOD’s name thanks to pay.  
<sup>5</sup> For thrones of judgment, ev’n the thrones  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of David’s house, there stay.

<sup>6</sup> Pray that Jerusalem may have  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;peace and felicity:  
Let them that love thee and thy peace  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;have still prosperity.

<sup>7</sup> Therefore I wish that peace may still  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within thy walls remain,  
And ever may thy palaces  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;prosperity retain.

<sup>8</sup> Now, for my friends’ and brethren’s sakes,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Peace be in thee, I’ll say.  
<sup>9</sup> And for the house of God our LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I’ll seek thy good alway.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 123

*A Song of degrees.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O thou that dwellest in the heav’ns,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I lift mine eyes to thee.  
<sup>2</sup> Behold, as servants’ eyes do look  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their masters’ hand to see,

As handmaid’s eyes her mistress’ hand;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;so do our eyes attend  
Upon the LORD our God, until  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to us he mercy send.

<sup>3</sup> O LORD, be gräcious to us,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto us gracious be;  
Because replenished with contempt  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;exceedingly are we.

<sup>4</sup> Our soul is filled with scorn of those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that at their ease abide,  
And with the insolent contempt  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of those that swell in pride.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 124

*A Song of degrees of David.*

### Version 1

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Had not the LORD been on our side,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;may Israèl now say;  
<sup>2</sup> Had not the LORD been on our side,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when men rose us to slay;

<sup>3</sup> They had us swallowed quick, when as  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their wrath ’gainst us did flame:  
<sup>4</sup> Waters had covered us, our soul  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;had sunk beneath the stream.

<sup>5</sup> Then had the waters, swelling high,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;over our soul made way.  
<sup>6</sup> Bless’d be the LORD, who to their teeth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;us gave not for a prey.

<sup>7</sup> Our soul’s escapèd, as a bird  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;out of the fowler’s snare;  
The snare asunder broken is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and we escapèd are.

<sup>8</sup> Our sure and all-sufficient help  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is in JEHOVAH’s name;  
His name who did the heav’n create,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and who the earth did frame.

---

### Version 2

*10.10.10.10.10*

<sup>1</sup> Now Israèl may say, and that truly,  
If that the LORD had not our cause  
maintained;  
<sup>2</sup> If that the LORD had not our right  
sustained,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;When cruel men against us furiously  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Rose up in wrath, to make of us their prey;

<sup>3</sup> Then certainly they had devoured us all,  
And swallowed quick, for ought that we  
could deem;  
Such was their rage, as we might well  
esteem.  
<sup>4</sup> And as fierce floods before them all things  
drown,  
So had they brought our soul to death quite  
down.

<sup>5</sup> The raging streams, with their proud  
swelling waves,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Had then our soul o’erwhelmèd in the deep.  
<sup>6</sup> But blessed be GOD, who doth us safely  
keep,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And hath not giv’n us for a living prey  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Unto their teeth, and bloody cruelty.

<sup>7</sup> Ev’n as a bird out of the fowler’s snare  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Escapes away, so is our soul set free:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Broke are their nets, and thus escapèd we.  
<sup>8</sup> Therefore our help is in the LORD’s great  
name,  
Who heav’n and earth by his great pow’r  
did frame.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 125

*A Song of degrees.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> They in the LORD that firmly trust  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall be like Zion hill,  
Which at no time can be removed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but standeth ever still.

<sup>2</sup> As round about Jerusalem  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the mountains stand alway,  
The LORD his folk doth compass so,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from henceforth and for aye.

<sup>3</sup> For ill men’s rod upon the lot  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of just men shall not lie;  
Lest righteous men stretch forth their hands  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto iniquity.

<sup>4</sup> Do thou to all those that be good  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy goodness, LORD, impart;  
And do thou good to those that are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upright within their heart.

<sup>5</sup> But as for such as turn aside  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;after their crooked way,  
GOD shall lead forth with wicked men:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on Isr’el peace shall stay.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 126

*A Song of degrees.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> When Zion’s bondage GOD turned back,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as men that dreamed were we.  
<sup>2</sup> Then filled with laughter was our mouth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our tongue with melody:

They ’mong the heathen said, The LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;great things for them hath wrought.  
<sup>3</sup> The LORD hath done great things for us,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whence joy to us is brought.

<sup>4</sup> As streams of water in the south,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our bondage, LORD, recall.  
<sup>5</sup> Who sow in tears, a reaping time  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of joy enjoy they shall.

<sup>6</sup> That man who, bearing precious seed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in going forth doth mourn,  
He doubtless, bringing back his sheaves,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;rejoicing shall return.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 127

*A Song of degrees for Solomon.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Except the LORD do build the house,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the builders lose their pain:  
Except the LORD the city keep,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the watchmen watch in vain.

<sup>2</sup> ’Tis vain for you to rise betimes,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;or late from rest to keep,  
To feed on sorrows’ bread; so gives  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he his belovèd sleep.

<sup>3</sup> Lo, children are GOD’s heritage,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the womb’s fruit his reward.  
<sup>4</sup> The sons of youth as arrows are,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for strong men’s hands prepared.

<sup>5</sup> O happy is the man that hath  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his quiver filled with those;  
They unashamèd in the gate  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall speak unto their foes.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 128

*A Song of degrees.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Blessed is each one that fears the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and walketh in his ways;  
<sup>2</sup> For of thy labour thou shall eat,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and happy be always.

<sup>3</sup> Thy wife shall as a fruitful vine  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by thy house’ sides be found:  
Thy children like to olive-plants  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;about thy table round.

<sup>4</sup> Behold, the man that fears the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thus blessèd shall he be.  
<sup>5</sup> The LORD shall out of Zion give  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his blessing unto thee:

Thou shalt Jerus’lem’s good behold  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whilst thou on earth dost dwell.  
<sup>6</sup> Thou shalt thy children’s children see,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and peace on Israel.

## Psalm 129

*A Song of degrees.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Oft did they vex me from my youth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;may Isr’el now declare;  
<sup>2</sup> Oft did they vex me from my youth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;yet not victorious were.

<sup>3</sup> The ploughers ploughed upon my back;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they long their furrows drew.  
<sup>4</sup> The righteous LORD did cut the cords  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of the ungodly crew.

<sup>5</sup> Let Zion’s haters all be turned  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;back with confüsion.  
<sup>6</sup> As grass on houses’ tops be they,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which fades ere it be grown:

<sup>7</sup> Whereof enough to fill his hand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the mower cannot find;  
Nor can the man his bosom fill,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whose work is sheaves to bind.

<sup>8</sup> Neither say they who do go by,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;GOD’s blessing on you rest:  
We in the name of God the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do wish you to be blessed.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 130

*A Song of degrees.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> LORD, from the depths to thee I cried.  
<sup>2</sup> My voice, Lord, do thou hear:  
Unto my supplications’ voice  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;give an attentive ear.

<sup>3</sup> Lord, who shall stand, if thou, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;should’st mark iniquity?  
<sup>4</sup> But yet with thee forgiveness is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that fear’d thou mayest be.

<sup>5</sup> I wait for GOD, my soul doth wait,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my hope is in his word.  
<sup>6</sup> More than they that for morning watch,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my soul waits for the Lord;

I say, more than they that do watch  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the morning light to see.  
<sup>7</sup> Let Israèl hope in the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for with him mercies be;

And plenteous redëmption  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is ever found with him.  
<sup>8</sup> And from all his iniquities  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he Isr’el shall redeem.

## Psalm 131

*A Song of degrees of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> My heart not haughty is, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mine eyes not lofty be;  
Nor do I deal in matters great,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;or things too high for me.

<sup>2</sup> I surely have myself behaved  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with quiet spirit and mild,  
As child of mother weaned: my soul  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;is like a weaned child.

<sup>3</sup> Upon the LORD let all the hope  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of Israèl rely,  
Ev’n from the time that present is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto eternity.

## Psalm 132

*A Song of degrees.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> David, and his afflictions all,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;LORD, do thou think upon;  
<sup>2</sup> How unto GOD he sware, and vowed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to Jacob’s mighty One.

<sup>3</sup> I will not come within my house,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor rest in bed at all;  
<sup>4</sup> Nor shall mine eyes take any sleep,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor eyelids slumber shall;

<sup>5</sup> Till for the LORD a place I find,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;where he may make abode;  
A place of habitätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for Jacob’s mighty God.

<sup>6</sup> Lo, at the place of Ephratah  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of it we understood;  
And we did find it in the fields,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and city of the wood.

<sup>7</sup> We’ll go into his tabernacles,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and at his footstool bow.  
<sup>8</sup> Arise, O LORD, into thy rest,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;th’ ark of thy strength, and thou.

<sup>9</sup> O let thy priests be clothèd, Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with truth and righteousness;  
And let all those that are thy saints  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shout loud for joyfulness.

<sup>10</sup> For thine own servant David’s sake,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do not deny thy grace:  
Nor of thine own anointed one  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;turn thou away the face.

<sup>11</sup> The LORD in truth to David sware,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he will not turn from it,  
I of thy body’s fruit will make  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon thy throne to sit.

<sup>12</sup> My cov’nant if thy sons will keep,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and laws to them made known,  
Their children then shall also sit  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for ever on thy throne.

<sup>13</sup> For GOD of Zion hath made choice;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;there he desires to dwell.  
<sup>14</sup> This is my rest, here still I’ll stay;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for I do like it well.

<sup>15</sup> Her food I’ll greatly bless; her poor  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with bread will satisfy.  
<sup>16</sup> Her priests I’ll clothe with health; her saints  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall shout forth joyfully.

<sup>17</sup> And there will I make David’s horn  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to bud forth pleasantly:  
For him that mine anointed is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a lamp ordained have I.

<sup>18</sup> As with a garment I will clothe  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with shame his en’mies all:  
But yet the crown that he doth wear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon him flourish shall.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 133

*A Song of degrees of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Behold, how good a thing it is,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and how becoming well,  
Together such as brethren are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in unity to dwell!

<sup>2</sup> Like precious ointment on the head,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that down the beard did flow,  
Ev’n Aaron’s beard, and to the skirts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did of his garments go.

<sup>3</sup> As Hermon’s dew, the dew that doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on Zion hills descend:  
For there the blessing GOD commands,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;life that shall never end.

<sup>2</sup> Your hands within God’s holy place

## Psalm 135

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Praise ye the LORD, the LORD’s name  
praise;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his servants, praise ye GOD.  
<sup>2</sup> Who stand in GOD’s house, in the courts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of our God make abode.

<sup>3</sup> Praise ye the LORD, for he is good;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;unto him praises sing:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Sing praises to his name, because  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it is a pleasant thing.

<sup>4</sup> For Jacob to himself the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did choose of his good pleasure,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And he hath chosen Israel  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for his peculiar treasure.

<sup>5</sup> Because I know assuredly  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD is very great,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And that our Lord above all gods  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in glory hath his seat.

<sup>6</sup> What things soever pleased the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that in the heav’n did he,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And in the earth, the seas, and all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the places deep that be.

<sup>7</sup> He from the ends of earth doth make  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the vapours to ascend;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;With rain he lightnings makes, and wind  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth from his treasures send.

<sup>8</sup> Egypt’s first-born, from man to beast  
<sup>9</sup> who smote. Strange tokens he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On Pharaoh and his servants sent,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Egypt, in midst of thee.

<sup>10</sup> He smote great nations, slew great kings:  
<sup>11</sup> Sihon of Heshbon king,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And Og of Bashan, and to nought  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did Canaan’s kingdoms bring:

<sup>12</sup> And for a wealthy heritage  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their pleasant land he gave,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;An heritage which Israèl,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his chosen folk, should have.

<sup>13</sup> Thy name, O LORD, shall still endure,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and thy memorial  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;With honour shall continued be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to generations all.

<sup>14</sup> For why? the righteous GOD will judge  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his people righteously;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Concerning those that do him serve,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;himself repent will he.

<sup>15</sup> The idols of the nätions  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of silver are and gold,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And by the hands of men is made  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their fäshion and mould.

<sup>16</sup> Mouths have they, but they do not speak;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;eyes, but they do not see;  
<sup>17</sup> Ears have they, but hear not; and in  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their mouths no breathing be.

<sup>18</sup> Their makers are like them; so are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all that on them rely.  
<sup>19</sup> O Isr’el’s house, bless GOD; bless GOD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O Aaron’s family.

<sup>20</sup> O bless the LORD, of Levi’s house  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ye who his servants are;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And bless the holy name of GOD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all ye the LORD that fear.

<sup>21</sup> And blessèd be the LORD our God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from Zion’s holy hill,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Who dwelleth at Jerusalem.  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The LORD O praise ye still.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)
