## Psalm 136

### Version 1

*8.7.8.7*

<sup>1</sup> Give thanks to GOD, for good is he:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for mercy hath he ever.  
<sup>2</sup> Thanks to the God of gods give ye:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for his grace faileth never.

<sup>3</sup> Thanks give the Lord of lords unto:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for mercy hath he ever.  
<sup>4</sup> Who only wonders great can do:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for his grace faileth never.

<sup>5</sup> Who by his wisdom made heav’ns high:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for mercy hath he ever.  
<sup>6</sup> Who stretched the earth above the sea:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for his grace faileth never.

<sup>7</sup> To him that made the great lights shine:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for mercy hath he ever.  
<sup>8</sup> The sun to rule till day decline:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for his grace faileth never.

<sup>9</sup> The moon and stars to rule by night:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for mercy hath he ever.  
<sup>10</sup> Who Egypt’s first-born killed outright:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for his grace faileth never.

<sup>11</sup> And Isr’el brought from Egypt land:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for mercy hath he ever.  
<sup>12</sup> With stretch’d-out arm, and with strong  
hand:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for his grace faileth never.

<sup>13</sup> By whom the Red Sea parted was:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for mercy hath he ever.  
<sup>14</sup> And through its midst made Isr’el pass:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for his grace faileth never.

<sup>15</sup> But Pharaoh and his host did drown:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for mercy hath he ever.  
<sup>16</sup> Who through the desert led his own:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for his grace faileth never.

<sup>17</sup> To him great kings who overthrew:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for he hath mercy ever.  
<sup>18</sup> Yea, famous kings in battle slew:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for his grace faileth never.

<sup>19</sup> Ev’n Sihon king of Amorites:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for he hath mercy ever.  
<sup>20</sup> And Og the king of Bashanites:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for his grace faileth never.

<sup>21</sup> Their land in heritage to have:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;(for mercy hath he ever).  
<sup>22</sup> His servant Isr’el right he gave:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for his grace faileth never.

<sup>23</sup> In our low state who on us thought:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for he hath mercy ever.  
<sup>24</sup> And from our foes our freedom wrought:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for his grace faileth never.

<sup>25</sup> Who doth all flesh with food relieve:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for he hath mercy ever.  
<sup>26</sup> Thanks to the God of heaven give:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for his grace faileth never.

---

### Version 2

*6.6.6.6.8.8*

<sup>1</sup> Praise GOD, for he is kind:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;His mercy lasts for aye.  
<sup>2</sup> Give thanks with heart and mind  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;To God of gods alway:  
For certainly his mercies dure  
Most firm and sure eternally.

<sup>3</sup> The Lord of lords praise ye,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Whose mercies still endure.  
<sup>4</sup> Great wonders only he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Doth work by his great pow’r:  
For certainly his mercies dure  
Most firm and sure eternally.

<sup>5</sup> Which God omnipotent,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;By might and wisdom high,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The heav’n and firmament  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Did frame, as we may see:  
For certainly his mercies dure  
Most firm and sure eternally.

<sup>6</sup> To him who did outstretch  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;This earth so great and wide,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Above the waters’ reach  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Making it to abide:  
For certainly his mercies dure  
Most firm and sure eternally.

<sup>7</sup> Great lights he made to be;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For his grace lasteth aye:  
<sup>8</sup> Such as the sun we  see,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;To rule the lightsome day:  
For certainly his mercies dure  
Most firm and sure eternally.

<sup>9</sup> Also the moon so clear,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Which shineth in our sight;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The stars that do appear,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;To guide the darksome night:  
For certainly his mercies dure  
Most firm and sure eternally.

<sup>10</sup> To him that Egypt smote,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Who did his message scorn;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And in his anger hot  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Did kill all their first-born:  
For certainly his mercies dure  
Most firm and sure eternally.

<sup>11</sup> Thence Isr’el out he brought;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For his grace lasteth ever.  
<sup>12</sup> With a strong hand he wrought,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And stretched-out arm deliver:  
For certainly his mercies dure  
Most firm and sure eternally.

<sup>13</sup> The sea he cut in two;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For his grace lasteth still.  
<sup>14</sup> And through its midst to go  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Made his own Israèl:  
For certainly his mercies dure  
Most firm and sure eternally.

<sup>15</sup> But overwhelmed and lost  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Was proud king Pharàoh,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;With all his mighty host,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And chariots there also:  
For certainly his mercies dure  
Most firm and sure eternally.

<sup>16</sup> To him who pow’rfully  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;His chosen people led,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Ev’n through the desert dry,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And in that place them fed:  
For certainly his mercies dure  
Most firm and sure eternally.

<sup>17</sup> To him great kings who smote;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For his grace hath no bound.  
<sup>18</sup> Who slew, and sparèd not  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Kings famous and renowned:  
For certainly his mercies dure  
Most firm and sure eternally.

<sup>19</sup> Sihon the Am’rites’ king;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For his grace lasteth ever:  
<sup>20</sup> Og also, who did reign  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The land of Bashan over:  
For certainly his mercies dure  
Most firm and sure eternally.

<sup>21</sup> Their land by lot he gave;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For his grace faileth never,  
<sup>22</sup> That Isr’el might it have  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In heritage for ever:  
For certainly his mercies dure  
Most firm and sure eternally.

<sup>23</sup> Who hath rememberèd  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Us in our low estate;  
<sup>24</sup> And us deliverèd  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;From foes which did us hate:  
For certainly his mercies dure  
Most firm and sure eternally.

<sup>25</sup> Who to all flesh gives food;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For his grace faileth never.  
<sup>26</sup> Give thanks to God most good,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;The God of heav’n, for ever:  
For certainly his mercies dure  
Most firm and sure eternally.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 137

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> By Babel’s streams we sat and wept,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when Zion we thought on.  
<sup>2</sup> In midst thereof we hanged our harps  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the willow-trees upon.

<sup>3</sup> For there a song requirèd they,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who did us captive bring:  
Our spoilers called for mirth, and said,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;A song of Zion sing.

<sup>4</sup> O how the LORD’s song shall we sing  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;within a foreign land?  
<sup>5</sup> If thee, Jerus’lem, I forget,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;skill part from my right hand.

<sup>6</sup> My tongue to my mouth’s roof let cleave,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;if I do thee forget,  
Jerusalem, and thee above  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my chief joy do not set.

<sup>7</sup> Remember Edom’s children, LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who in Jerus’lem’s day,  
Ev’n unto its foundätion,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Raze, raze it quite, did say.

<sup>8</sup> O daughter thou of Babylon,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;near to destrüction;  
Bless’d shall he be that thee rewards,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as thou to us hast done.

<sup>9</sup> Yea, happy surely shall he be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy tender little ones  
Who shall lay hold upon, and them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall dash against the stones.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 138

*A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Thee will I praise with all my heart,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I will sing praise to thee  
<sup>2</sup> Before the gods: And worship will  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;toward thy sanctuary.

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I’ll praise thy name, ev’n for thy truth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and kindness of thy love;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For thou thy word hast magnified  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all thy great name above.

<sup>3</sup> Thou didst me answer in the day  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when I to thee did cry;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And thou my fainting soul with strength  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;didst strengthen inwardly.

<sup>4</sup> All kings upon the earth that are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall give thee praise, O LORD;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;When as they from thy mouth shall hear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy true and faithful word.

<sup>5</sup> Yea, in the righteous ways of GOD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with gladness they shall sing:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For great’s the glory of the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who doth for ever reign.

<sup>6</sup> Though GOD be high, yet he respects  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;all those that lowly be;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Whereas the proud and lofty ones  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;afar off knoweth he.

<sup>7</sup> Though I in midst of trouble walk,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I life from thee shall have:  
’Gainst my foes’ wrath thou ’lt stretch thine  
hand;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy right hand shall me save.

<sup>8</sup> Surely that which concerneth me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD will perfect make:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;LORD, still thy mercy lasts; do not  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thine own hands’ works forsake.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 139

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O LORD, thou hast me searched and  
known.  
<sup>2</sup> Thou know’st my sitting down,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And rising up; yea, all my thoughts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;afar to thee are known.

<sup>3</sup> My footsteps, and my lying down,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou compassest always;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Thou also most entirely art  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;acquaint with all my ways.

<sup>4</sup> For in my tongue, before I speak,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;not any word can be,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;But altogether, lo, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it is well known to thee.

<sup>5</sup> Behind, before, thou hast beset,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and laid on me thine hand.  
<sup>6</sup> Such knowledge is too strange for me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;too high to understand.

<sup>7</sup> From thy Spirit whither shall I go?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;or from thy presence fly?  
<sup>8</sup> Ascend I heav’n, lo, thou art there;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;there, if in hell I lie.

<sup>9</sup> Take I the morning wings, and dwell  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in utmost parts of sea;  
<sup>10</sup> Ev’n there, Lord, shall thy hand me lead,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy right hand hold shall me.

<sup>11</sup> If I do say that darkness shall  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;me cover from thy sight,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Then surely shall the very night  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;about me be as light.

<sup>12</sup> Yea, darkness hideth not from thee,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but night doth shine as day:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;To thee the darkness and the light  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are both alike alway.

<sup>13</sup> For thou possessèd hast my reins,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and thou hast covered me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;When I within my mother’s womb  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;inclosèd was by thee.

<sup>14</sup> Thee will I praise; for fearfully  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and strangely made I am;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Thy works are marv’llous, and right well  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my soul doth know the same.

<sup>15</sup> My substance was not hid from thee,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when as in secret I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Was made; and in earth’s lowest parts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;was wrought most curiously.

<sup>16</sup> Thine eyes my substance did behold,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;yet being unperfect;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And in the volume of thy book  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my members all were writ;

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Which after in continuance  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;were fashioned ev’ry one,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;When as they yet all shapeless were,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and of them there was none.

<sup>17</sup> How precious also are thy thoughts,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O gracious God, to me!  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And in their sum how passing great  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and numberless they be!

<sup>18</sup> If I should count them, than the sand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they more in number be:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;What time soever I awake,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I ever am with thee.

<sup>19</sup> Thou, Lord, wilt sure the wicked slay:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hence from me bloody men.  
<sup>20</sup> Thy foes against thee loudly speak,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and take thy name in vain.

<sup>21</sup> Do not I hate all those, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that hatred bear to thee?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;With those that up against thee rise  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;can I but grievèd be?

<sup>22</sup> With perfect hatred them I hate,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my foes I them do hold.  
<sup>23</sup> Search me, O God, and know my heart,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;try me, my thoughts unfold:

<sup>24</sup> And see if any wicked way  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;there be at all in me;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And in thine everlasting way  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to me a leader be.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 140

*To the chief Musician, A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> LORD, from the ill and froward man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;give me deliverance,  
And do thou safe preserve me from  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the man of violence:

<sup>2</sup> Who in their heart mischievous things  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;are meditating ever;  
And they for war assembled are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;continually together.

<sup>3</sup> Much like unto a serpent’s tongue  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their tongues they sharp do make;  
And underneath their lips there lies  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the poison of a snake.

<sup>4</sup> LORD, keep me from the wicked’s hands,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from vi’lent men me save;  
Who utterly to overthrow  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my goings purposed have.

<sup>5</sup> The proud for me a snare have hid,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and cords; yea, they a net  
Have by the wayside for me spread;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they gins for me have set.

<sup>6</sup> I said unto the LORD, Thou art  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my God: unto the cry  
Of all my supplicätions,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;LORD, do thine ear apply.

<sup>7</sup> O GOD the Lord, who art the strength  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of my salvätion:  
A cov’ring in the day of war  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my head thou hast put on.

<sup>8</sup> Unto the wicked man, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his wishes do not grant;  
Nor further thou his ill device,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;lest they themselves should vaunt.

<sup>9</sup> As for the head and chief of those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;about that compass me,  
Ev’n by the mischief of the lips  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let thou them covered be.

<sup>10</sup> Let burning coals upon them fall,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;them throw in fiery flame,  
And in deep pits, that they no more  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;may rise out of the same.

<sup>11</sup> Let not an evil speaker be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on earth establishèd:  
Mischief shall hunt the vi’lent man,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;till he be ruinèd.

<sup>12</sup> I know GOD will th’ afflicted’s cause  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;maintain, and poor men’s right.  
<sup>13</sup> Surely the just shall praise thy name;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;th’ upright dwell in thy sight.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 141

*A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O LORD, I unto thee do cry,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;do thou make haste to me,  
And give an ear unto my voice,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;when I cry unto thee.

<sup>2</sup> As incense let my prayer be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;directed in thine eyes;  
And the uplifting of my hands  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as th’ ev’ning sacrifice.

<sup>3</sup> Set, LORD, a watch before my mouth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;keep of my lips the door.  
<sup>4</sup> My heart incline thou not unto  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the ills I should abhor,

To practise wicked works with men  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that work iniquity;  
And with their delicates my taste  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let me not satisfy.

<sup>5</sup> Let him that righteous is me smite,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it shall a kindness be;  
Let him reprove, I shall it count  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a precious oil to me:

Such smiting shall not break my head;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for yet the time shall fall,  
When I in their calamities  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to God pray for them shall.

<sup>6</sup> When as their judges down shall be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in stony places cast,  
Then shall they hear my words; for they  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;shall sweet be to their taste.

<sup>7</sup> About the grave’s devouring mouth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our bones are scattered round,  
As wood which men do cut and cleave  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;lies scattered on the ground.

<sup>8</sup> But unto thee, O GOD the Lord,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;mine eyes uplifted be:  
My soul do not leave destitute;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my trust is set on thee.

<sup>9</sup> Lord, keep me safely from the snares  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which they for me prepare;  
And from the subtle gins of them  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that wicked workers are.

<sup>10</sup> Let workers of iniquity  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;into their own nets fall,  
Whilst I do, by thine help, escape  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the danger of them all.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 142

*Maschil of David; A Prayer when he was in the cave.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> I with my voice cried to the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with it made my request:  
<sup>2</sup> Poured out to him my plaint, to him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my trouble I expressed.

<sup>3</sup> When in me was o’erwhelmed my spirit,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;then well thou knew’st my way;  
Where I did walk a snare for me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they privily did lay.

<sup>4</sup> I looked on my right hand, and viewed,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;but none to know me were;  
All refuge failèd me, no man  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;did for my soul take care.

<sup>5</sup> I cried to thee; I said, Thou art  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my refuge, LORD, alone;  
And in the land of those that live  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thou art my pörtion.

<sup>6</sup> Because I am brought very low,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;attend unto my cry:  
Me from my persecutors save,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who stronger are than I.

<sup>7</sup> From prison bring my soul, that I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy name may glorify:  
The just shall compass me, when thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with me deal’st bounteously.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 143

*A Psalm of David.*

### Version 1

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> LORD, hear my pray’r, attend my suits;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and in thy faithfulness  
Give thou an answer unto me,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and in thy righteousness.

<sup>2</sup> Thy servant also bring thou not  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in judgment to be tried:  
Because no living man can be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in thy sight justified.

<sup>3</sup> For th’ en’my hath pursued my soul,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my life to ground down tread:  
In darkness he hath made me dwell,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as who have long been dead.

<sup>4</sup> My spirit is therefore overwhelmed  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in me perplexedly;  
Within me is my very heart  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;amazèd wondrously.

<sup>5</sup> I call to mind the days of old,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to meditate I use  
On all thy works; upon the deeds  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I of thy hands do muse.

<sup>6</sup> My hands to thee I stretch; my soul  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thirsts, as dry land, for thee.  
<sup>7</sup> Haste, Lord, to hear, my spirit fails:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hide not thy face from me;

Lest like to them I do become  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that go down to the dust.  
<sup>8</sup> At morn let me thy kindness hear;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for in thee do I trust.

Teach me the way that I should walk:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I lift my soul to thee.  
<sup>9</sup> LORD, free me from my foes; I flee  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to thee to cover me.

<sup>10</sup> Because thou art my God, to do  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy will do me instruct:  
Thy Spirit is good, me to the land  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of uprightness conduct.

<sup>11</sup> Revive and quicken me, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ev’n for thine own name’s sake;  
And do thou, for thy righteousness,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my soul from trouble take.

<sup>12</sup> And of thy mercy slay my foes;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let all destroyèd be  
That do afflict my soul: for I  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a servant am to thee.

---

### Version 2

*6.6.6.6.D*

<sup>1</sup> Oh, hear my prayer, LORD,  
And unto my desire  
To bow thine ear accord,  
I humbly thee require;  
And, in thy faithfulness,  
Unto me answer make,  
And, in thy righteousness,  
Upon me pity take.

<sup>2</sup> In judgment enter not  
With me thy servant poor;  
For why, this well I wot,  
No sinner can endure  
The sight of thee, O God:  
If thou his deeds shalt try,  
He dare make none abode  
Himself to justify.

<sup>3</sup> Behold, the cruel foe  
Me persecutes with spite,  
My soul to overthrow:  
Yea, he my life down quite  
Unto the ground hath smote,  
And made me dwell full low  
In darkness, as forgot,  
Or men dead long ago.

<sup>4</sup> Therefore my spirit much vexed,  
O’erwhelmed is me within;  
My heart right sore perplexed  
And desolate hath been.  
<sup>5</sup> Yet I do call to mind  
What ancient days record,  
Thy works of ev’ry kind  
I think upon, O Lord.

<sup>6</sup> Lo, I do stretch my hands  
To thee, my help alone;  
For thou well understands  
All my complaint and moan:  
My thirsting soul desires,  
And longeth after thee,  
As thirsty ground requires  
With rain refreshed to be.

<sup>7</sup> LORD, let my pray’r prevail,  
To answer it make speed;  
For, lo, my spirit doth fail:  
Hide not thy face in need;  
Lest I be like to those  
That do in darkness sit,  
Or him that downward goes  
Into the dreadful pit.

<sup>8</sup> Because I trust in thee,  
O Lord, cause me to hear  
Thy loving-kindness free,  
When morning doth appear:  
Cause me to know the way  
Wherein my path should be;  
For why, my soul on high  
I do lift up to thee.

<sup>9</sup> From my fierce enemy  
In safety do me guide,  
Because I flee to thee,  
LORD, that thou may’st me hide.  
<sup>10</sup> My God alone art thou,  
Teach me thy righteousness:  
Thy Spirit ’s good, lead me to  
The land of uprightness.

<sup>11</sup> O LORD, for thy name’s sake,  
Be pleased to quicken me;  
And, for thy truth, forth take  
My soul from misery.  
<sup>12</sup> And of thy grace destroy  
My foes, and put to shame  
All who my soul annoy;  
For I thy servant am.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 144

*A Psalm of David.*

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O blessèd ever be the LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who is my strength and might,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Who doth instruct my hands to war,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my fingers teach to fight.

<sup>2</sup> My goodness, fortress, my high tow’r,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;deliverer, and shield,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;In whom I trust: who under me  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;my people makes to yield.

<sup>3</sup> LORD, what is man, that thou of him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;dost so much knowledge take?  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Or son of man, that thou of him  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;so great account dost make?

<sup>4</sup> Man is like vanity; his days,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;as shadows, pass away.  
<sup>5</sup> LORD, bow thy heav’ns, come down, touch  
thou  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the hills, and smoke shall they.

<sup>6</sup> Cast forth thy lightning, scatter them;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thine arrows shoot, them rout.  
<sup>7</sup> Thine hand send from above, me save;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from great depths draw me out;

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And from the hand of children strange,  
<sup>8</sup> Whose mouth speaks vanity;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And their right hand is a right hand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that works deceitfully.

<sup>9</sup> A new song I to thee will sing,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Lord, on a psaltery;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I on a ten-stringed instrument  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;will praises sing to thee.

<sup>10</sup> Ev’n he it is that unto kings  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;salvätion doth send;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Who his own servant David doth  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;from hurtful sword defend.

<sup>11</sup> O free me from strange children’s hand,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whose mouth speaks vanity;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And their right hand a right hand is  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that works deceitfully.

<sup>12</sup> That, as the plants, our sons may be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in youth grown up that are;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Our daughters like to corner-stones,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;carved like a palace fair.

<sup>13</sup> That to afford all kind of store  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;our garners may be filled;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;That our sheep thousands, in our streets  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;ten thousands they may yield.

<sup>14</sup> That strong our oxen be for work,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that no in-breaking be,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Nor going out; and that our streets  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;may from complaints be free.

<sup>15</sup> Those people blessèd are who be  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in such a case as this;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Yea, blessèd all those people are,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whose God JEHOVAH is.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 145

*David's Psalm of praise.*

### Version 1

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> I’ll thee extol, my God, O King;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;I’ll bless thy name always.  
<sup>2</sup> Thee will I bless each day, and will  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy name for ever praise.

<sup>3</sup> Great is the LORD, much to be praised;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his greatness search exceeds.  
<sup>4</sup> Race unto race shall praise thy works,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and show thy mighty deeds.

<sup>5</sup> I of thy glorious majesty  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the honour will record;  
I’ll speak of all thy mighty works,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which wondrous are, O Lord.

<sup>6</sup> Men of thine acts the might shall show,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thine acts that dreadful are;  
And I, thy glory to advance,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy greatness will declare.

<sup>7</sup> The mem’ry of thy goodness great  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;they largely shall express;  
With songs of praise they shall extol  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy perfect righteousness.

<sup>8</sup> The LORD is very gräcious,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in him compassions flow;  
In mercy he is very great,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and is to anger slow.

<sup>9</sup> The Lord JEHOVAH unto all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his goodness doth declare;  
And over all his other works  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his tender mercies are.

<sup>10</sup> Thee all thy works shall praise, O LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and thee thy saints shall bless;  
<sup>11</sup> They shall thy kingdom’s glory show,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy pow’r by speech express:

<sup>12</sup> To make the sons of men to know  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his acts done mightily,  
And of his kingdom th’ excellent  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and glorious majesty.

<sup>13</sup> Thy kingdom shall for ever stand,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy reign through ages all.  
<sup>14</sup> GOD raiseth all that are bowed down,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upholdeth all that fall.

<sup>15</sup> The eyes of all things wait on thee,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the giver of all good;  
And thou, in time convenient,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;bestow’st on them their food:

<sup>16</sup> Thine hand thou open’st lib’rally,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and of thy bounty gives  
Enough to satisfy the need  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of everything that lives.

<sup>17</sup> The LORD is just in all his ways,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;holy in his works all.  
<sup>18</sup> GOD’s near to all that call on him,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in truth that on him call.

<sup>19</sup> He will accomplish the desire  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of those that do him fear:  
He also will deliver them,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and he their cry will hear.

<sup>20</sup> The LORD preserves all who him love,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that nought can them annoy:  
But he all those that wicked are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;will utterly destroy.

<sup>21</sup> My mouth the praises of the LORD  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to publish cease shall never:  
Let all flesh bless his holy name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for ever and for ever.

---

### Version 2

*L.M.*

<sup>1</sup> O Lord, thou art my God and King;  
Thee will I magnify and praise:  
I will thee bless, and gladly sing  
Unto thy holy name always.

<sup>2</sup> Each day I rise I will thee bless,  
And praise thy name time without end.  
<sup>3</sup> Much to be praised, and great God is;  
His greatness none can comprehend.

<sup>4</sup> Race shall thy works praise unto race,  
The mighty acts show done by thee.  
<sup>5</sup> I will speak of the glorious grace,  
And honour of thy majesty;

Thy wondrous works I will record.  
<sup>6</sup> By men the might shall be extolled  
Of all thy dreadful acts, O LORD:  
And I thy greatness will unfold.

<sup>7</sup> They utter shall abundantly  
The mem’ry of thy goodness great;  
And shall sing praises cheerfully,  
Whilst they thy righteousness relate.

<sup>8</sup> The LORD our God is gräcious,  
Compassionate is he also;  
In mercy he is plenteous,  
But unto wrath and anger slow.

<sup>9</sup> Good unto all men is the LORD:  
O’er all his works his mercy is.  
<sup>10</sup> Thy works all praise to thee afford:  
Thy saints, O LORD, thy name shall bless.

<sup>11</sup> The glory of thy kingdom show  
Shall they, and of thy power tell:  
<sup>12</sup> That so men’s sons his deeds may know,  
His kingdom’s grace that doth excel.

<sup>13</sup> Thy kingdom hath none end at all,  
It doth through ages all remain.  
<sup>14</sup> The LORD upholdeth all that fall,  
The cast-down raiseth up again.

<sup>15</sup> The eyes of all things, Lord, attend,  
And on thee wait that here do live,  
And thou, in season due, dost send  
Sufficient food them to relieve.

<sup>16</sup> Yea, thou thine hand dost open wide,  
And ev’rything dost satisfy  
That lives, and doth on earth abide,  
Of thy great liberality.

<sup>17</sup> The LORD is just in his ways all,  
And holy in his works each one.  
<sup>18</sup> He’s near to all that on him call,  
Who call in truth on him alone.

<sup>19</sup> God will the just desire fulfil  
Of such as do him fear and dread:  
Their cry regard, and hear he will,  
And save them in the time of need.

<sup>20</sup> The LORD preserves all, more and less,  
That bear to him a loving heart:  
But workers all of wickedness  
Destroy will he, and clean subvert.

<sup>21</sup> Therefore my mouth and lips I’ll frame  
To speak the praises of the LORD:  
To magnify his holy name  
For ever let all flesh accord.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

## Psalm 146

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Praise GOD. The LORD praise, O my soul.  
<sup>2</sup> I’ll praise GOD while I live;  
While I have being to my God  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in songs I’ll praises give.

<sup>3</sup> Trust not in princes, nor man’s son,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in whom there is no stay:  
<sup>4</sup> His breath departs, to ’s earth he turns;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that day his thoughts decay.

<sup>5</sup> O happy is that man and blest,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;whom Jacob’s God doth aid;  
Whose hope upon the LORD doth rest,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and on his God is stayed:

<sup>6</sup> Who made the earth and heavens high,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who made the swelling deep,  
And all that is within the same;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who truth doth ever keep:

<sup>7</sup> Who righteous judgment executes  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;for those oppressed that be,  
Who to the hungry giveth food;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;GOD sets the pris’ners free.

<sup>8</sup> The LORD doth give the blind their sight,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the bowèd down doth raise:  
The LORD doth dearly love all those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that walk in upright ways.

<sup>9</sup> The stranger’s shield, the widow’s stay,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the orphan’s help, is he:  
But yet by him the wicked’s way  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;turn’d upside down shall be.

<sup>10</sup> The LORD shall reign for evermore:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy God, O Zion, he  
Reigns to all generätions.  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Praise to the LORD give ye.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 147

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Praise ye the LORD; for it is good  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;praise to our God to sing:  
For it is pleasant, and to praise  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;it is a comely thing.

<sup>2</sup> GOD doth build up Jerusalem;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and he it is alone  
That the dispersed of Israel  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;doth gather into one.

<sup>3</sup> Those that are broken in their heart,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and grievèd in their minds,  
He healeth, and their painful wounds  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he tenderly up-binds.

<sup>4</sup> He counts the number of the stars;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;he names them ev’ry one.  
<sup>5</sup> Great is our Lord, and of great pow’r;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his wisdom search can none.

<sup>6</sup> The LORD lifts up the meek; and casts  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the wicked to the ground.  
<sup>7</sup> Sing to the LORD, and give him thanks;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on harp his praises sound;

<sup>8</sup> Who covereth the heav’n with clouds,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who for the earth below  
Prepareth rain, who maketh grass  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon the mountains grow.

<sup>9</sup> He gives the beast his food, he feeds  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the ravens young that cry.  
<sup>10</sup> His pleasure not in horses’ strength,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;nor in man’s legs, doth lie.

<sup>11</sup> But in all those that do him fear  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the LORD doth pleasure take;  
In those that to his mercy do  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;by hope themselves betake.

<sup>12</sup> The LORD praise, O Jerusalem;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Zion, thy God confess:  
<sup>13</sup> For thy gates’ bars he maketh strong;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;thy sons in thee doth bless.

<sup>14</sup> He in thy borders maketh peace;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with fine wheat filleth thee.  
<sup>15</sup> He sends forth his command on earth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his word runs speedily.

<sup>16</sup> Hoar-frost, like ashes, scatt’reth he;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;like wool he snow doth give:  
<sup>17</sup> Like morsels casteth forth his ice;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;who in its cold can live?

<sup>18</sup> He sendeth forth his mighty word,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and melteth them again;  
His wind he makes to blow, and then  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the waters flow amain.

<sup>19</sup> The doctrine of his holy word  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to Jacob he doth show;  
His statutes and his judgments he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;gives Israèl to know.

<sup>20</sup> To any nation never he  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;such favour did afford;  
For they his judgments have not known.  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O do ye praise the LORD.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 148

### Version 1

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Praise GOD. From heavens praise the  
LORD,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in heights praise to him be.  
<sup>2</sup> All ye his angels, praise ye him;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his hosts all, praise him ye.

<sup>3</sup> O praise ye him, both sun and moon;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;praise him, all stars of light.  
<sup>4</sup> Ye heav’ns of heav’ns him praise, and floods  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;above the heavens’ height.

<sup>5</sup> Let all the creatures praise the name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of our almighty LORD:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;For he commanded, and they were  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;created by his word.

<sup>6</sup> He also, for all times to come,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;hath them established sure;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;He hath appointed them a law,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;which ever shall endure.

<sup>7</sup> Praise ye JEHOVAH from the earth,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;dragons, and ev’ry deep:  
<sup>8</sup> Fire, hail, snow, vapour, stormy wind,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his word that fully keep.

<sup>9</sup> All hills and mountains, fruitful trees,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and all ye cedars high:  
<sup>10</sup> Beasts, and all cattle, creeping things,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and all ye birds that fly.

<sup>11</sup> Kings of the earth, all nätions,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;princes, earth’s judges all:  
<sup>12</sup> Both young men, yea, and maidens too,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;old men, and children small.

<sup>13</sup> Let them GOD’s name praise; for his name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;alone is excellent:  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;His glory reacheth far above  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the earth and firmament.

<sup>14</sup> His people’s horn, the praise of all  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his saints, exalteth he;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Ev’n Isr’el’s seed, a people near  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;to him. The LORD praise ye.

---

### Version 2

*6.6.6.6.8.8*

<sup>1</sup> The LORD of heav’n confess,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;On high his glory raise.  
<sup>2</sup> Him let all angels bless,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Him all his armies praise.  
<sup>3</sup> Him glorify sun, moon, and stars;  
<sup>4</sup> Ye higher spheres, and cloudy sky.

<sup>5</sup> From GOD your beings are,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Him therefore famous make;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;You all created were,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;When he the word but spake.  
<sup>6</sup> And from that place, where fixed you be  
By his decree, you cannot pass.

<sup>7</sup> Praise GOD from earth below,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Ye dragons, and ye deeps:  
<sup>8</sup> Fire, hail, clouds, wind, and snow,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Whom in command he keeps.  
<sup>9</sup> Praise ye his name, hills great and small,  
<sup>10</sup> Trees low and tall; beasts wild and tame;

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;All things that creep or fly.  
<sup>11</sup> Ye kings, ye vulgar throng,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;All princes mean or high;  
<sup>12</sup> Both men and virgins young,  
<sup>13</sup> Ev’n young and old, exalt his name;  
For much his fame should be extolled.

&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O let GOD’s name be praised  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Above both earth and sky;  
<sup>14</sup> For he his saints hath raised,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;And set their horn on high;  
Ev’n those that be of Isr’el’s race,  
Near to his grace.  The LORD praise ye.

## Psalm 149

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Praise ye the LORD: unto him sing  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a new song, and his praise  
In the assembly of his saints  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in sweet psalms do ye raise.

<sup>2</sup> Let Isr’el in his Maker joy,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and to him praises sing:  
Let all that Zion’s children are  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;be joyful in their King.

<sup>3</sup> O let them unto his great name  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;give praises in the dance;  
Let them with timbrel and with harp  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in songs his praise advance.

<sup>4</sup> For GOD doth pleasure take in those  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;that his own people be;  
And he with his salvätion  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the meek will beautify.

<sup>5</sup> And in his glory excellent  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;let all his saints rejoice:  
Let them to him upon their beds  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;aloud lift up their voice.

<sup>6</sup> Let in their mouth aloft be raised  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the high praise of the Lord,  
And let them have in their right hand  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;a sharp two-edgèd sword;

<sup>7</sup> To execute the vengeance due  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon the heathen all,  
And make deservèd punishment  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;upon the people fall.

<sup>8</sup> And ev’n with chains, as pris’ners, bind  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;their kings that them command;  
Yea, and with iron fetters strong,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;the nobles of their land.

<sup>9</sup> On them the judgment to perform  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;found written in his word:  
This honour is to all his saints.  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;O do ye praise the LORD.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)

<div style="page-break-after: always; break-after: page;"></div>

## Psalm 150

*C.M.*

<sup>1</sup> Praise ye the LORD. God’s praise within  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his sanctuary raise;  
And to him in the firmament  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;of his pow’r give ye praise.

<sup>2</sup> Because of all his mighty acts,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;with praise him magnify:  
O praise him, as he doth excel  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;in glorious majesty.

<sup>3</sup> Praise him with trumpet’s sound;  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;his praise with psaltery advance:  
<sup>4</sup> With timbrel, harp, stringed instruments,  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;and organs, in the dance.

<sup>5</sup> Praise him on cymbals loud; him praise  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;on cymbals sounding high.  
<sup>6</sup> Let each thing breathing praise the LORD.  
&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;Praise to the LORD give ye.

[Back to Top](#the-psalter)
